Quiz Attempt #118958

Total Questions: 24
Question 1
Which of the following statements relating to transactional analysis are true? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2024)A. There are 3 different types oftransactionsnamely complimentary, crossed andulterioroccur between the egos.B. In the crossed transaction there is no scope for conflict.C. In the ulterior transaction there ishighscope of conflict.D. In the complimentarytransectionthere is no scope of conflict.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.A, B and C only
  • B.B, C and D only
  • C.A, B, and D only
  • D.A, C and D only
Correct Answer: A, C and D only

The correct answer is option (D) A, C, and D only.

 

A: True. Transactional Analysis identifies three types of transactions: complementary, crossed, and ulterior. These describe the interactions between ego states (Parent, Adult, and Child).

 

B: False. In a crossed transaction, communication does not meet expectations, and this can lead to conflict since the response is from an unexpected ego state.

 

C: True. In an ulterior transaction, there is a hidden or double message, which can lead to high scope for conflict because the overt and covert communication are not aligned.

 

D: True. In a complementary transaction, the communication is straightforward and aligns between expected ego states, so there is no scope for conflict.

Question 2
Consider the following: (UGC NET HRM Jul 2016)a. Structural Analysisb. Interaction Analysisc. Life position Analysisd. Environmental Analysise. Dispositional Analysisf. Coping Behaviour AnalysisWhich among the above are the components ofDr.Eric Berne’s Transactional Analysis Theory?
  • A.c, d and e
  • B.a, c and e
  • C.a, b and c
  • D.b, c and e
Correct Answer: a, b and c

Eric Berne's Transactional Analysis (TA) theory encompasses various components, each shedding light on different facets of human interactions and psychological states. Among the options provided, the components associated with TA include:

 

a. Structural Analysis: This refers to the understanding of different ego states within an individual and their impact on behavior and communication.

 

b. Interaction Analysis: TA focuses on understanding social interactions between individuals and how they communicate through transactions.

 

c. Life position Analysis: This component delves into the different life positions individuals might assume based on their perceptions of themselves and others.

 

Therefore, the correct match for Dr. Eric Berne's Transactional Analysis Theory among the options provided is (C) a, b, and c. These components form integral parts of understanding human behavior, social interactions, and psychological dynamics according to Transactional Analysis.

Question 3
Match the authors (List – I) with the seminal works they have published (List – II): (UGC NET HRM Jul 2016)List – Ia. Eric Berneb. Thomas A. Harrisc. PeterSenged.AlwinTofflerList – IIi. The Fifth Disciplineii. The Games People Playiii. The Future Shockiv. I am OK; you are OK
  • A.a-ii, b-iv, c-i, d-iii
  • B.a-ii, b-i, c-iii, d-iv
  • C.a-ii, b-i, c-iv, d-iii
  • D.a-iv, b-ii, c-i, d-iii
Correct Answer: a-ii, b-iv, c-i, d-iii

a. Eric Berne - The Games People Play

"Games People Play: The Psychology of Human Relationships" is a bestselling 1964 book by psychiatrist Eric Berne. In the book, Berne introduces transactional analysis as a way of interpreting social interactions. He describes three roles or ego states, known as the Parent, the Adult, and the Child, and postulates that many negative behaviors can be traced to switching or confusion of these roles.

 

b. Thomas A. Harris - I am OK; you are OK

I'm OK – You're OK” is a 1969 self-help book by Thomas Anthony Harris. It is a practical guide to transactional analysis as a method for solving problems in life.

 

c. Peter Senge - The Fifth Discipline

"The Fifth Discipline: The Art and Practice of the Learning Organization" (in year 1990) is a book by Peter Senge (a senior lecturer at MIT) focusing on group problem solving using the systems thinking method in order to convert companies into learning organizations. The five disciplines represent approaches for developing three core learning capabilities: fostering aspiration, developing reflective conversation, and understanding complexity.

 

d. Alwin Toffler - The Future Shock

"Future Shock" is a book written by the futurist Alvin Toffler in 1970. In the book, Toffler defines the term "future shock" as a certain psychological state of individuals and entire societies.

Question 4
Which of the following is not one of the ego states of transactional analysis:(UGC NET Management Jun 2009)
  • A.Child
  • B.Young
  • C.Adult
  • D.Parents
Correct Answer: Young

In transactional analysis, the recognized ego states are the Child, Adult, and Parent. "Young" isn't considered an ego state within the framework of transactional analysis. So, the correct answer is (B) Young.

Question 5
Life position comprises certain deeply ingrained convictions about worth of the self and others. The conviction about himself or herself may either beI’amOK or I’m not OK. Similarly he or she may look at others and think you’re OK or you’re not OK. Match the life positions in Column – A with their nature in Column – B. (UGC NET HRM Aug 2016)Column – A (Life Positions)a. I’m OK, you’re OKb. I’m OK, you’re not OKc. I’m not OK, you’re OKd. I’m not OK, you’re not OKColumn – B (Nature)i. This is the depressive positionii. This is the paranoid positioniii. This is the Schizoid position or futility position.iv. This is the healthy position.
  • A.a-i, b-ii, c-iii, d-iv
  • B.a-iii, b-ii, c-i, d-iv
  • C.a-iv, b-i, c-ii, d-iii
  • D.a-iv, b-ii, c-i, d-iii
Correct Answer: a-iv, b-ii, c-i, d-iii

Life positions are basic beliefs about self and others, which are used to justify decisions and behavior. It was originally described by Eric Berne (1962/1976) in an article entitled "Classification of Positions." 

 

Based on transactions, there can be following life positions:

1) I am OK, you are OK: A person accepts others in spite of their shortcomings and feels OK about himself despite not being perfect. 

 

2) I am OK, you are not OK: Comes over as distrustful, arrogant superior. Thinks that others are inferiors. This is a distrustful life position. It often results from a person being brutalized by grown-ups when they were small. The people who base their lives on those recordings spend much of their energy getting rid of other people. It is also called the super-ego mode. Some people in authoritative positions can employ this mode to treat those under their authority as someone who is not important, who have no value or who do not count.

 

3) I am not OK, you are OK: Recognized by attitudes of depression, powerlessness and inferiority. Thinks that others are better. This is the life position held by many people, especially during the growing up years. It is a conclusion based mostly on early negative or Not Ok feelings about you rather than on a more comprehensive later review of data available in all 3-ego states. We are bombarded in our early childhood years by the numerous parent commands, the does and don'ts, and the always and never statements from those in authority over us. As a result it is easy to place oneself in I'M Not OK-You're OK mode often.

 

4) I am not OK, you are not OK: A position of thorough hopelessness and despair. This is a despairing life position. From it, life appears hopeless. People in this position use up much of their energy getting nowhere with other people in their own lives. Someone who is in this mode is often very depressed, withdrawn and may experience serious mental problems which can even lead to suicide. This individual has a very poor self-image, negative feelings, and is in a dead end position.

 

The theory of Transaction Analysis and the Games can be gainfully used in organizational Training programs to make employees aware of the ego states, the scripts and how they influence the inter-personal skills. Continuous training and efforts can shape the change in our behavior pattern. Positive attitude towards self and others (I am OK-YOU are OK) is the desirable position to be attained through reinforcing the Adult, the Nurturing Parent and the Natural child.

 

In short,

"I'm OK, You're OK" (I+U+) – Good Life (Healthy) position;

"I'm not- OK, You're OK" (I-U+) – Depressive position;

"I'm OK, You're not-OK" (I+U-) – Paranoid position; and 

"I'm not- OK, You're not-OK" (IU-) – Futile position.

Question 6
Dinesh, a young executive, joinedSoftechco. three months back. Coming with a brilliant academic record, he played key role to revamp the company’s finance and management procedures for which he was recognized by the management.But now his performance has come down with mistakes found in most of his actions. Several things transpired against him. His only son turned spastic and he was overlooked for promotion against a newcomer. This witnessed him becoming less popular among staff. Adding to that, a mild flirtation with a female employee was blown out of proportion.Dinesh hasbecameemotionally and professionally depressed with morale down and seemed loosing self-confidence badly.(UGC NET Management Dec 2019)As HR Manager which life positions in Transactional Analysis would you expect Dinesh to have?
  • A.I’m Ok, You are Ok
  • B.I’m Ok, You are not Ok
  • C.I’m not Ok, You are Ok
  • D.I’m not Ok, You are not Ok
Correct Answer: I’m Ok, You are Ok

The theory of Transaction Analysis and the Games can be gainfully used in organizational Training programs to make employees aware of the ego states, the scripts and how they influence the inter-personal skills. Continuous training and efforts can shape the change in our behavior pattern. Positive attitude towards self and others (I am OK-YOU are OK) is the desirable position to be attained through reinforcing the Adult, the Nurturing Parent and the Natural child. Therefore, as HR manager we would expect Dinesh to have I’m Ok, You are Ok life position from Transactional Analysis.

Question 7
In Transactional Analysis, if the response is by the same ego state as through which the message was received, the transaction is called: (UGC NET HRM Jan 2017)
  • A.Crossed Transaction
  • B.Complementary Transaction
  • C.Ulterior Transaction
  • D.Feed-forward Transaction
Correct Answer: Complementary Transaction

Within ego states of Transaction Analysis, there are three different types of transaction: complementary, crossed, and ulterior.

 

Complementary Transactions A complementary transaction occurs when the sender of the message gets the intended response from the receiver. For example, an employee makes a mistake and, wanting some sympathy, apologizes to the boss. Employee ­ `I just dropped the thing when I was almost done. Now I have to do it all over again. 'Supervisor ­ `It happens to all of us; don't worry about it.' 

 

Crossed transactions occur when the sender of the message does not get the expected response from the receiver. Returning to our first example: Employee ­ `I just dropped the thing when I was almost done. Now I have to do it all over again.' Supervisor ­ `you are so clumsy.'

 

Ulterior, or hidden transactions occur when the words seem to be coming from one ego state, but in reality the words or behaviours are coming from another. For example, after a training program, one of the participants came up to a consultant asking advice on an adult ego sate. When the consultant gave advice, the participant twice had quick responses as to why the advice would not work (child rather than adult behaviour). The consultant realized that what the participant actually wanted was sympathetic understanding for his situation, not advice. The consultant stopped making suggestions and listened actively, using reflective responses. The consultant changed from the adult to the sympathetic parent ego state in order to have a complimentary transaction.

Question 8
Match the following 'Expressions' and the 'Ego states' given in List-I and List-II respectively. (UGC NET HRM Dec 2015) (UGC NET HRM Dec 2014)List – I (Expressions)(a) Rationality(b) Fantasizing(c) DemonstratingList – II (Ego states)(i) Parent(ii) Adult(iii) Child
  • A.a-(ii), b-(iii), c-(i)
  • B.a-(iii), b-(i), c-(ii)
  • C.a-(i), b-(ii), c-(iii)
  • D.a-(iii), b-(ii), c-(i)
Correct Answer: a-(ii), b-(iii), c-(i)

(a) Rationality - Adult

(b) Fantasizing - Child

(c) Demonstrating - Parent

 

As a theory of personality, Transactional Analysis proposes how people are structured psychologically, by making use of a much simplified model - the PAC model. It incorporates the Parent, Adult and Child, - three personality instances that have parallels to the superego, ego, and libido (id) of Freudian thought, and are given the added names exteropsyche (Parent), neopsyche (Adult), and archaeopsyche (Child). Parent state is a state in which people behave, feel, and think in response to an unconscious mimicking of how their parents acted, or how they interpreted their parent's actions. Adult ego is a state of the ego which is most like a computer processing information and making predictions absent of major emotions that could affect its operation. Child is a state in which people behave, feel and think similarly to how they did in childhood.

Question 9
Who gave the concept of ‘Life-Positions’ in the context of Transactional Analysis? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2014)
  • A.Eric Berne
  • B.Thomas A. Harris
  • C.JosephLufthand HarryInghams
  • D.Jay Galbraith
Correct Answer: Thomas A. Harris

In Transactional Analysis theory, "Life Position" refers to the general feeling about life (specifically, the unconscious feeling, as opposed to a conscious philosophical position) that colours every dyadic (i.e. person-to-person) transaction. Initially four such Life Positions were proposed: 1). "I'm Not OK, You're OK" (I-U+) 2) "I'm Not OK, You're Not OK" (I-U-) 3) "I'm OK, You're Not OK" (I+U-) 4). "I'm OK, You're OK" (I+U+). Life Position was written by Thomas Anthony Harris. Transactional Analysis concept was given by  Eric Berne.

Question 10
Match the following: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2012)Books and Conceptsa. Games People Playb. I am OK you are OKc. Johari Windowd. Force Field AnalysisAuthorsi. Eric Berneii. Kurt Lewiniii. Thomas A. Harrisiv. JosephLufth& HarryInghams
  • A.a-ii, b-i, c-iv, d-iii
  • B.a-i, b-iii, c-iv, d-ii
  • C.a-iv, b-ii, c-iii, d-i
  • D.a-iii, b-i, c-ii, d-iv
Correct Answer: a-i, b-iii, c-iv, d-ii

a. Games People Play - Eric Bernie

In the Introduction of the book Games People Play, Dr. Eric Berne laid out stroke theory and made clear that he considered strokes to be the fundamental motive for human behaviour and the reason why people play games.

 

b. I am OK you are OK - Thomas A. Harris

I'm OK – You're OK is a 1967 self-help book by Thomas Anthony Harris. It is a practical guide to transactional analysis as a method for solving problems in life.

 

c. Johari Window - Joseph Lufth & Harry Inghams

Joe Luft and Harry Ingham developed the technique of Johari Window (Johari representing the combination of their first names).  Johari Window is a tool that is used to improve the understanding between individuals. Using this tool one can build trust with others by disclosing information about him and with the help of feedback from others; one can learn about himself and come to terms with personal issues.

 

d. Force Field Analysis - Kurt Lewin

Kurt Lewin's force field analysis change model was designed to weigh the driving and restraining forces that affect change in organizations. The 'force field' can be described as two opposite forces working for and against change.

Question 11
In which of the following transactions, stimulus and response are parallel? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2010)
  • A.Cross Transactions
  • B.Complementary Transactions
  • C.Ulterior Transactions
  • D.All the above
Correct Answer: Complementary Transactions

In complementary transactions within Transactional Analysis, the stimulus and response align or are parallel, resulting in an intended or expected exchange between individuals involved in the communication. This alignment indicates that the response from the receiver corresponds directly to the message's intent from the sender, fostering effective communication and understanding.

Question 12
Transactional managerial styles refer to four life positions. These life positions can be used to understand one’s style of working with others. Match Four Life Positions (List - A) with Parent (Regulating/Nurturing) Ego States (List - B). (UGC NET HRM Jun 2015)List - A (Life Positions)a. I am not ok, you are not okb. I am ok, you are not okc. I am ok, you are okd. I am not ok, you are okList – B (Parent Ego State)i. Prescriptive/Patronisingii. Normative/Supportiveiii. Indifferent/Ingratiatingiv.) Traditional/Overindulgent
  • A.a-iv, b-i, c-ii, d-iii

a. I am not ok, you are not ok → iv. Traditional/Overindulgent

Question 14
Read the statements and choose the correct answer: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2015)Statement:(a) Sigmund Freud proposed the concept of thestructure ofpsyche in terms of Id, Ego, and Superego.(b) The ‘Id’ does not careabout reality, about the needs of anyone else, only its own satisfaction.
  • A.Both the statements are True
  • B.Both the statements are False
  • C.Statement (a) is True and (b) is False
  • D.Statement (b) is True and (a) is False
Correct Answer: Both the statements are True

Sigmund Freud indeed introduced the concept of the structure of the psyche comprising the Id, Ego, and Superego. The Id is primarily focused on immediate gratification and doesn't consider reality or the needs of others, aligning with the second statement as well. Therefore, both statements are true.

Question 15
Given below are 2 statements.[UGC NET Management June 2021]Statement I:The Transactional Analysis Model is an effective tool to understand why people behave in certain ways.Statement II:The Transactional Analysis Model cannot be used to improve communication.In light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are true
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are false
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true
Correct Answer: Statement I is true but Statement II is false

Statement I is correct, but Statement II is incorrect.

 

Transactional Analysis (TA) is a psychoanalytic theory and method of therapy, developed by Eric Berne during the 1950s. Transactions refer to the communication exchanges between people. Transactional analysis is the method used to analyses this process of transactions in communication with others. It requires us to be aware of how we feel, think and behave during interactions with others. Hence statement 1 is correct.

 

TA recognized that the human personality is made up of three "ego states"; each of which is an entire system of thought, feeling, and behavior from which we interact with each other. The Parent, Adult and Child ego states and the interaction between them form the foundation of transactional analysis theory. This understanding can be used to improve communication. Hence Statement 2 is incorrect.

Question 16
Match List I and List II: (UGC NET Management Jun 2020)List Ia. I am OK, you are Okb. I am OK, you are not Okc. I am Ok, you are okd. I am not ok, you are not OkList IIi. Avoidantii. Bossingiii. Competentiv. DiffidentChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii
  • B.a-iii, b-ii, c-iv, d-i
  • C.a-ii, b-iv, c-iv, d-i
  • D.a-ii, b-iv, c-iii, d-i
Correct Answer: a-iii, b-ii, c-iv, d-i

Transactional analysis identifies 4 basic life positions, all of which are based on decisions made as a result of childhood experiences, and all of which determine how people feel about themselves and how they relate to others:

 

1. I am Ok, you are OK (Competent)

This is an ideal life position because this position is rationally chosen one. In this position individual behaves rationally and accept significance of others. People feel happy and life is worth living. Individual with this life position expresses confidence in his subordinates, work with high level of delegation of authority, and believes in give and take. Manages enjoys good communication network, work with confidence and there is work sharing and positive attitude towards work. People remain happy and have high level of job satisfaction. People work with adult ego state. There is no conflict situation and there is total understanding among subordinates and peer group. An Ideal life positions.

 

2. I am OK, you are not OK (Bossing)

This is distrustful psychological life position taken by individual who feel that others are wrong. They blame others for their failure. People who have been neglected by parents in their childhood take this position. They generally operate from rebellion child ego state that feel victimized and blame others for their miseries. Mangers lack trust, confidence in the intellectual level, skills and talent in their subordinates and do not believe in delegation of authority. They perceive delegation as threat to their personal existence. Managers are critical, oppressive and point out flaws in the working of subordinates. They operate from critical parent ego state and rarely give positive remarks. They feel their workers lazy, irresponsible and find them as stated in theory X of Mc Gregor. Expresses bossing attitude.

 

3. I am not OK, you are OK (Diffident)

This life position is common to persons who feel powerless in comparison to others. Persons in this life position always grumble and feel at the mercy of others. They have tendency to withdraw and at times experience depression that may lead to suicide in extreme cases. People with this life position operate from child ego state. Managers tend to give and receive bad feelings. They are unpredictable and display erratic behaviours. It is not a

good life position. People are diffident in this life position.

 

4. I am not OK; you are not OK (Avoidant)

This is the worst life position in which individual feel defeated and sees whole world as miserable. It is a desperate life position where people lose interest in living. In extreme cases people commit suicide or homicide. This position is caused due to children having brought up by servants and very scant or no attention having been paid by the parents. At managerial level, no decision is taken in time and managers make mistakes. They at times provoke others in the negative direction and display a lack of personal potency. Manager with this position look to others for final decision and often delegate in-appropriately.

Question 17
Transactional Analysis does NOT help in:[UGC NET Management June 2019]
  • A.Problem solving
  • B.Higher social status
  • C.Improved communication within the organisation
  • D.Better leadership
Correct Answer: Higher social status

When people transact and exchange ideas and information, they are either comfortable or uncomfortable communicating with each other. Transactional analysis is a technique which helps to understand the behaviour of other person so that communication becomes effective. Understanding human behaviour helps to motivate, guide and direct other persons. Hence, transaction analysis helps in problem solving, better leadership, improving communication within the organisation. But it does not help in improving social status or achieving higher social status.

Question 20
Who among the following has given the concept of structure of psyche in terms of id, ego and superego? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)
  • A.S.Schacter
  • B.Carl Yung
  • C.Sigmund Freud
  • D.Eric Berne
Correct Answer: Sigmund Freud

Sigmund Freud has given the concept of structure of psyche in terms of id, ego and superego. The theory given by him is known as ‘Freudian Psychoanalytic Theory of Personality’ which is explained below.

 

Psychoanalytic theories explain human behaviour in terms of the interaction of various components of personality. According to Sigmund Freud’s famous psychoanalytic theory, personality is composed of three elements, known as the id, the ego, and the superego, which work together to create complex human behaviors. Each of these three elements of personality emerges at different points in life.

 

1. The Id: The Id is the only component of personality that is present from birth. This aspect of personality is entirely unconscious and includes instinctive and primitive behaviors. According to Freud, the Id is the source of all psychic energy, making it the primary component of personality. The Id is driven by the pleasure principle, which strives for immediate gratification of all desires, wants, and needs. If these needs are not satisfied immediately, the result is a state of anxiety or tension. For example, an increase in hunger or thirst should produce an immediate attempt to eat or drink.

 

2. The Ego: The ego is the component of personality that is responsible for dealing with reality. According to Freud, the ego develops from the id and ensures that the impulses of the id can be expressed in a manner acceptable in the real world. The ego functions in both the conscious, preconscious, and unconscious mind. The ego operates based on the reality principle, which strives to satisfy the id's desires in realistic and socially appropriate ways. The reality principle weighs the costs and benefits of an action before deciding to act upon or abandon impulses. In many cases, the id's impulses can be satisfied through a process of delayed gratification—the ego will eventually allow the behaviour, but only in the appropriate time and place.

 

3. The Superego: The last component of personality to develop is the superego. The superego is the aspect of personality that holds all of our internalized moral standards and ideals that we acquire from both parents and society—our sense of right and wrong. The superego provides guidelines for making judgments. According to Freud, the superego begins to emerge at around age five.

Question 21
Which one of the following represents the moral values that develop on the basis of influence of role models and other significantpersons? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2022)
  • A.Id
  • B.Ego
  • C.Esteem
  • D.Superego
Correct Answer: Superego

The superego, according to Freud's psychoanalytic theory, represents the moral values that individuals acquire from significant figures like role models, parents, and society. It acts as a kind of moral compass, influencing ethical decision-making and behavior.

Question 22
Transactional Analysis is associated with _______. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)
  • A.Intrapersonal Conflict
  • B.Interpersonal Conflict
  • C.Union Management Conflict
  • D.Inter Group Conflict
Correct Answer: Interpersonal Conflict

Transactional Analysis is associated with Interpersonal Conflict.

 

Transactional analysis is a psychoanalytic theory and method of therapy wherein social transactions are analysed to determine the ego state of an individual as a basis for understanding behaviour. In transactional analysis, the individual is taught to alter the ego state as a way to solve emotional problems. TA provides a comprehensive model to understand behavioural patterns, communication, interpersonal relationship, motivation, time management, attitudes, conflict management, and life span development. These skills have been found to be essential for an employee to work effectively in an organisation. Hence, TA acts a great tool to managers in understanding their employees, find out where they are lacking and provide training accordingly.

Question 23
The behaviour of a person under the Adult ego state under Transactional Analysis is: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)
  • A.Protective and critical
  • B.Impulsive and emotional
  • C.Rational and logical
  • D.Evaluative and judgmental
Correct Answer: Rational and logical

The Adult ego state in Transactional Analysis is characterized by rationality, logic, and objective thinking. It operates like a human computer, processing information based on facts and logic, aiming to make decisions without being influenced by emotions from the Child or Parent ego states.

Question 24
Technique of ‘Transaction Analysis’ was developed by: (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2013)
  • A.Elton Mayo
  • B.Peter Drucker
  • C.Eric Berne
  • D.Adam Smith
Correct Answer: Eric Berne

Eric Berne was the developer of Transactional Analysis (TA). His work on TA emphasized the analysis of social transactions to understand and improve human interactions. The concept delves into different ego states and their impacts on interpersonal relationships, shedding light on how individuals communicate and behave in various situations. TA remains a valuable tool in psychology and communication studies, offering insights into human behavior, communication patterns, and relationships.

Quiz Attempt #118959

Total Questions: 11
Question 1
Which of the following is not a factor of emotional intelligence? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2012)
  • A.Ability
  • B.Reason
  • C.Emotion
  • D.Thinking without feeling
Correct Answer: Thinking without feeling

Emotional intelligence involves understanding and managing emotions, using emotional information in decision-making, and navigating social complexities effectively. Thinking without feeling, as indicated in option (D), doesn't align with the principles of emotional intelligence, which inherently involve recognizing and integrating emotions into thinking and decision-making processes.

Question 2
Which of the following approaches of leadership focuses on ‘personal competence’ and ‘social competence’? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)
  • A.Trait theory of leadership
  • B.Charismatic leadership approach
  • C.Situational approach of leadership
  • D.Emotional intelligence approach
Correct Answer: Emotional intelligence approach

Emotional intelligence is understanding one's own feelings, empathy for the feelings of others and the regulation of emotion in a way that enhances living. Daniel Goleman popularized the term in the title of his bestselling book, "Emotional Intelligence: Why it can Matter More than IQ".

 

Levinson (1980) grouped EI into three categories. These are—desire to manage, ability to communicate with empathy, integrity and honesty.

 

Goleman's model describes EQ in terms of four quadrants. Two of the domains are related to personal competence and two are related to social competence. The theory of emotional intelligence is popular because it implies that EQ can be developed and improved. This is not universally accepted but research has supported the idea that emotional intelligence competencies can be significantly improved over time.

 

Personal competence is made up of "self-awareness" and "self-management". Self-awareness is the ability to recognize your own emotions and their effects on self and other people. Self-management builds on your self-awareness, using your own self-control to ensure your emotions don't control you.

 

Social competence is made up of "social awareness" and "relationship management". Social awareness competencies include empathy, organizational awareness, and service orientation. Relationship management competencies include influence, leadership, developing others, communication, change catalyst, conflict management, building bonds, and teamwork and collaboration.

Question 3
Which of the following statements best differentiates emotions from moods?
  • A.Emotions are typically brief and triggered by specific events, while moods last longer and lack a clear cause.
  • B.Emotions are general in nature and lack distinct expressions, while moods are specific and accompanied by facial expressions.
  • C.Emotions are cognitive in nature and often last for hours or days, while moods are action-oriented and brief in duration.
  • D.Emotions are characterized by distinct facial expressions and numerous specific types, while moods are action-oriented and caused by specific events.
Correct Answer: Emotions are typically brief and triggered by specific events, while moods last longer and lack a clear cause.

Emotions are intense and brief, triggered by specific events, while moods are less intense, longer-lasting, and often arise without a clear stimulus.

Question 4

Emotional labor involves regulating and managing one's emotions to match the expectations and requirements of a job, often involving the intentional manipulation of emotions to create desired emotional responses in others.

Question 5

Surface acting occurs when an employee displays emotions required by the organization but doesn't genuinely feel those emotions internally. They are adhering to display rules without aligning their inner emotions.

Emotional dissonance refers to the discomfort caused by the mismatch between an individual's displayed emotions (required by the job) and their true internal emotions. This discrepancy often results in psychological discomfort.

Question 7

  • B.Insecurity
  • C.Distrust
  • D.Fear
Correct Answer: Fear

Option D is the correct answer.

 

Robert Plutchik devised the psycho-evolutionary theory of emotion, and this helps categorize emotions into primary emotions and the responses to them. He argued that the primary emotions are an evolutionary development and that the response to each such emotion is the one that is likely to deliver the highest level of survival possibility.

 

The 8 basic emotions that Plutchik devised were: Anger, Disgust, Fear, Sadness, Anticipation, Joy, Surprise, Trust.

Quiz Attempt #118960

Total Questions: 60
Question 1
Maslow’s Hierarchy of Heeds depicts human needs in the form of hierarchy ascending from the lowest to highest need. The correct order is (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2023)
  • A.Esteem needs, Acceptance needs, Safety needs, Physiological needs, Need for Self- Actualization
  • B.Physiological needs, Safety needs, Acceptance needs, Need for Self - Actualization
  • C.Safety needs, Esteem, needs, Need for Self- Actualization, Physiological needs, Acceptance needs
  • D.Physiological needs, Acceptance needs, Safety, Need for self- Actualization, Esteem needs
Correct Answer: Physiological needs, Safety needs, Acceptance needs, Need for Self - Actualization

The correct order in Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs is (B) Physiological needs, Safety needs, Acceptance needs, Need for Self-Actualization.

 

Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs suggests that individuals must satisfy lower-level needs before progressing to higher-level ones. It starts with physiological needs (like food, water, and shelter), followed by safety needs (such as security and stability), then belongingness and love needs (acceptance and social relationships), and finally self-esteem needs (like achievement and recognition). At the top of the hierarchy is self-actualization, representing the desire for personal growth and fulfillment.

Question 2
Arrange the following content theories of work motivation in the increasing order of their development - (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2024)A. Herzberg-motivation and hygiene factorsB. Alderfer ERG NeedsC. Maslow-Hierarchy of NeedsD. Scientific ManagementE. Human RelationsChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.D, C, E, A, B
  • B.D, E, C, A, B
  • C.B, C, A, D, E
  • D.D, E, A, C, B
Correct Answer: D, E, C, A, B

arrange the content theories of work motivation in the increasing order of their development, we need to consider the chronological development of these theories. Here’s the breakdown:

 

D. Scientific Management: Developed by Frederick Taylor in the early 20th century (1911), this theory focuses on optimizing work processes and efficiency, laying the groundwork for later motivational theories.

 

E. Human Relations: Emerging in the 1930s, this approach, influenced by the Hawthorne studies, emphasized the importance of social relations and worker satisfaction, shifting the focus from purely mechanical productivity to human aspects.

 

C. Maslow - Hierarchy of Needs: Proposed by Abraham Maslow in 1943, this theory introduced the idea that human motivation is based on a hierarchy of needs, from physiological to self-actualization.

 

A. Herzberg - Motivation and Hygiene Factors: Developed in the 1950s, Frederick Herzberg's theory distinguished between motivators and hygiene factors, emphasizing that job satisfaction and dissatisfaction arise from different sources.

 

B. Alderfer ERG Needs: Introduced by Clayton Alderfer in the 1960s, this theory refined Maslow’s model into three core needs: Existence, Relatedness, and Growth, allowing for more flexibility than Maslow's hierarchy.

 

Given this chronological order, the correct arrangement in increasing order of development is: option (B) D, E, C, A, B.

Question 3
Which of the following are NOT motivational factors according to Herzberg? (UGC NET Management Jun 2023)a. Interpersonal relationsb. Work itselfc. Advancementd. Achievemente. SalaryChoose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.a and e only
  • B.a and b only
  • C.b and d only
  • D.c and e only
Correct Answer: a and e only

The correct answer is (A) a and e only. Here’s the explanation based on Herzberg's two-factor theory:

 

Herzberg's theory divides job factors into hygiene factors and motivational factors:

 

Hygiene factors are those factors that are necessary to prevent dissatisfaction but do not necessarily lead to long-term satisfaction. If these factors are inadequate or absent, they cause dissatisfaction, but if they are present, they do not lead to significant motivation or satisfaction.

 

Interpersonal relations (a) and Salary (e) are considered hygiene factors. They are essential for preventing dissatisfaction but do not directly contribute to increased motivation or job satisfaction.

 

Motivational factors are those that lead to positive satisfaction and motivate employees to perform better. These factors are intrinsic to the job itself and lead to superior performance and long-term satisfaction.

 

Work itself (b), Advancement (c), and Achievement (d) are motivational factors according to Herzberg. These factors are linked to the intrinsic rewards of doing meaningful and fulfilling work.

Question 4
Match List-I with List-II. (UGC NET Management Dec 2023)List-I (Motivational Theory)(A) Need Hierarchy Theory(B) Two-Factor Theory(C) Expectancy Theory(D) Theory of X vs YList-II (Propounders)(I) Fedrick Herzberg(II) Abraham H. Maslow(III) Douglas MC Gregar(IV) V.H. VroomChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.(A)-(I), (B)-(III), (C)-(II), (D)-(IV)
  • B.(A)-(II), (B)-(I), (C)-(IV), (D)-(III)
  • C.(A)-(III), (B)-(I), (C)-(II), (D)-(IV)
  • D.(A)-(IV), (B)-(II), (C)-(I), (D)-(III)
Correct Answer: (A)-(II), (B)-(I), (C)-(IV), (D)-(III)

To correctly match List-I with List-II, let's identify the propounders of each motivational theory:

 

(A) Need Hierarchy Theory: This theory, also known as Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs, was developed by Abraham H. Maslow. It categorizes human needs into a hierarchy, starting from basic physiological needs to self-actualization.

 

(B) Two-Factor Theory: This theory, also known as Herzberg's Motivation-Hygiene Theory, was developed by Frederick Herzberg. It distinguishes between hygiene factors that can cause dissatisfaction and motivational factors that can drive satisfaction.

 

(C) Expectancy Theory: This theory was developed by Victor H. Vroom. It states that individuals' motivation is influenced by their expectations regarding the outcomes of their actions.

 

(D) Theory of X vs Y: This theory was developed by Douglas McGregor. It contrasts two views of workers: Theory X, which assumes workers are inherently lazy and need to be controlled, and Theory Y, which assumes workers are self-motivated and seek responsibility.

Question 5
Which theory says that people are motivated if they believe in the worth of the goal and outcome of the effort? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2023)
  • A.Equity Theory
  • B.Expectancy Theory
  • C.Reinforcement Theory
  • D.ERG Theory
Correct Answer: Expectancy Theory

Expectancy Theory, proposed by Victor Vroom, suggests that individuals are motivated to exert effort when they believe that their efforts will lead to a desired outcome (expectancy), that the desired outcome is valuable or worth achieving (valence), and that they have the necessary skills and resources to achieve the desired outcome (instrumentality). In other words, people are motivated when they believe their efforts will lead to a valuable and attainable goal.

Chester Barnard introduced the idea that managers have to examine the environment and then adjust the organization to maintain a state of equilibrium. He emphasized the importance of adapting organizations to their environments and maintaining a balance between internal operations and external demands. Chester Barnard's work contributed significantly to the understanding of organizational theory and management.

Question 7
Match List I with List II. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2023)List IA. Herzberg TheoryB. Equity TheoryC. Reinforcement TheoryD. McClelland’s TheoryList III. Dissatisfies and SatisfiersII. Motivation by praiseIII. Fairness of reward structureIV. Need for power, affiliation and achievement.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:Codes
  • A.A – I, B - II, C- III, D - IV
  • B.A - I, B - III, C - II, D - IV
  • C.A - I, B - II, C - IV D - III
  • D.A - IV, B - II, C- III, D - I
Correct Answer: A - I, B - III, C - II, D - IV

Option B is the correct answer.

 

A. Herzberg Theory – I. Dissatisfies and Satisfiers: This theory distinguishes between hygiene factors (dissatisfiers) and motivators (satisfiers) in the workplace.

 

B. Equity Theory – III. Fairness of reward structure: Equity theory focuses on perceptions of fairness and suggests that employees are motivated when they perceive their rewards to be equitable in relation to their inputs compared to others.

Question 8
As per Herzberg’s two factor theory of motivation which of the following are the motivators? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2023)(A) Interpersonal relations(B) Achievement(C) Advancement(D) Supervision(E) ResponsibilityChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.(A), (B) and (D) Only
  • B.(B), (C) and (E) Only
  • C.(B), (C) and (D) Only
  • D.(A), (D) and (E) Only
Correct Answer: (B), (C) and (E) Only

Option B is the correct answer.

The Two-Factor Theory, also known as the Motivator-Hygiene Theory, was introduced by Frederick Herzberg, a behavioural scientist, in 1959. The theory proposes that job satisfaction and job dissatisfaction are determined by different factors. According to Herzberg, the presence of certain job factors leads to satisfaction while the absence of others leads to dissatisfaction.

 

The job factors that lead to satisfaction are classified as Motivational Factors, while the factors that prevent dissatisfaction are known as Hygiene Factors.

 

1. Hygiene Factors: Hygiene Factors are the basic necessities that an employee needs in order to maintain motivation in the workplace. These factors, such as pay, benefits, working conditions, job security, and interpersonal relations, are not enough to lead to long-term job satisfaction. Instead, they are essential to prevent dissatisfaction.

 

2. Motivational Factors: Motivational Factors are those that lead to job satisfaction. These factors, such as recognition, opportunities for growth and advancement, meaningful work, and a sense of achievement, are inherent to the job and motivate employees to perform at a high level. Employees find these factors intrinsically rewarding.

(B) Equity Theory - Propagated by J. Stacy Adams, Equity Theory focuses on the concept of fairness and how perceived inequities can influence motivation. Associated with: (I) J. Stacy Adams

 

(C) ERG Theory - Developed by Clayton P. Alderfer, ERG Theory condenses Maslow's five needs into three core needs: Existence, Relatedness, and Growth. Associated with: (IV) Clayton P. Alderfer

Question 14
Who has modified Maslow’s Hierarchical levels of needs and developed ERG model? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2014)
  • A.Frederick Herzberg
  • B.David C. McClelland
  • C.Douglas McGregor
  • D.ClaytonAlderfer
Correct Answer: ClaytonAlderfer

Clayton Alderfer reworked Maslow’s need hierarchy to align it with the empirical research.  Alderfer argues that there are three groups of core needs:

1. Existence

  • Provides our basic material existence requirements.
  • They include Maslow’s physiological and safety needs. 

2. Relatedness

  • The desire we have for maintaining important interpersonal relationships.
  • These social and status desires require interaction with others.
  • They align with Maslow’s social need and the external component.

3. Growth needs

  • An intrinsic desire for personal development
  • These include the intrinsic component from Maslow’s esteem category and the characteristics included under self-actualization.
Question 15
Which of the following is not a content theory of motivation? (UGC NET Commerce Aug 2016)(a) Maslow’s Need Hierarchy Theory(b) Herzberg’s Two Factor Theory(c) Vroom’s Vector Valence Theory(d)Alderfer’sERG Theory
  • A.(d) only
  • B.(c) and (d)
  • C.(c) only
  • D.(b) and (d)
Correct Answer: (c) only

Vroom’s Vector Valence Theory is among the ‘Process Theories’ of Motivation. 

 

We can distinguish between content and process motivation theories. Content theories (also called Needs Theories) focus on WHAT, while Process theories focus on HOW human behaviour is motivated. Content theories are the earliest theories of motivation. Within the work environment they have had the greatest impact on management practice and policy, whilst within academic circles they are the least accepted. Content theories are also called needs theories: they try to identify what our needs are and relate motivation to the fulfilling of these needs. The content theories cannot entirely explain what motivate or demotivate us. Process theories are concerned with “how” motivation occurs, and what kind of process can influence our motivation.

 

Content theories are Maslow’s Needs hierarchy, Alderfer’s ERG theory, McClelland’s Achievement Motivation theory and Herzberg’s Two-factor theory

 

Process theories are Skinner’s Reinforcement theory, Victor Vroom's Expectancy theory, Adam’s Equity theory and Locke’s Goal-setting theory

Question 17
The popular statement, - “if all you have is a hammer, everything looks like a nail”, is given by: (UGC NET Commerce Jul 2018)
  • A.A.H. Maslow (Hierarchy of Needs)
  • B.Henry Fayol (Industrial and General Administration)
  • C.F.W. Taylor (Scientific Management)
  • D.Fredrick Herzberg (Hygiene Theory)
Correct Answer: A.H. Maslow (Hierarchy of Needs)

The statement refers to the concept known as the law of the instrument, otherwise known as the law of the hammer, Maslow's hammer (or gavel), or the golden hammer, is a cognitive bias that involves an over-reliance on a familiar tool. As Abraham Maslow said in 1966, "I suppose it is tempting, if the only tool you have is a hammer, to treat everything as if it were a nail."

 

The concept is attributed both to Maslow and to Abraham Kaplan, although the hammer and nail line may not be original to either of them. It has in fact been attributed to sources ranging from Buddha to the Bible to Mark Twain, though it cannot be found in any of their writings. It has also been attributed to the stock market speculator and author Bernard M. Baruch.

Question 18
Consider the following. (UGC NET Commerce Jan 2017)Assertion “A”:Herzberg believes that today’s motivators are tomorrow’s hygiene factors.Reason “R”:Some job conditions operate primarily to dissatisfy employees when they are absent, but their presence does not motivate them in strong way.
  • A.A and R both are correct and R is the right explanation of A.
  • B.A and R both are correct, but R is not the right explanation of A.
  • C.A is not correct while R is a correct.
  • D.Both A and R are incorrect.
Correct Answer: A and R both are correct, but R is not the right explanation of A.

The assertion ("A") states: "Herzberg believes that today’s motivators are tomorrow’s hygiene factors." This assertion is true based on Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory. Herzberg posited that what motivates employees initially (motivational factors) might eventually become expected or routine aspects of the job, thus transitioning into hygiene factors. For instance, factors like recognition, a sense of achievement, growth opportunities, and responsibility can initially motivate employees. However, over time, once these become standard or expected elements of the job, they cease to be motivating and transform into hygiene factors.

 

The reason ("R") provided for the assertion is: "Some job conditions operate primarily to dissatisfy employees when they are absent, but their presence does not motivate them in a strong way." This reason aligns with Herzberg's concept of hygiene factors. Hygiene factors, such as working conditions or job security, when inadequate, lead to dissatisfaction, but when present, they don't strongly motivate employees. These factors are more related to the environment and conditions of work rather than directly driving motivation.

 

So, the assertion and reason are both correct. However, the reason is not a direct explanation of the assertion, so the correct option is (B) A and R both are correct, but R is not the right explanation of A.

Question 20
Who did give the concept of hierarchy of needs? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2012)
  • A.Fredrick Herzberg
  • B.Victor Vroom
  • C.DouglasMcgregor
  • D.A.H. Maslow
Correct Answer: A.H. Maslow

The concept of hierarchy of needs was given by A. H. Maslow. The theory is explained below:

Abraham Maslow’s hierarchy of needs is the most well-known theory of motivation. He hypothesized that within every human being there exists a hierarchy of five needs: 

(a) Physiological: Includes hunger, thirst, shelter, sex, and other bodily needs

(b) Safety: Includes security and protection from physical and emotional harm

(c) Social: Includes affection, belongingness, acceptance, and friendship

(d) Esteem: Includes internal esteem factors such as self-respect, autonomy, and achievement; and external esteem factors such as status, recognition, and attention

(e) Self-actualization: The drive to become what one is capable of becoming; includes growth, achieving one’s potential, and self-fulfillment

    

As a need becomes substantially satisfied, the next need becomes dominant. No need is ever fully gratified; a substantially satisfied need no longer motivates. 

 

Maslow separated the five needs into higher and lower orders. 

(i) Physiological and safety needs are described as lower-order.

(ii) Social, esteem, and self-actualization are as higher-order needs

(iii) Higher-order needs are satisfied internally.

(iv) Lower-order needs are predominantly satisfied externally.

Maslow’s need theory has received wide recognition, particularly among practicing managers. Research does not generally validate the theory.

Match the following:(UGC NET Commerce Dec 2012)List-Ia. An ordinary person does not want to work on his ownb. An individual is willing to work on his ownc. Motivational Factorsd. Esteem NeedsList-II1. Hierarchy Theory2. Hygiene Theory3. X-Theory4. Y-Theory

Question 22
While establishing relation between Maslow’s and Herzberg’s theories, which Needs of Hierarchy Theory will fall under the Hygiene Factors? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2012)
  • A.Self actualization, esteem and social needs
  • B.Esteem, social and safety needs
  • C.Social, safety and physiological needs
  • D.Only social needs
Correct Answer: Social, safety and physiological needs

When establishing a relation between Maslow’s Hierarchy of Needs and Herzberg’s Two-Factor Theory, the needs from Maslow's hierarchy that would fall under the Hygiene Factors as per Herzberg's theory are:

 

Social needs: These encompass the desire for affection, belongingness, acceptance, and friendship. In Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory, factors such as interpersonal relations could be linked to these social needs, falling under hygiene factors that, when absent or inadequate, can lead to dissatisfaction.

 

Safety needs: These include the need for security and protection from physical and emotional harm. In Herzberg's model, job security is considered a hygiene factor, essential for avoiding dissatisfaction in the workplace.

 

Physiological needs: These cover the basic bodily requirements like hunger, thirst, shelter, etc. Herzberg suggests that factors such as physical working conditions and fringe benefits fall under hygiene factors, satisfying these basic physiological needs, although they do not lead to long-term positive satisfaction.

 

Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory differentiates between hygiene factors (essential for preventing dissatisfaction) and motivational factors (related to positive satisfaction). The hygiene factors primarily correspond to the lower-order needs in Maslow's hierarchy, ensuring that these basic needs are met to avoid dissatisfaction, although they do not necessarily lead to long-term positive satisfaction or motivation.

Question 24
According to Vroom’s Expectancy Theory of Motivation, (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)
  • A.Force = valence divided by expectancy
  • B.Force = valence × expectancy × Instrumentality
  • C.Force = strength of an individual preference for an outcome
  • D.Valence = probability that a particular action shall lead to a desired outcome
Correct Answer: Force = valence × expectancy × Instrumentality

The correct answer is (B) Force = valence × expectancy × Instrumentality. This formula represents Vroom's expectancy theory of motivation, where the motivational force is calculated as the product of valence, expectancy, and instrumentality.

 

In Vroom's theory:

Expectancy is the belief that increased effort will lead to increased performance.

Instrumentality is the belief that good performance will lead to desired outcomes or rewards.

Valence is the value or importance an individual places on the anticipated outcomes or rewards.

Question 25
According to McClelland’s Needs Theory, which of the following is not a motivating need? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)
  • A.Need for Power
  • B.Need for Security
  • C.Need for Achievement
  • D.Need for Affiliation
Correct Answer: Need for Security

According to McClelland’s Needs Theory, ‘Need for Security’ is not a motivating need.

 

The theory by McClelland focuses on three needs: 

 

(i) Need for achievement: The drive to excel, to achieve in relation to a set of standards, to strive to succeed

(ii) Need for power: The need to make others behave in a way that they would not have behaved otherwise

(iii) Need for affiliation: The desire for friendly and close interpersonal relationships

 

‘Need for Security’ is the part of Maslow Need Hierarchy Theory among the lower-level needs.

Question 27
As per the Herzberg’s Hygiene Theory of motivation, which among the following is not a motivational factor? (UGC NET Commerce Nov 2017)
  • A.Recognition
  • B.Working Conditions
  • C.Responsibility
  • D.Achievements
Correct Answer: Working Conditions

As per the Herzberg’s Hygiene Theory of motivation, ‘Working Conditions’ is not a motivational factor.

In 1959, Frederick Herzberg, a behavioural scientist proposed a "two-factor theory" or the "motivator-hygiene theory". According to Herzberg, there are some job factors that result in satisfaction while there are other job factors that prevent dissatisfaction. According to Herzberg, the opposite of “Satisfaction” is “No satisfaction” and the opposite of “Dissatisfaction” is “No Dissatisfaction”. Herzberg classified these job factors into two categories:

 

Hygiene factors: Hygiene factors are those job factors which are essential for existence of motivation at workplace. This does not lead to positive satisfaction in the long term. But if these factors are absent / if these factors are non-existent at the workplace, then they lead to dissatisfaction. In other words, hygiene factors are those factors which when adequate/reasonable in a job, pacify the employees and do not make them dissatisfied. These factors are extrinsic to work. Hygiene factors are also called dissatisfiers or maintenance factors as they are required to avoid dissatisfaction. These factors describe the job environment/scenario. The hygiene factors symbolized the physiological needs which the individuals wanted and expected to be fulfilled. Hygiene factors include Pay, Fringe benefits, Physical Working conditions, Status, Interpersonal relations, Job Security.

 

Motivational factors: According to Herzberg, the hygiene factors cannot be regarded as motivators. The motivational factors yield positive satisfaction. These factors are inherent to work. These factors motivate the employees for a superior performance. These factors are called satisfiers. These are factors involved in performing the job. Employees find these factors intrinsically rewarding. The motivators symbolized the psychological needs that were perceived as an additional benefit. Motivational factors include Recognition, Sense of achievement, Growth and promotional opportunities, Responsibility, Meaningfulness of the work.

Question 28
Examine the following statements and choose the correct code: (UGC NET Commerce Aug 2016)Statement – I:Motivation is expensive and above all difficult.Statement – II:Things that are the most motivating to employees tend to be relatively easy to do and less costly.Statement – III:Personally recognizing the accomplishments of employees can be easy.
  • A.All the three statements are correct.
  • B.Statements – II and III only are correct.
  • C.Statements – I and III only are correct.
  • D.Statement – I only is correct.
Correct Answer: Statements – II and III only are correct.

Statement I claims that "Motivation is expensive and above all difficult." This statement is incorrect. While motivation strategies might vary in cost and effort, the most effective motivators for employees are not necessarily expensive or hard to implement. So, Statement I is incorrect.

 

Statement II mentions that "Things that are the most motivating to employees tend to be relatively easy to do and less costly." This statement is accurate. Many impactful motivators for employees, such as personal recognition, appreciation, or acknowledgment, can indeed be easy to implement and don't necessarily require substantial financial investments. So, Statement II is correct.

 

Statement III asserts that "Personally recognizing the accomplishments of employees can be easy." This statement aligns with the concept that personal recognition or appreciation of employees' achievements can be a relatively simple gesture and doesn't have to be a complex or expensive process. So, Statement III is correct.

 

Hence, based on the explanations provided, the correct code would be (B) Statements II and III only are correct.

Question 29
Who propounded “Theory Z”? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)
  • A.WilliamOuchi
  • B.Peter F. Drucker
  • C.Joseph H.Jurau
  • D.Douglas McGregor
Correct Answer: WilliamOuchi

Theory Z was propounded by “William Ouchi” and is explained below:

 

Back in the '70s and '80s, Japanese organizations were arguably the most productive and efficient in the world, and they were making significant inroads into North American and European markets. The secret to their success wasn't necessarily what they were producing. Rather, some argued, it was how they were managing their people – Japanese employees were engaged, empowered, and highly productive. 

 

Management professor William Ouchi argued that Western organizations could learn from their Japanese counterparts. He created Theory Z – a model that, he said, blended the best of Eastern and Western management practices.

 

Ouchi first wrote about Theory Z in his 1981 book, "Theory Z: How American Management Can Meet the Japanese Challenge." He created the theory after conducting research designed to help American companies compete with Japanese businesses. According to Ouchi, the benefits of using Theory Z include reducing employee turnover, increasing commitment, improving morale and job satisfaction, and drastically increasing productivity.

Question 31
Match the following: (UGC NET Management Jun 2013)List-Ia. Self-efficacyb. Goal settingc. Expectancyd. Equity TheoryList-IIA. Determining specific levels of performance for workers to attain them.B. The belief that one’s efforts will positively influence one’s performance.C. People strive to maintain ratio of their own outcomes to their own inputs that are equal to that of those with whom they compare themselves.D. One’s belief about having the capacity to perform a task.
  • A.a-A, b-B, c-C, d-D
  • B.a-D, b-A, c-B, d-C
  • C.a-C, b-D, c-A, d-B
  • D.a-B, b-C, c-D, d-A
Correct Answer: a-D, b-A, c-B, d-C

The correct answer is (B) a-D b-A c-B d-C.

 

Self-efficacy (a) - D: One’s belief about having the capacity to perform a task.

Self-efficacy theory, proposed by Albert Bandura, centers on an individual's belief in their capability to successfully execute tasks, influencing their actions, goals, and level of effort in achieving those goals.

 

Goal setting (b) - A: Determining specific levels of performance for workers to attain them.

Developed by Edwin Locke and Gary Latham, goal-setting theory emphasizes the importance of establishing clear, challenging, and specific objectives for motivation and performance improvement.

 

Expectancy (c) - B: The belief that one’s efforts will positively influence one’s performance.

Vroom's Expectancy Theory states that individuals make choices to maximize pleasure and minimize pain based on three key elements: expectancy (belief that effort leads to performance), instrumentality (belief that performance leads to outcomes), and valence (value attached to outcomes).

 

Equity Theory (d) - C: People strive to maintain a ratio of their own outcomes to their own inputs that are equal to that of those with whom they compare themselves.

John Stacey Adams formulated Equity Theory, suggesting that an individual's motivation is affected by their perception of fairness in the balance between their inputs (efforts, contributions) and outputs (rewards, benefits) compared to others.

Question 33
Which of the following is not perceived as the basic element of motivation?
  • A.Direction
  • B.Intensity
  • C.Performance
  • D.Persistence
Correct Answer: Performance

Direction, Intensity and Persistence are the basic element of motivation. Motivation is the result of the interaction between the individual and the situation. The Three key elements of our definition are intensity, direction, and persistence:

1. Intensity: Intensity is concerned with how hard a person tries. 

2. Direction: The direction is the orientation that benefits the organization.

3. Persistence: Persistence is a measure of how long a person can maintain his or her effort. Motivated individuals stay with a task long enough to achieve their goal.

Question 34
A theory of motivation that is concerned with the beneficial effects of intrinsic motivation and the harmful effects of extrinsic motivation, is termed as: (UGC NET Management Jun 2015)
  • A.Cognitive Evaluation Theory
  • B.Self-efficiency Theory
  • C.Self-determination Theory
  • D.Two-factor Theory
Correct Answer: Self-determination Theory

A theory of motivation that is concerned with the beneficial effects of intrinsic motivation and the harmful effects of extrinsic motivation, is termed as Self-determination Theory.

 

Self-Determination Theory (SDT) is an important theory of motivation that addresses issues of extrinsic and intrinsic motivation. It was given by Edward L. Deci and Richard M. Ryan, psychologists at the University of Rochester. People have innate psychological needs:

(a) Competence: seek to control the outcome and experience mastery.

(b) Relatedness: is the universal want to interact, be connected to, and experience caring for others.

(c) Autonomy: is the universal urge to be causal agents of one’s own life and act in harmony with one’s integrated self.

 

If these universal needs are met, the theory argues that people will function and grow optimally.  To actualize their inherent potential, the social environment needs to nurture these needs. Motivation has often been grouped into two main types: extrinsic and intrinsic.  With extrinsic motivation, a person tends to do a task or activity mainly because doing so will yield some kind of reward or benefit upon completion.  Intrinsic motivation, in contrast, is characterized by doing something purely because of enjoyment or fun.

Question 35
_________theoryof motivation ignores the inner state of the individual and concentrates solely on what happens when he or she takes some action. (UGC NET Management Dec 2014)
  • A.Equity
  • B.Expectancy
  • C.Goal-setting
  • D.Reinforcement
Correct Answer: Goal-setting

The Goal-Setting Theory of Motivation ignores the inner state of the individual and concentrates solely on what happens when he or she takes some action. The theory is explained below:

 

Goal-Setting Theory

Dr Edwin Locke and Dr Gary Latham spent many years researching the theory of goal setting, during which time they identified five elements that need to be in place for us to achieve our goals. In the late 1960s, Locke's pioneering research into goal setting and motivation gave us our modern understanding of goal setting. In his 1968 article "Toward a Theory of Task Motivation and Incentives," he showed that clear goals and appropriate feedback motivate employees. He went on to highlight that working towards a goal is also a major source of motivation – which, in turn, improves performance. Locke's research showed that the more difficult and specific a goal is, the harder people tend to work to achieve it.

 

In one study, Locke reviewed a decade's worth of laboratory and field studies on the effects of goal setting and performance. He found that, for 90 percent of the time, specific and challenging (but not too challenging) goals led to higher performance than easy, or "do your best," goals. For example, telling someone to "try hard" or "do your best" is less effective than saying "try to get more than 80 percent correct," or "concentrate on beating your best time." Likewise, having a goal that's too easy is not motivating. Hard goals are more motivating than easy ones, because it feels more of an accomplishment to achieve something you've worked hard for.

 

A few years after Locke published his article, Dr Gary Latham studied the effects of goal setting in the workplace. His results supported Locke's findings – that there is an inseparable link between goal setting and workplace performance.

 

In 1990, Locke and Latham published their seminal work, "A Theory of Goal Setting & Task Performance." In this book, they repeated the need to set specific and difficult goals, while outlining five other characteristics for successful goal setting.

Question 36
Which of the following best describes the theory X? (UGC NET Management Sep 2013)
  • A.People are committed to their responsibilities.
  • B.Motivation is a result of rational behaviour towards attaining goals.
  • C.The perceived relationship between a given level of efforts and an expected performance.
  • D.None of the above.
Correct Answer: None of the above.

None of the above options describes the theory X.

 

Theory X and Theory Y

Douglas McGregor concluded that a manager’s view of the nature of human beings is based on a certain grouping of assumptions and he or she tends to mold his or her behavior toward employees according to these assumptions.

 

Theory X assumptions are negative:

• Employees inherently dislike work and, whenever possible, will attempt to avoid it. 

• Since employees dislike work, they must be coerced, controlled, or threatened with punishment.

• Employees will avoid responsibilities and seek formal direction whenever possible.

 

Theory Y assumptions are positive:

• Employees can view work as being as natural as rest or play.

• People will exercise self-direction and self-control if they are committed to the objectives.

• The average person can learn to accept, even seek, responsibility.

• The ability to make innovative decisions is widely dispersed throughout the population.

Question 37
Which theory of human motivation focuses on personal perceptions of the performance process? (UGC NET Management Sep 2013)
  • A.Adam’s Theory of Equity
  • B.McClelland’s Need Theory
  • C.Vroom’s Expectancy Theory
  • D.Alderfer’sERG Theory
Correct Answer: Vroom’s Expectancy Theory

Vroom's Expectancy Theory of human motivation focuses on individuals' personal perceptions of the performance process. This theory emphasizes that an individual's motivation is based on their belief that increased effort will lead to better performance (Expectancy), the expectation that good performance will result in valued outcomes (Instrumentality), and the importance they place on these outcomes (Valence). It essentially highlights the conscious choices people make among alternatives to maximize pleasure and minimize pain in their pursuit of achieving specific outcomes.
