Question 27
Explaining motivation as a psychological process, which of the following suggests that “Performance leads to satisfaction”? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2021)
  • A.Herzberg’s two factor Theory
  • B.Vroom’s expectancy Theory
  • C.Porter-Lawler Model
  • D.Adam’s Equity Theory
Correct Answer: Porter-Lawler Model

The Porter and Lawler theory of motivation is based on the assumption that rewards cause satisfaction and that sometimes performance produces reward. They hypothesize that the relationship between satisfaction and performance is linked by another variable rewards. They see good- performance leading to reward which lead to satisfaction. It is a multi-variable model and explains the complex relationship among motivation, performance and satisfaction.

 

They argue that satisfaction does not always lead to performance. Rather is reverse is true, because people can become complacent after having achieved satisfaction once. On the other hand, performance can lead to satisfaction if the reward systems are effective.

Question 28
Consider the following:(a) Challenging work(b) Responsibility(c) Status(d) Job security(e) RecognitionWhich of the above are motivators under Herzberg’s Two Factor Theory? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.(a) and (c) only
  • B.(c), (d) and (e) only
  • C.(a), (b) and (e) only
  • D.(b), (c), (d) and (e) only
Correct Answer: (a), (b) and (e) only

The motivators under Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory are:

Challenging work (Meaningfulness of the work)

Responsibility

Recognition

 

These factors align with Herzberg's notion of motivational factors that yield positive satisfaction and are intrinsic to the job itself, leading to increased motivation and superior performance. Therefore, the correct answer is option (C) - (a), (b), and (e) only.

Question 29
Explaining the relationship between satisfaction and performance, which of the following models suggests that performance leads to satisfaction? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.Maslow’s Need Hierarchy Model
  • B.Herzberg’s Two factor Model
  • C.Adam’s Equity Model
  • D.Porter-Lawler Model
Correct Answer: Porter-Lawler Model

Porter and Lawler's Model posits that performance leads to satisfaction, deviating from the simplistic assumption that satisfaction directly leads to performance. According to this model, several factors interplay in the relationship between satisfaction and performance:

1. Effort: The amount of energy an individual puts into a job.

2. Value of Reward: People evaluate whether the expected rewards from a job are attractive to them.

3. Perceived Effort-Reward Probability: Individuals assess the likelihood that a certain effort level will lead to desired performance and subsequent rewards.

4. Performance: Effort contributes to performance, influenced by individual abilities, traits, and role perceptions.

5. Rewards: Performance leads to both extrinsic (external, e.g., money, recognition) and intrinsic (internal feelings of self-esteem) rewards.

6. Satisfaction: Satisfaction results from both extrinsic and intrinsic rewards. An individual compares actual rewards with perceived equitable rewards. If actual rewards meet or exceed perceived equitable rewards, satisfaction occurs; if less, dissatisfaction arises.

Question 30
Choose the correct answer regarding the theories of motivation from the following statements:(a) The concept of ERG theory is similar to Maslow’s hierarchy of needs(b) Theory ‘X’ and ‘Y’ are similar to each other(c) Two factor theory is similar to Vroom’s theoryChoose your answer from the following options: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.Only (a)
  • B.Only (b)
  • C.Only (a) and (b)
  • D.(a), (b) and (c)
Correct Answer: Only (a)

Statement (a) is correct. The ERG theory, formulated by Clayton Alderfer, shares similarities with Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs theory. Alderfer's ERG theory realigned Maslow's hierarchy into three core needs: Existence, Relatedness, and Growth. These needs bear resemblance to Maslow's categories of physiological, safety, social, esteem, and self-actualization needs.

 

However, statements (b) and (c) are incorrect:

 

Theory X and Theory Y, formulated by Douglas McGregor, present contrasting assumptions about employee behavior. Theory X assumes negative views about employees, whereas Theory Y presents more positive assumptions. They are not similar; rather, they offer divergent perspectives.

 

Two-Factor Theory, introduced by Frederick Herzberg, and Vroom's Expectancy Theory are distinct models of motivation. Herzberg's theory categorizes job factors into hygiene and motivational factors, while Vroom's theory focuses on effort, performance, and outcomes linked to motivation. They aren't similar in their approach or classifications.

Question 31
Choose the correct option regarding theories of motivation:A. The concept of ERG theory is similar to Maslow’s hierarchy of needs.B. Theory X has positive assumptions and Theory Y has negative assumptions.C. Two factor Theory is derived by Mcgregor.Choose the correct answer from the options given below: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)
  • A.A only
  • B.A and B only
  • C.B and C only
  • D.A, B and C only
Correct Answer: A only

The correct answer is indeed (A). Here's why:

 

Statement A is accurate. The ERG theory proposed by Clayton Alderfer aligns with Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs. Alderfer restructured the hierarchy into three core groups: Existence, Relatedness, and Growth, which correspond to Maslow's categories of physiological, safety, social, esteem, and self-actualization needs, respectively.

 

However, the other statements are incorrect:

 

Statement B, about Theory X and Theory Y, is not accurate. Theory X presents negative assumptions about employees, while Theory Y offers more positive assumptions about their behavior. It's the reverse of what's stated in the question.

 

Statement C, concerning the Two-Factor Theory, is attributed to Frederick Herzberg, not McGregor. Herzberg introduced this theory that categorizes job factors into hygiene and motivational factors, indicating elements that prevent dissatisfaction and those that lead to positive satisfaction, respectively.

Question 32
As per the Vroom’s Expectancy theory of motivation ‘Instrumentality’ relates: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)
  • A.Efforts to performance
  • B.Efforts with first level outcome
  • C.Performance with first level outcome
  • D.First level outcome to second level outcome
Correct Answer: First level outcome to second level outcome

The correct answer is (D). In Vroom's Expectancy Theory:

 

Instrumentality relates to the relationship between the first level outcome and the second level outcome. It's the belief that performing well (first level outcome) will result in obtaining valued rewards or outcomes (second level outcome). It essentially concerns whether a person believes that their effort and performance will lead to the desired outcomes.

 

Expectancy refers to the belief that effort will result in improved performance. This is the belief that if someone works harder, they will achieve better results.

 

Valence signifies the value an individual places on the expected outcome. It's about the importance attached to the anticipated outcome. Positive valence means the person prefers achieving the outcome to not achieving it.

Question 33
According to Vroom’s expectancy theory of motivation, which of the following refers to the term ‘valence’? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2019)
  • A.Subjective probability of achieving an outcome
  • B.Efforts made by an individual for the first level outcome
  • C.Relation between the first level an second level outcomes to each other
  • D.Strength to an individual’s preference for a particular outcome
Correct Answer: Strength to an individual’s preference for a particular outcome

Valence refers to the strength of an individual's preference for a specific outcome. It represents the importance or value that an individual places on the expected outcome. If someone highly values a particular outcome, they will have a positive valence towards it.

Question 34
Theory ‘Y’ of Motivation assumes that:
  • A.A person works only when coerced
  • B.An average employee cannot be motivated
  • C.A person has inherent dislike for work
  • D.People do not hate work
Correct Answer: People do not hate work

Theory Y of motivation, as proposed by Douglas McGregor, assumes that people do not inherently dislike work. Instead, it suggests a positive view of employees:

  • Employees can view work as natural, similar to rest or play.
  • They can exercise self-direction and self-control if they are committed to the objectives.
  • The average person is capable of accepting responsibility and seeking it out.
  • The ability to make innovative decisions is not limited but rather dispersed throughout the population.

 

This theory is in stark contrast to Theory X, which assumes a more negative perspective on employee motivation, stating that individuals inherently dislike work and must be coerced or controlled to perform effectively.

Question 35
According to Herzberg, which of the following is a satisfier? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2022)
  • A.Job Security
  • B.Company Policy
  • C.Recognition
  • D.Working Conditions
Correct Answer: Recognition

According to Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory, recognition is categorized as a satisfier or a motivator factor. Satisfiers are intrinsic to the job and lead to positive satisfaction. They are factors inherently involved in performing the job and are found to be intrinsically rewarding by employees. Recognition at work is one such motivational factor, contributing to job satisfaction and intrinsic motivation among employees.

Question 36
Arrange the following in the correct sequence of Maslow’s Hierarchy of need starting from the lowest order need. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2022)A. Job SecurityB. AchievementC. Transforming perception of self into reality.D. HungerE.BelonginessChoose the correct answerfrom the options given below:
  • A.D, B, E, A, C

  • C.D, A, E, B, C
  • D.E, D, C, B, A
Correct Answer: D, A, E, B, C

Option C is the correct answer. The correct sequence of Maslow’s Hierarchy of Needs starting from the lowest order need is:

D. Hunger (Physiological needs)

A. Job Security (Safety needs)

E. Belongingness (Social needs)

B. Achievement (Esteem needs)

C. Transforming perception of self into reality (Self-actualization)

Question 37
Arrange the following needs of Maslow's Need Hierarchy in right sequence starting from the highest order to the lowest order need.a. Social Belongingnessb. Physiologicalc. Safety-Securityd. Esteeme. Self-ActualisationChoose the correct answer from the options given below: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)
  • A.b, c, a, d, e
  • B.b, a, c, d, e
  • C.e, d, a, c, b
  • D.e, d, c, a, b
Correct Answer: e, d, a, c, b

Maslow’s Need Hierarchy from the highest order to the lowest order need is as follows:

a) Self-Actualization Needs: These are the highest order needs and include the desire for personal growth, fulfilment, and realizing one's full potential.

b) Esteem Needs: These needs include the desire for recognition, respect, and status from others, as well as a sense of self-esteem and self-respect.

c) Love and Belonging Needs: These needs include the desire for social interaction, companionship, love, and a sense of belonging and acceptance by others.

d) Safety Needs: These needs include the desire for physical safety, security, stability, and freedom from harm.

f) Physiological Needs: These are the lowest order needs and include the basic requirements for survival, such as food, water, shelter, warmth, and other biological needs.

Question 38
Herzberg proposed two-factor theory. According to him the distinction between the Hygiene factors and motivators is: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2015)
  • A.Hygiene factors lead to dissatisfaction while motivators lead to satisfaction.
  • B.Hygiene factors prevent satisfaction while motivators prevent dissatisfaction.
  • C.Hygiene factors prevent dissatisfaction while motivators provide satisfaction.
  • D.Hygiene factors provide satisfaction while motivators enhance satisfaction.
Correct Answer: Hygiene factors prevent dissatisfaction while motivators provide satisfaction.

Herzberg's two-factor theory distinguishes between hygiene factors and motivators based on their effects (C) Hygiene factors prevent dissatisfaction while motivators provide satisfaction.

 

Hygiene factors, like job security and working conditions, are essential to avoid dissatisfaction. When present, they prevent employees from being dissatisfied, but their presence alone doesn’t lead to satisfaction. On the other hand, motivators, such as recognition and opportunities for growth, are intrinsic to the work itself and lead to satisfaction when present.

Question 39

  • B.Under the conditions of modern industrial life, the intellectual potentialities of the average human being are only partially utilised.
  • C.External control and the threat of punishment are the only means for producing effort towards organizational objectives.
  • D.Average human beings learn, under proper conditions, not only to accept responsibility but also to seek it.

McGregor's Theory Y is based on the idea that employees are intrinsically motivated to work towards organizational objectives and that they seek responsibility and self-fulfilment in their work.

 

The assumptions that are part of Theory Y are:

A. The degree of commitment to objectives is in proportion to the size of the rewards associated with their achievement.

B. Under the conditions of modern industrial life, the intellectual potentialities of the average human being are only partially utilised.

D. Average human beings learn, under proper conditions, not only to accept responsibility but also to seek it.

 

Therefore, option C is the assumption that is not part of McGregor's Theory Y.

Question 42
Given below are two statements: One is labelled as Assertion A and the other is labelled as Reason R:(UGC NET Commerce Jun 2020)Assertion A:According to Herzberg, preventing or reducing dissatisfaction at work is not the same as providing satisfaction.Reason R:Under the ‘two factory theory’, job satisfaction and dissatisfaction are the two different aspects of work motivation.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are true but R is NOT the correct explanation of A
  • C.A is true but R is false
  • D.A is false but R is true
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true and R is the correct explanation of A

Herzberg's Two-Factor Theory makes a clear distinction between factors that lead to satisfaction and those that prevent dissatisfaction at the workplace. The hygiene factors prevent dissatisfaction but do not directly lead to long-term satisfaction, while the motivators are directly linked to positive satisfaction and intrinsic motivation. Therefore, both the assertion and the reason are true, and the reason correctly explains the assertion, making option (A) the correct choice.

Question 43
‘Motivation-force or level of efforts is not equal to satisfaction and performance’ is propounded by:(UGC NET Commerce Jun 2019)
  • A.Porter-Lawler model
  • B.Vroom’s expectancy theory
  • C.XandYtheory
  • D.Adam’s equity theory
Correct Answer: Porter-Lawler model

The Porter-Lawler model presents a more complex relationship between motivation, satisfaction, and performance. Unlike some traditional assumptions that link motivation directly to satisfaction and performance, this model emphasizes that effort or motivation doesn't directly lead to performance. Instead, it's mediated by abilities, traits, and role perceptions. Ultimately, performance influences satisfaction, as per the Porter-Lawler model.

Question 44
Mr. Mohan an MBA with specialisation in Human Resources joined a company XYZ into the business of garments in Delhi. Before joining the company XYZ, he had a prior experience of working in corporates for 5 years. He has worked in the area of compensation dealing with workers and employees. In the company XYZ, Mr. Mohan was entrusted with the work of dealing with both workers and executives and look towards their compensation both in theory and as prescribed by the government of Delhi. The company XYZ believed in both types of benefits to be given to their employees- both workers and executives- fringe benefits and non-fringe benefits. For executives, the company XYZ believes in equity both within the company and outside also. All policies of the company relating to compensation management were told to Mr Mohan and he must follow them objectively.Management of XYZ company asks Mr. Mohan to answer the question that,’ A behaviour which has a rewarding experience is likely to be repeated’ is postulated by ________? (UGC NET Management Jun 2020)
  • A.Behavioural theory
  • B.Reinforcement and expectancy theory
  • C.Agency theory
  • D.Contingency theory
Correct Answer: Reinforcement and expectancy theory

The answer is indeed (B) Reinforcement and expectancy theory. This theory suggests that behaviors followed by positive consequences or rewards are more likely to be repeated. It focuses on the idea that individuals are motivated to perform certain behaviors if they believe that such behaviors will lead to desired outcomes or rewards.

Question 45
According to Maslow's hierarchy of needs, which one of the following organizational aspects will not be included in the self-actualization needs? (UGC NET Management Dec 2022)
  • A.Advancement
  • B.Job challenge
  • C.Status
  • D.Self-image
Correct Answer: Status

Maslow's hierarchy of needs is a theory of human motivation that suggests that individuals have different needs that must be met in a specific order. According to this theory, individuals have five primary needs, which are arranged in a hierarchy, with each need building upon the previous one. The needs are physiological, safety, love/belonging, esteem, and self-actualization.

 

Self-actualization is the highest level of need in Maslow's hierarchy and refers to the desire to achieve one's full potential and to become everything that one is capable of becoming. It is a state of being in which individuals feel fulfilled, satisfied, and content with themselves and their lives.

 

Status and organizational aspects, such as job title, rank, and authority, are often associated with the need for esteem in Maslow's hierarchy. Esteem needs include both the need for self-esteem, which involves a sense of self-worth and self-respect, and the need for esteem from others, which involves recognition, respect, and admiration from others.

 

While self-actualization is a higher need than esteem, it does not necessarily exclude the importance of status and organizational aspects altogether. However, the focus on self-actualization is on personal growth, self-fulfilment, and the realization of one's full potential, rather than on external markers of success such as job title or rank.

  • D.Goal definition → Goal acceptance → Efforts → Satisfaction → Performance → Rewards.
Correct Answer: Goal definition → Goal acceptance → Efforts → Performance → Reward → Satisfaction.

Absolutely, (B) is the correct order for the stages in goal-setting theory:

1. Goal definition

2. Goal acceptance

3. Efforts

4. Performance

5. Reward

6. Satisfaction

Question 47
Assertion A:The physiological needs are essential for living but they are determined by social environment.Reasoning R:These needs may be motivators in backward countries but in a developed country, these needs are supposed to be satisfied, hence, they may not be considered motivators.(UGC NET Commerce Jul 2016)
  • A.Assertion A and Reasoning R, both are correct, but R is not right explanation of A.
  • B.Assertion A and Reasoning R, both are correct, and R is correct explanation of A.
  • C.Assertion A is correct, whereas Reasoning R is incorrect.
  • D.Reasoning R is correct, whereas Assertion A is incorrect.
Correct Answer: Assertion A and Reasoning R, both are correct, and R is correct explanation of A.

Assertion A is indeed correct as physiological needs, such as food, water, and shelter, are crucial for sustaining life. However, Reasoning R is not an accurate explanation. In developed countries, while these basic needs are often fulfilled, they still serve as motivators. Even in societies where these needs are generally satisfied, they can still drive motivation. Thus, while the assertion is true, the reasoning provided doesn't offer an accurate explanation for it. Hence, the correct choice is (A) Assertion A and Reasoning R, both are correct, but R is not the right explanation of A.

Quiz Attempt #118962

Total Questions: 35
Question 1
A phenomenon in which the norm for consensus overrides that realistic appraisal of alternative course of action is: (UGC NET Management Jun 2024)
  • A.Groupshift
  • B.Groupthink
  • C.Brainstorming
  • D.Nominal group technique
Correct Answer: Groupthink

Groupthink is a psychological phenomenon where the desire for harmony or conformity in a group results in irrational or dysfunctional decision-making. Members suppress dissenting viewpoints, fail to critically analyze alternatives, and prioritize consensus over realistic appraisal, which can lead to poor outcomes.

 

Groupshift (A) refers to a change in group behavior or attitudes towards a more extreme position after group discussion.

 

Brainstorming (C) is a creative group activity to generate ideas without criticism.

 

Nominal group technique (D) is a structured method for group brainstorming that encourages contributions from all participants.

 

Thus, the phenomenon described is best captured by option (B) Groupthink.

Question 2
Who is thepropounderof the ‘Group Exchange Theory’? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2023)
  • A.John Thibaut and Harold Kelly
  • B.Keith Davis
  • C.William G.Scoll
  • D.George Terry
Correct Answer: John Thibaut and Harold Kelly

John Thibaut and Harold Kelley are social psychologists who are well-known for their development of the Social Exchange Theory, also referred to as the Group Exchange Theory. This theory explores the social and interpersonal dynamics of how individuals form and maintain relationships based on the principles of costs and rewards.

 

In the context of relationships, the Social Exchange Theory proposes that individuals engage in relationships where the benefits or rewards outweigh the costs. People evaluate their relationships based on what they give and receive, aiming to maximize rewards and minimize costs. This theory has been influential in understanding various aspects of human interactions, including friendships, romantic relationships, and even economic transactions.

Question 3
Which of the following are the advantages of group decision making? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2023)(A) More information and knowledge are available(B) Enhanced communication of decision may result(C) Undesirable compromises may happen(D) Groupthink may occur(E) It is costlierChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A and B Only
  • B.A and D Only
  • C.A, B and D Only
  • D.A, B and C Only
Correct Answer: A and B Only

The correct answer is option (A) - A and B Only

 

Advantages of group decision making include:

 

(A) More information and knowledge are available: Group decision making allows for pooling of diverse perspectives, expertise, and information from multiple individuals, leading to better-informed decisions.

 

(B) Enhanced communication of decision may result: Group discussions facilitate the exchange of ideas, clarification of viewpoints, and collective understanding of the decision-making process, which can lead to better communication of the decision to stakeholders.

 

The disadvantages mentioned in options (C) and (D) are not advantages of group decision making:

 

(C) Undesirable compromises may happen: Undesirable compromises are a potential disadvantage of group decision making, not an advantage.

 

(D) Groupthink may occur: Groupthink, which is the tendency for group members to conform to a dominant viewpoint and suppress dissenting opinions to maintain harmony, is also a disadvantage, not an advantage.

Question 4

Eager, Anxious, gather data about similarities and differences among members and keep things simpleb. Upset and Depressedc. Less dissatisfied and a feeling of belongings to the groupd. Forming: Members are eager, anxious, gathering data about similarities and differences among members, and keeping things simple.

Behaviour: (a) Eager, anxious, gather data about similarities and differences among members and keep things simple.

Behavior: (d) Confront the differences, feel angry or frustrated, a lot of competition and hostilities.

Behavior: (e) Interdependence in personal relations, tendency to get involved in problem-solving.

Behavior: (b) Upset and depressed.

Question 7
TheRinglemanneffect describes: (UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.the tendency of groups to make risky decisions
  • B.social loafing
  • C.social facilitation
  • D.the satisfaction of members’ social needs
Correct Answer: social loafing

The Ringlemann effect is synonymous with social loafing. It denotes the phenomenon where individual members of a group become progressively less productive as the group's size increases. This effect, discovered by Maximilien Ringelmann, illustrates the inverse relationship between group size and individual contribution to task completion.

 

Social loafing, encompassed by the Ringlemann effect, refers to the tendency of individuals to exert less effort when working together in a group compared to when working individually.

Question 8
Consider the following. (UGC NET HRM Jul 2016)Assertion “A”:The organizational effectiveness should be measured in terms of the entire cycle of the input-process-output system.Reason “R”:Organization shall depend on its capacity to adjust with the environment while holding together its internal sub-systems.
  • A.A is right and R is wrong.
  • B.Both A and R are right, but, R does not explain the R.
  • C.A is wrong and in attempting to prove a wrong assertion, the R also is wrong.
  • D.Both A and R are right; and R explains the A.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are right; and R explains the A.

Both the Assertion (A) and Reason (R) are correct, and R explains A.

 

The Assertion emphasizes that organizational effectiveness should be assessed considering the entire cycle of the input-process-output system. This approach enables a comprehensive evaluation of how inputs are transformed into outputs through organizational processes.

 

The Reason complements the Assertion by highlighting that an organization's success relies on its capability to adapt to the environment while maintaining cohesion within its internal subsystems. This aligns with the input-process-output model, which emphasizes understanding how organizations interact with their environment (inputs), process information or resources internally, and generate outputs accordingly.

 

The Input-Process-Output model is instrumental in assessing team effectiveness by elucidating the connections between team inputs, processes, and outputs. It allows for a deeper comprehension of team performance and aids in optimizing their effectiveness by providing necessary resources and support systems, including rewards, training, physical environment, managerial support, and technology.

Question 9
Match the following management techniques (List – I) with theirpropounders(List – II): (UGC NET HRM Aug 2016)List – Ia. MBO as a system of managerial leadershipb. TOWS matrix of strategic planningc. Delphi Techniqued. BrainstormingList – IIi. HeinzWeihrichii. Alex F. Osborniii. GeorgeOdiorneiv. Olaf Helmer
  • A.a-ii, b-iv, c-iii, d-i

  • C.a-iv, b-ii, c-i, d-iii
  • D.a-iii, b-ii, c-iv, d-i
Correct Answer: a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii

a. MBO as a system of managerial leadership - George Odiorne

Peter Drucker first used the term "Management by Objectives", MBO in his 1954 book "The Practice of Management". While the basic ideas of MBO were not original to Drucker, they pulled from other management practices to create a complete “system”. The idea draws on the many ideas presented in Mary Parker Follett's 1926 essay, "The Giving of Orders". After the term and idea were brought up, Drucker's student, George Odiorne, continued to develop the idea in his book "Management Decisions by Objectives", published in the mid-1960s. Later MBO was popularized by companies like Hewlett-Packard, who claimed it led to their success.

 

b. TOWS matrix of strategic planning - Heinz Weihrich

The TOWS Matrix, proposed by Heinz Weihrich, is a conceptual framework for a systematic analysis that facilities matching the external threats and opportunities with the internal weaknesses and strengths of the organization. The TOWS Matrix indicates four conceptually distinct alternative strategies, tactics and actions. The process of strategy formulation and the TOWS analysis is represented by 'T' stands for threats, 'O' for opportunities, 'W' for weaknesses and 'S' for strengths.

 

c. Delphi Technique - Olaf Helmer

The Delphi method was originally developed in the early 1950s at the RAND Corporation by Olaf Helmer and Norman Dalkey.  In Delphi decision groups, a series of questionnaires, surveys, etc. are sent to selected respondents (the Delphi group) through a facilitator who oversees responses of their panel of experts. The group does not meet face-to-face. All communication is normally in writing (letters or email). Members of the groups are selected because they are experts or they have relevant information. The responses are collected and analysed to determine conflicting viewpoints on each point. The process continues in order to work towards synthesis and building consensus.

 

d. Brain storming - Alex F. Osborn

In 1941 Alex Osborn, an advertising executive, found that conventional business meetings were inhibiting the creation of new ideas and proposed some rules designed to help stimulate them. He was looking for rules which would give people the freedom of mind and action to spark off and reveal new ideas. To "think up" was originally the term he used to describe the process he developed, and that in turn came to be known as Brainstorming. He described brainstorming as "a conference technique by which a group attempts to find a solution for a specific problem by amassing all the ideas spontaneously by its members".

Question 10
Which of the following statements are true/false about a dyadic unit? (UGC NET HRM Aug 2016)(a) A dyadic unit is defined in terms of an employee and his supervisor.(b) The stronger dyads weaken organizational linkages.(c) Helping relationship in a dyad is a one way process offered by the supervisor.(d) A dyad will prosper despite absence of trusting relationships between the employee and the supervisor.
  • A.(b) is true, (a), (c) and (d) are false.
  • B.(a) is true, (b), (c) and (d) are false.
  • C.(d) is true, (a), (b) and (c) are false.
  • D.(a)and(c) are true, (b) and (d) are false.
Correct Answer: (a) is true, (b), (c) and (d) are false.

The correct answer is (B): (a) is true, (b), (c), and (d) are false.

 

Explanation:

(a) True: A dyadic unit is indeed defined in terms of an employee and their supervisor. A dyad represents a relationship between two individuals, in this case, an employee and their immediate supervisor.

 

(b) False: Stronger dyads do not weaken organizational linkages. On the contrary, stronger and positive dyadic relationships, characterized by trust and mutual respect, can strengthen organizational cohesion and effectiveness.

 

(c) False: The helping relationship in a dyad is not solely a one-way process offered by the supervisor. In a healthy dyadic relationship, support and assistance are exchanged reciprocally between the employee and the supervisor.

 

(d) False: A dyad will not prosper in the absence of trusting relationships between the employee and the supervisor. Trust and mutual understanding are fundamental elements for a successful and productive dyadic relationship within an organization.

Question 11
Which of the following may be a possible consequence of inter-group conflict within the involved groups? (UGC NET HRM Jan 2017)a. Group cohesiveness increases.b. Group becomes task oriented.c. Organisation structure becomes more rigid.d. Leadership becomes more rigid.
  • A.a, b and d
  • B.b, c and d
  • C.a, b, c and d
  • D.a and b only
Correct Answer: a, b, c and d

The possible consequences of inter-group conflict within the involved groups are:

a. Group cohesiveness increases.

b. Group becomes task-oriented.

c. Organization structure becomes more rigid.

d. Leadership becomes more rigid.

 

Inter-group conflict impacts group dynamics significantly. It can lead to increased group cohesiveness as members unite against the other group. This cohesion might intensify pressures to conform to group norms, fostering strong alignment but potentially leading to groupthink.

 

Within conflicting groups, focus on the task often intensifies, making them more efficient and loyal to their objectives. However, this intense focus might lead to the groups becoming closed off from others and losing sight of the organization's goals, contributing to rigidity in the organization's structure and leadership styles.

 

Effective communication between conflicting groups is crucial. Lack of communication can result in misunderstandings and isolation, which can negatively impact inter-group relationships and the organization as a whole.

Question 12
Which of the following describes "Command Groups"? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2015)
  • A.A group established to solve a particular problem.
  • B.A unit established by the organisation to accomplish specific tasks.
  • C.Group characterised by intimate, face-to-face association and cooperation.
  • D.Formal groups that consist of managers and their direct subordinates.
Correct Answer: Formal groups that consist of managers and their direct subordinates.

The correct answer is (D): Formal groups that consist of managers and their direct subordinates.

 

Command groups are a type of formal group within an organization. They specifically comprise managers and their immediate subordinates, forming a hierarchical structure. These groups are instrumental in the chain of command, facilitating communication and decision-making between managers and their direct reports.

 

These groups are a part of formal organizational structures designed to accomplish specific tasks or execute managerial directives within the organization.

Question 13
A small voluntary group of employees doing similar or related work who meet regularly to identify, analyse and solve product quality problems and to improve general operations is known as: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2013)
  • A.Task Group
  • B.Kaizen Groups
  • C.Quality Circles
  • D.Informal Groups
Correct Answer: Quality Circles

A Quality Circle is a group of workers who do the same or similar work, who meet regularly to identify, analyze and solve work-related problems. Normally small in size, the group is usually led by a supervisor or manager and presents its solutions to management; where possible, workers implement the solutions themselves in order to improve the performance of the organization and motivate employees. "Quality circle in India" was written by S R Udpa. Quality circle activity was brought to India by the Bharat Heavy Electricals Ltd.

 

Other options of the question defined below:

 

Task Groups: Created to handle specific organizational assignments or tasks.

 

Kaizen Groups: A part of the Kaizen (continuous improvement) approach, these groups focus on introducing small incremental changes in a business to enhance quality and efficiency.

 

Informal Groups: Unlike formal groups established by organizations, informal groups emerge naturally based on common interests among organizational members.

Question 14
Arrange the following phases of group formation in their right sequence: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2013)(a) forming(b) norming(c) performing(d) storming(e) adjourning
  • A.(a), (d), (c), (b), (e)
  • B.(a), (d), (b), (c), (e)
  • C.(a), (b), (d), (c), (e)
  • D.(a), (c), (d), (b), (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (d), (b), (c), (e)

The correct sequence of phases of group formation according to the model proposed by Bruce Tuckman is:

(a) Forming

(d) Storming

(b) Norming

(c) Performing

(e) Adjourning

 

The stages are:

 

1. Forming: This is the initial stage where the team comes together, and members get acquainted with each other.

2. Storming: In this phase, conflicts may arise as team members begin to express differing opinions and challenge each other. Trust starts to develop, allowing for more open communication.

3. Norming: The team starts to resolve conflicts, establishes norms and rules, and works cohesively toward shared goals.

4. Performing: At this stage, the team operates efficiently, collaboratively, and effectively to achieve its objectives.

5. Adjourning: Tuckman and Jensen added this phase, where the group disbands or adjourns after successfully achieving its goals.

Question 15
The essence of Exchange theory regarding formation of a group is: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2014)
  • A.People are attracted to one another on the basis of exchange of similar attitudes towards common objects and goals.
  • B.People are attracted to one another interacting with one another and cooperating to achieve the goals.
  • C.People are attracted to one another by having propinquity to each other.
  • D.People are attracted to one another by interacting through reward-cost outcomes.
Correct Answer: People are attracted to one another by interacting through reward-cost outcomes.

The essence of Exchange theory regarding the formation of a group is described in option (D) “People are attracted to one another by interacting through reward-cost outcomes”.

 

Exchange Theory of Group Formation revolves around the concept of interactions being driven by the perceived rewards and costs involved. Individuals are attracted to a group when they perceive a positive outcome or rewards from interacting with its members, exceeding the costs or negatives associated with the interaction. Rewards from these interactions satisfy needs, while costs can lead to feelings of anxiety, frustration, embarrassment, or fatigue. While propinquity (physical proximity), interaction, and common attitudes do play roles, the theory's core lies in assessing the balance of rewards and costs in social interactions.

Question 16
Which of the following sequences of the Group Development Process is correct? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2009)I. PerformingII. StormingIII. AdjourningIV. FormingV. Norming
  • A.IV, V, III, II, I
  • B.I, III, II, V, IV
  • C.II, IV, III, V, I
  • D.IV, II, V, I, III
Correct Answer: IV, II, V, I, III

In 1965, psychologist Bruce Tuckman proposed model of group development. This model suggests that groups and teams move through a series of stages in order to achieve their peak level of performance. Four stages of the model are: Forming – Storming – Norming – Performing. In the first stage of team building, the forming of the team takes place. In the storming stage, enough initial trust has been developed between team members that they start to feel comfortable expressing discontent and challenging others' opinions. In the norming stage the team manages to have one goal and come to a mutual plan for the team at this stage. It is possible for some teams to reach the performing stage. Tuckman, along with his colleague Mary Ann Jensen, proposed a fifth stage of group development in 1977 called Adjourning. If a group has fulfilled its goals and objectives, it will move into the adjourning stage.

Question 17
Which of the following decreases group cohesiveness? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2012)
  • A.Agreement on group goals
  • B.Frequency of interaction
  • C.Large group size
  • D.All the above
Correct Answer: Large group size

The correct option is (C) Large group size.

 

In larger groups, it becomes more challenging to maintain cohesiveness due to several factors. Communication becomes more complex, individuals might feel less connected to the group due to less interaction, and it can be harder to reach consensus or agreement on group goals or tasks. As a result, larger group size tends to decrease cohesiveness compared to smaller, more closely-knit groups where it's easier to coordinate work and foster agreement on common goals.

Question 18
The group to which a person would like to belong is known as: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2012)
  • A.Primary Group
  • B.Membership Group
  • C.Reference Group
  • D.None of the above
Correct Answer: Reference Group

The group to which a person aspires to belong is termed as a Reference Group. These are the groups individuals identify with or aim to be a part of, often consisting of socially or professionally esteemed entities. For instance, individuals joining protests led by Team Anna can form reference groups.

 

On the other hand, Primary Groups, as defined by Cooley, involve intimate, face-to-face relationships and cooperation, like family or peer groups.

 

Membership Groups refer to the groups an individual is actively a part of, such as clubs, worker unions, or cooperative societies.

Question 19
A type of group discussion process in which members of the group are encouraged to generate as many imaginative and creative ideas in a relatively short period of time is known as (UGC NET Management Dec 2009)
  • A.Brain storming
  • B.Group working
  • C.Simulation
  • D.Group effect
Correct Answer: Brain storming

It is referred to as "brainstorming," a group discussion method that encourages members to generate numerous imaginative and creative ideas within a concise timeframe. This technique aims to foster a free flow of ideas without judgment, allowing for diverse thinking and ideation within a group setting.

Question 20
Group norms are strongly enforced by groups if they
  • A.aid in group survival
  • B.simplify expected behaviour of members
  • C.express central values of the group
  • D.All the above
Correct Answer: All the above

Group norms are guidelines or standards of behavior that dictate what is considered acceptable or expected within a group. These norms are often strongly enforced by groups when they serve various crucial purposes:

 

1. Aid in group survival: Norms that contribute to the group's ability to function effectively and cohesively, ultimately aiding its survival, tend to be strongly enforced.

 

2. Simplify expected behavior of members: Norms simplify and clarify what behaviors are anticipated from each member, fostering a sense of predictability and coherence within the group.

 

3. Express central values of the group: Norms often embody the core values and principles upheld by the group, helping to define its identity and unique characteristics.

 

When norms align with these purposes—supporting group survival, simplifying expected behavior, and expressing central values—they tend to be enforced more rigorously by the group.

Question 21
Which of the following is not a correct statement? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2011)
  • A.Informal groups always hamper the performance of formal groups.
  • B.Informal groups do not have prescribed goals and relationships.
  • C.Informal and formal groups co-exist in organisations.
  • D.Informal groups provide safety valve for employee emotions.
Correct Answer: Informal groups always hamper the performance of formal groups.

Informal groups within an organization do not always hamper the performance of formal groups. While they exist outside the formal structure and might not have the explicit approval of management, their impact on formal groups can vary. Informal groups often serve social needs and can enhance the organizational environment by providing emotional support, easing rigid bureaucratic practices, and even improving task performance at times.

 

Informal groups are more social in nature and primarily cater to the needs and interests of their members, rather than focusing solely on organizational objectives. These groups can serve various functions, from providing emotional support to facilitating smoother task execution or challenging bureaucratic norms.

 

So, the statement (A) that informal groups always hamper the performance of formal groups is not universally accurate. The impact of informal groups on formal groups can be diverse, and in some cases, they may complement or even enhance formal group performance.

Question 22
When team-building can be attempted by creating artificial teams in which people get opportunity to experiment and learn from their behaviour in a less threatening context, it is based on: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2013)
  • A.Behaviour Modification Approach
  • B.Action Research Approach
  • C.Simulation Approach
  • D.Team Role Approach
Correct Answer: Simulation Approach

These methods of team-building are rooted in the Simulation Approach. This involves creating artificial teams or scenarios where individuals can experiment and learn from their behavior within a less pressured environment. Here are some key techniques within the Simulation Approach:

 

1. Management Games: These games are designed to encourage innovative thinking, team collaboration, decision-making under limited information, and leadership skills. They serve as practical tools for understanding management concepts and are tailored for different management levels.

 

2. Case Studies: These are detailed examples presenting real-life scenarios to demonstrate theoretical concepts in a practical setting. Case studies facilitate active learning, problem-solving, and the application of theoretical knowledge to real-world situations.

 

3. Role Playing: In role-playing, participants assume specific roles and act out scenarios related to the learning objectives. This method fosters quick thinking and realistic reactions in various situations, such as customer service training or employee-employer interactions.

 

4. In-basket Training: This exercise involves a set of business-related materials like emails, reports, and memos, requiring the trainee to prioritize and make decisions based on the given information.

 

All these techniques fall under the Simulation Approach, offering participants a safe space to practice and learn without the high stakes or pressures of actual workplace situations.

Question 23
Who among the following concluded that the factory was a social system and informal groups at workplace play a vital role in industrial affairs?
  • A.Elton Mayo
  • B.Henry Fayol
  • C.Blake and Mouton
  • D.Herzberg
Correct Answer: Elton Mayo

Elton Mayo, indeed, was a key figure in highlighting the significance of informal groups within the workplace and emphasizing the social aspects of organizations. His research, notably the Hawthorne Studies, delved into the social dynamics of work environments, shedding light on the importance of informal groups in industrial affairs. Mayo's findings were instrumental in shaping the human relations movement and steering attention toward the social and psychological aspects of work settings, rather than solely focusing on formal organizational structures.

Question 24
The tendency of people to expend less effort when working collectively than when working individually is called: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2014)
  • A.Social loafing
  • B.Socialising
  • C.Adjourning
  • D.Social action
Correct Answer: Social loafing

Social loafing refers to the phenomenon where individuals tend to exert less effort when working in a group compared to when working alone. This reduced effort stems from a perceived diffusion of responsibility or the belief that individual contributions may not be as crucial or noticeable within a collective effort.

Question 25
When one group’s performance depends on another group’s performance, it may result into inter-group conflict. Such dependence is described as: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2014)
  • A.Pooled interdependence
  • B.Classical interdependence
  • C.Reciprocal interdependence
  • D.Sequential interdependence
Correct Answer: Sequential interdependence

In the 1967 book "Organizations in Action," sociologist James D. Thompson defined three types of interdependence to describe the intensity of interactions and behaviours within an organizational structure. The study of interdependence helps business owners understand how the different departments or units within their organization depend on the performance of others.

 

1. Pooled Interdependence: Pooled interdependence is perhaps the loosest form of the three. In this type of interdependence, each organizational department or business unit performs completely separate functions. While departments may not directly interact and do not directly depend on each other in the pooled interdependence model, each does contribute individual pieces to the same overall puzzle. This creates an almost blind, indirect dependence on the performance of others wherein one department's failures could lead to the failure of the overall process.

 

2. Sequential Interdependence: Sequential interdependence occurs when one unit in the overall process produces an output necessary for the performance by the next unit. Perhaps the most obvious example of sequential interdependence is an assembly line. According to the Proven Models website, "The demand for coordination to prevent slowdown is greater than for pooled task interdependence." Scheduling and planning your organization's resources in a sequential interdependence model is essential to efficient operations.

 

3. Reciprocal Interdependence: Reciprocal interdependence is similar to sequential interdependence in that the output of one department becomes the input of another, with the addition of being cyclical. In this model, an organization's departments are at their highest intensity of interaction. Reciprocal models are the most complex and difficult to manage--the Business Intelligence website notes that "one unit can change the rules and affect everyone else at any time."

Question 26
Feeling arising out of inadequate definition of roles is known as (UGC NET Management Dec 2009)
  • A.Role ambiguity
  • B.Role conflict
  • C.Role perception
  • D.Role expectation
Correct Answer: Role ambiguity

The sensation that emerges due to an insufficiently defined or unclear set of responsibilities and expectations associated with a role is termed as role ambiguity. It signifies the lack of clarity or understanding regarding one's duties, leading to confusion about what is expected in a particular position within an organization.

Question 27
An informal group encompassing individuals from different levels within a given area or department, is known as: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2014)
  • A.Horizontal clique
  • B.Vertical clique
  • C.In-group
  • D.Out-group
Correct Answer: Vertical clique

An informal group that includes individuals from various hierarchical levels within a specific area or department is termed a Vertical Clique. These groups bring together individuals from different ranks or positions within the same department, fostering informal connections that transcend hierarchical boundaries. This form of clique allows for interaction and collaboration between members across various organizational levels, promoting camaraderie and collaboration within a shared unit or area.

Question 28
Match List-I wish List-II[UGC NET Management June 2019]List-I(a) Gate Keeper(b) Supporter(c) Consensus Tester(d) HarmonizerList-II(i) Encourages silent or shy members to contribute to the discussion(ii) Explores with the group if all group members agree with the decision(iii)Reduces tension in the group, reconciles differences and explores opportunities(iv) Invites all group members one by one to speak and encourages people to participateChoose the correct option from those given below:
  • A.(a)-(ii);(b)-(i);(c)-(iv);(d)-(iii)
  • B.(a)-(ii); (b)-(iv); (c)-(i); (d)-(iii)
  • C.(a)-(iv); (b)-(i), (c)-(iii); (d)-(ii)
  • D.(a)-(iv);(b)-(i), (c)-(ii); (d)-(iii)
Correct Answer: (a)-(iv);(b)-(i), (c)-(ii); (d)-(iii)

The correct match between the roles and their corresponding behaviors is as follows:

 

(a) Gate Keeper - (iv) Invites all group members one by one to speak and encourages people to participate

(b) Supporter - (i) Encourages silent or shy members to contribute to the discussion

(c) Consensus Tester - (ii) Explores with the group if all group members agree with the decision

(d) Harmonizer - (iii) Reduces tension in the group, reconciles differences, and explores opportunities

 

Task roles are instrumental in the group's task completion or achieving its goals. These roles typically fall into leadership, informational, or procedural functions. There are various roles associated with task-related behaviors:

 

(i) Task Leader - Typically found within any group, this individual holds high group status due to their experience, knowledge, problem-solving abilities, and leadership skills. Their primary function is guiding the group towards task completion.

 

(ii) Expediter - Functions to keep the group focused on task completion by managing the agenda, setting and assessing goals, and monitoring the group’s progress.

 

(iii) Information Provider - Involves behaviors where all group members contribute new ideas, initiate discussions, and share relevant knowledge and experiences.

 

(iv) Information Seeker - Seeks further information, elaboration, or clarification on relevant items related to the group’s task, including factual information or group member opinions.

 

(v) Gatekeeper - Manages conversation flow to ensure all group members participate meaningfully, achieving a balanced participation.

 

(vi) Recorder - Takes notes during group discussions and activities. Typically limited to one person as multiple recorders may not be necessary or beneficial.

 

Maintenance roles, on the other hand, focus on creating social cohesion and meeting interpersonal needs within the group. These roles require strong interpersonal skills and include the following behaviors:

 

(i) Social-Emotional Leader - Often well-liked within the group, performs various maintenance roles, complementing the task leader without competing. They also provide reassurance and support to the task leader when required.

 

(ii) Supporter - Engages in communication behaviors that encourage group members and provides emotional support, often through more intimate one-on-one exchanges.

 

(iii) Tension Releaser - Uses humor and sensitivity to manage the group’s frustration levels in different situations.

 

(iv) Harmonizer - Manages various types of group conflicts that arise during group communication, intervening before they escalate.

 

(v) Interpreter - Mediates intercultural conflicts, finds common ground between different people, and fosters a climate where diversity is seen as an opportunity.

 

(vi) Consensus Tester - Ensures unanimity among group members, confirming agreement with group decisions.

Question 29
Arrange the team member’s behaviour in the group building process in the proper sequence.1. Lot of competition and hostilities2. Upset and depressed3. Eager, anxious, gather impressions and data about the similarities and differences among members4. Interdependence in personal relations5. Less dissatisfied and a feeling of belongingness to the groupChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.2, 3, 1, 4, 5
  • B.1, 2, 4, 3, 5
  • C.3, 1, 4, 2, 5
  • D.3, 1, 5, 4, 2
Correct Answer: 3, 1, 5, 4, 2

The sequence of team member behaviors aligns with the stages of group development proposed by psychologist Bruce Tuckman in 1965. These stages—forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning—highlight the various behavioral patterns exhibited during the team-building process.

 

1. The forming stage initiates with individuals feeling eager, anxious, and engaged in gathering information about similarities and differences among team members. There's a sense of uncertainty and a search for leadership.

 

2. As the group progresses into the storming stage, competition and hostilities become more prevalent. Personalities clash, resulting in conflicts, and some members may feel upset and depressed. Productivity may decrease as energy is diverted to these confrontations.

 

3. The norming stage witnesses a shift towards resolution as consensus develops around leaders and individual roles. Interpersonal differences start to get resolved, leading to a sense of cooperation and unity within the team.

 

4. The performing stage showcases a mature and organized team, demonstrating high commitment to the shared mission. While conflicts may arise, they are managed constructively, fostering a well-functioning environment.

 

5. Finally, in the adjourning stage, team members, acknowledging the temporary nature of the group, might experience a sense of loss or dissatisfaction as the team is disbanded or completes its purpose. This phase is often associated with reflections on the shared journey and accomplishments made by the team.

Question 30
Select the four stages of group development from the following: (UGC NET Commerce Sep 2013)1. Forming2. Storming3. Discussing4. Norming5. Warning6. Performing
  • A.1, 2, 3 and 5
  • B.2, 3, 4 and 6
  • C.3, 4, 5 and 6
  • D.1, 2, 4 and 6
Correct Answer: 1, 2, 4 and 6

The four stages of Group Development are Forming, Storming, Norming and Performing.

 

Psychologist Bruce Tuckman first came up with the memorable phrase "forming, storming, norming, and performing" back in 1965. He used it to describe the path to high-performance that most teams follow. Later, he added a fifth stage that he called "adjourning" (and others often call "mourning" – it rhymes better!)

 

1. Forming - Stage 1: High dependence on leader for guidance and direction. Little agreement on team aims other than received from leader. Individual roles and responsibilities are unclear. Leader must be prepared to answer lots of questions about the team's purpose, objectives and external relationships. Processes are often ignored. Members test tolerance of system and leader. Leader directs (similar to Situational Leadership 'Telling' mode).

 

2. Storming - Stage 2: Decisions don't come easily within group. Team members vie for position as they attempt to establish themselves in relation to other team members and the leader, who might receive challenges from team members. Clarity of purpose increases but plenty of uncertainties persist. Cliques and factions form and there may be power struggles. The team needs to be focused on its goals to avoid becoming distracted by relationships and emotional issues. Compromises may be required to enable progress. Leader coaches (similar to Situational Leadership 'Selling' mode).

 

3. Norming - Stage 3: Agreement and consensus largely forms among team, who respond well to facilitation by leader. Roles and responsibilities are clear and accepted. Big decisions are made by group agreement. Smaller decisions may be delegated to individuals or small teams within group. Commitment and unity is strong. The team may engage in fun and social activities. The team discusses and develops its processes and working style. There is general respect for the leader and some of leadership is more shared by the team. Leader facilitates and enables (similar to the Situational Leadership 'Participating' mode).

 

4. Performing - Stage 4: The team is more strategically aware; the team knows clearly why it is doing what it is doing. The team has a shared vision and is able to stand on its own feet with no interference or participation from the leader. There is a focus on over-achieving goals, and the team makes most of the decisions against criteria agreed with the leader. The team has a high degree of autonomy. Disagreements occur but now they are resolved within the team positively and necessary changes to processes and structure are made by the team. The team is able to work towards achieving the goal, and also to attend to relationship, style and process issues along the way. Team members look after each other. The team requires delegated tasks and projects from the leader. The team does not need to be instructed or assisted. Team members might ask for assistance from the leader with personal and interpersonal development. Leader delegates and oversees (similar to the Situational Leadership 'Delegating' mode).

Question 31
Which of the following approaches of team building is based on the belief that each person possesses positive and negative characteristics that must be owned up to a permitted expression? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2015)
  • A.Process approach
  • B.Gestalt approach
  • C.Role analysis approach
  • D.Parallel learning structure approach
Correct Answer: Gestalt approach

The Gestalt Approach to Team Building is centered on the belief that each individual possesses both positive and negative traits that should be acknowledged and expressed. This approach prioritizes the individual over the group, viewing individuals as complete organisms with inherent characteristics that need acceptance and permissible expression. The core of this approach lies in fostering self-awareness, authenticity, and responsibility among individuals. It encourages individuals to live in the present moment, accept their actions, and avoid hindering their awareness or authenticity due to dysfunctional behaviors. Gestalt therapy emphasizes personal growth, aiming to make individuals stronger, more genuine, and in tune with their emotions, ultimately contributing to building stronger teams. Expressing both positive and negative feelings openly and resolving interactions rather than suppressing emotions is crucial in this approach. While the Gestalt OD practitioner often works within group settings, the focus remains primarily on individual development.

 

Other approaches, such as Parallel Learning Structures, focus on enhancing employee effectiveness through informal peer communication and the sharing of daily experiences. Formalizing this process ensures all employees, irrespective of hierarchical positions, contribute ideas to the organization. On the other hand, the Role Analysis Technique (RAT) aims to clarify the expectations and obligations of team members within specialized roles, addressing role ambiguity or confusion within new or established teams.

Question 32
Which of the following factors lead to group cohesiveness? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2015)(a) agreement on group goals(b) high intra-group competition(c) frequent interaction of members(d) personal attractiveness
  • A.(a) and (b)
  • B.(a), (b) and (c)
  • C.(a), (c) and (d)
  • D.(a), (b) and (d)
Correct Answer: (a), (c) and (d)

Factors contributing to group cohesiveness include:

a. Agreement on group goals

b. Frequent interaction among members

c. Personal attractiveness

 

Cohesiveness, the attraction and motivation for group members to remain part of the group, is influenced by various factors:

Status of the Group: High-status groups often command more loyalty from their members. Individuals tend to conform to such groups' norms, reinforcing the group's strength and status.

 

Size of the Group: Smaller groups tend to foster stronger bonds as constant face-to-face interactions are easier to maintain within a smaller circle.

 

Nature of the Group: Homogeneous groups, where members share similar backgrounds or interests, tend to be more effective in tasks requiring cooperation.

 

Communication: Groups with frequent and easy interaction among members develop stronger cohesiveness. Proximity facilitates the development of unique communication methods and strengthens bonds.

 

Location of the Group: Isolation from other groups can increase cohesiveness. Close proximity and isolation from other groups often foster stronger bonds among members.

 

Autonomy: Groups with interdependent tasks tend to have higher cohesiveness compared to groups with more independent activities among members.

 

Leadership Style: Different leadership styles impact group cohesiveness differently. Effective leadership can foster closer relationships among group members by addressing their social needs.

 

Management Behavior: Management practices like fostering competition or rewarding cooperation significantly influence the degree of closeness within a group.

 

Outside Pressure: Groups often provide security against external pressures. Common threats or pressures from outside sources can strengthen group bonds, but excessive external pressure might hinder the formation of cohesiveness within the group.

Question 33
Which of the following is a deterioration of mental efficiency, reality testing and moral judgment that results from in-group pressure? (UGC NET Commerce Jul 2016)
  • A.Harassment
  • B.Group think
  • C.Group burnout
  • D.Group control
Correct Answer: Group think

Groupthink represents the decline in mental efficiency, reality testing, and moral judgment due to intense in-group pressure. It occurs when a group unanimously agrees on a course of action despite evidence suggesting an alternative. Irving Janis, a social psychologist, coined this term to understand how groups sometimes make excellent decisions and other times make disastrous ones.

 

In a groupthink scenario, there's a strong emphasis on unanimous agreement within the group, often leading to the neglect of better alternatives. Members tend to suppress dissenting opinions or new ideas, resulting in flawed decision-making and unmet objectives. This phenomenon arises from a strong sense of group cohesion, where individuals prioritize harmony within the group over individual critical thinking.

Question 34
‘No ideas are ever criticized’ and ‘the more radical the ideas are the better’ – are the rules of which decision-making process? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)
  • A.Programmed decision-making
  • B.Non-programmed decision making
  • C.Brainstorming
  • D.Group discussion
Correct Answer: Brainstorming

The question refers to the concept of Brainstorming.

 

Brainstorming is a group creativity technique by which efforts are made to find a conclusion for a specific problem by gathering a list of ideas spontaneously contributed by its members. In other words, brainstorming is a situation where a group of people meet to generate new ideas and solutions around a specific domain of interest by removing inhibitions. People are able to think more freely and they suggest many spontaneous new ideas as possible. All the ideas are noted down and those ideas are not criticized and after brainstorming session the ideas are evaluated. The term was popularized by Alex Faickney Osborn in the 1953 book Applied Imagination.

Question 35
The group formation theory explaining affiliation based on spatial proximity is called ___(UGC NET Management Jul 2016)
  • A.Homan’s theory
  • B.Propinquity theory
  • C.Balance theory
  • D.Exchange theory
Correct Answer: Propinquity theory

The theory explaining affiliation based on spatial proximity is known as the Propinquity Theory.

 

Various theories describe group formation:

 

1. Propinquity Theory: This theory highlights that individuals tend to affiliate based on spatial or geographical proximity. Employees sharing a workplace area or managers with offices close to each other are more likely to form groups due to their physical proximity.

 

2. Homan’s Theory: George C. Homans proposed a theory stating that the more activities individuals share, the stronger their interactions and shared sentiments become. Sentiments foster more shared activities and interactions. This theory encompasses activities, interactions, and sentiments, all interconnected.

 

3. Balance Theory: Theodore Newcomb's theory suggests that individuals are attracted to each other based on similar attitudes towards common goals. Relationships strive to maintain a symmetrical balance between attraction and common attitudes. Imbalances prompt efforts to restore equilibrium, but if balance cannot be regained, relationships dissolve.

 

4. Exchange Theory: This theory revolves around the outcomes of interactions in terms of rewards and costs. Individuals gauge what they'll gain from interactions with group members. An attraction to a group hinges on a minimum positive outcome (rewards surpassing costs). Interactions offer rewards that fulfill needs but also incur costs such as anxiety or frustration. Propinquity, interaction, and shared attitudes play roles in this theory.

Question 1
Arrange the following group task performance according to the ascending stages of group development: (UGC NET Management Jun 2020)a. Clarify all misunderstandingsb. Termination of taskc. Highly productived. work output is low, focus on defining the goals and taskse. Issues are resolved, group norm developChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b, e, c, b
  • B.d, a, c, e, b
  • C.d, a, e, c, b
  • D.d, a, e, b, c
Correct Answer: d, a, e, c, b

The stages of group development concerning task performance are delineated as follows:

 

1. Work output is low, focus on defining the goals and tasks: This phase marks the initial stage where productivity might be minimal as the group concentrates on delineating objectives and tasks.

 

2. Clarify all misunderstandings: Group members work through misunderstandings and uncertainties that arise during task initiation.

 

3. Issues are resolved, group norms develop: The group addresses underlying issues and establishes norms that guide their functioning, promoting better collaboration.

 

4. Highly productive: As the group dynamics settle, productivity surges with efficient collaboration and task engagement.

 

5. Termination of task: This final stage occurs when the task is successfully completed, leading to the disbandment of the group.

 

Group development signifies the process of forming an association to achieve common goals. This journey typically includes the forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning stages.

 

1. Forming Stage (Orientation): Group members experience initial uncertainty, learning the group's operation, expectations, and norms.

 

2. Storming Stage (Power Struggle): Conflicts and competition emerge as group members gain familiarity with the work and their roles within the group.

 

3. Norming Stage (Cooperation and Integration): The group becomes more cooperative, enjoyable, and productive, resolving disputes effectively and maintaining focus.

 

4. Performing Stage (Synergy): Morale remains high, fostering a sense of belonging and concentration on shared objectives, leveraging individual skills.

 

5. Adjourning Stage (Closure): Occurring when the task concludes, this phase involves the disbandment of the group, leading members in different directions.

Question 2
Which of the following comprises people with complementary skills committed to a common purpose, common performance goals and an approach to which they hold themselves mutually accountable? (UGC NET Management Jun 2020)
  • A.Group
  • B.Team
  • C.Organisation
  • D.Firm
Correct Answer: Team

A team constitutes individuals possessing complementary skills, dedicated to a shared purpose and performance objectives. They align themselves with an accountable approach, holding mutual responsibility for their collective goals. The fundamental essence of a team lies in this unified commitment.

Question 3
The right sequence in respect of stages of group development is:(UGC NET Management Dec 2019)
  • A.Forming, storming, norming, performing, adjourning
  • B.Storming, forming, norming, adjourning, performing
  • C.Norming, performing, storming, forming, adjourning
  • D.Storming, forming, norming, performing, adjourning
Correct Answer: Forming, storming, norming, performing, adjourning

The sequential stages of group development, as per the proposed model by psychologist Bruce Tuckman, follow the path of "forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning." This model outlines the phases through which teams typically progress on their journey to high-performance.

 

1. Forming: This initial stage involves a high dependency on a leader for guidance, unclear team objectives beyond those set by the leader, and undefined roles and responsibilities among members.

 

2. Storming: The subsequent stage witnesses decision-making challenges within the group, as members strive to establish their positions and may challenge the leader. Power struggles, uncertainties, and the emergence of cliques or factions might occur.

 

3. Norming: At this phase, the team strives towards consensus and agreement. Roles become clearer, major decisions are made through group agreement, and smaller decisions may be delegated. Commitment and unity strengthen, and the team may engage in social activities.

 

4. Performing: In this stage, the team gains strategic awareness, possesses a shared vision, and operates independently without much interference from the leader. The focus shifts to surpassing goals, with the team making most decisions based on agreed-upon criteria.

 

5. Adjourning: The final stage acknowledges the completion of the task, where the team disbands. Often called the "adjourning" or "mourning" phase, team members may experience a sense of loss as they move on to other endeavors.

Question 4
Arrange the following characteristics of stages of group development in the increasing order: (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2021)1. Members begin to resolve differences and clarify the purpose of the group and the roles of group member.2. It includes recognition for participation and achievement.3. Members are highly task-oriented and there is unity in the group.4. Conflicts start arising due to the differences of opinion among members.5. Members are moderately eager, have positive expectations, anxious about why they are there, and who other members areChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.5, 4, 1, 2, 3
  • B.4, 5, 3, 1, 2
  • C.5, 4, 1, 3, 2
  • D.4, 2, 1, 5, 3
Correct Answer: 5, 4, 1, 3, 2

Option C is the correct answer.

 

The increasing order of characteristics corresponding to the stages of group development, as described by psychologist Bruce Tuckman, progresses as follows:

 

1. Members are moderately eager, have positive expectations, are anxious about their roles and the identities of other members - this signifies the initial phase of forming, where uncertainty is high and individuals seek direction and leadership.

 

2. Conflicts start arising due to differences of opinion among members - this marks the storming stage, characterized by the emergence of individual personalities, conflict, and competition.

 

3. Members begin to resolve differences and clarify the purpose of the group and the roles of group members - this indicates the norming stage, where consensus around leadership, roles, and goals begins to form, resolving interpersonal differences.

 

4. It includes recognition for participation and achievement - this reflects the performing stage, where the team is mature, well-organized, and committed to its mission, dealing constructively with conflicts.

 

5. Members are highly task-oriented, and there is unity in the group - this describes the final stage, adjourning, acknowledging the completion of the task and the potential feelings of loss as the group disbands.

 

Therefore, the correct order of these characteristics in terms of increasing progression within group development is 5, 4, 1, 3, 2, corresponding to stages of group forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning, respectively. Hence, option C is the correct sequence.

Question 5
Beliefs, attitudes, traditions and expectations which are shared by group members is called: (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2020)
  • A.Group norms
  • B.Group communication
  • C.Group cohesiveness
  • D.Group structure
Correct Answer: Group norms

Group norms encapsulate the shared beliefs, attitudes, traditions, and expectations among members within a group. These norms are essentially the behavioral standards set and adhered to by group members. Michael Argyle succinctly defines group norms as "rules or guidelines of accepted behavior established by a group to monitor the behavior of its members."

 

These norms serve the purpose of aligning the group towards its objectives and can encompass both social and equitable principles. They play a crucial role in delineating the boundaries between what is deemed acceptable and what isn't within the group's context. Additionally, norms foster a sense of identification and belonging among the members to the collective entity.

Question 6
Match the following.List I (Theory of Group Formation)a. Propinquity theoryb. Balance theoryc. Exchange theoryd. GeorgeHomans' theoryList II (Characteristics)i. Activities interactions and sentimentsii. Similar attitudes towards commonly relevant objects and goalsiii. Reward-cost outcomes of interactioniv. Spatial or geographical proximityChoose the correct answer from the options given below: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2021)
  • A.a-i, b-ii, c-iii, d-iv
  • B.a-ii, b-iv, c-i, d-iii
  • C.a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii
  • D.a-iv, b-ii, c-iii, d-i
Correct Answer: a-iv, b-ii, c-iii, d-i

Option D is the correct answer.

 

Theory of Group Formation encompasses various theories explaining how and why individuals form groups. The four significant theories are:

 

1. Propinquity Theory: This theory, proposed by Leon Festinger, Stanley Schacher, and Curt Back, focuses on spatial or geographical proximity as a basis for affiliation. It suggests that individuals are more likely to form groups if they share physical proximity, such as working in the same area of an office or plant.

 

2. George Homans' Theory: George C. Homans' theory emphasizes that the more activities individuals share, the stronger their interactions and shared sentiments become. It suggests that activities, interactions, and sentiments are interconnected, influencing each other within group dynamics.

 

3. Balance Theory: Theodore Newcomb's Balance Theory emphasizes attraction based on similar attitudes toward common goals and objects. It asserts that relationships aim to maintain symmetrical balance between mutual attraction and shared attitudes. Any imbalance prompts efforts to restore equilibrium, and unresolved imbalances may lead to relationship dissolution.

 

4. Exchange Theory: Proposed by Thaibaunt and Kelly, the Exchange Theory revolves around the concept of reward-cost outcomes in interactions. It posits that individuals are attracted to groups based on the perceived benefits of interaction. A positive outcome (rewards exceeding costs) is necessary for affiliation, where rewards fulfill needs while costs incur negative emotions like anxiety or fatigue. Propinquity, interaction, and shared attitudes play roles in this theory.

 

Correctly matching these theories with their characteristics yields:

Propinquity theory - iv. Spatial or geographical proximity

Balance theory - ii. Similar attitudes towards commonly relevant objects and goals

Exchange theory - iii. Reward-cost outcomes of interaction

George Homans' theory - i. Activities interactions and sentiments
