Group activities within an enterprise offer several advantages aligned with organizational functions. The advantages are as follows:

 

(1) Logical reflection of functions: Group activities enable a logical and coordinated approach towards fulfilling various functions within an organization. Groups can structure their activities to align with the specific objectives and functions of the enterprise, promoting logical workflow and task execution.

This can help maintain authority and enhance the prestige associated with these critical functions.

This specialization within groups contributes to increased efficiency and effectiveness in handling specific functions.

Question 8
Edgar Schein has identified different dimensions of organizational roles, one of which is a social dimension. Which one of the following terms is associated with the social dimension? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)

  • B.Functional
  • C.Hierarchical

Edgar Schein describes three dimensions of organizational roles. These are:

1. Inclusionary – a social dimension (e.g., outsider, probationary status, permanent status)

2. Functional – a task dimension (e.g., sales, engineering, plant operations)

3. Hierarchical – a rank dimension (e.g., line employee, supervisor, middle manager, officer)

Question 10
Given below are different stages of group formation:(a) Storming(b) Norming(c) Adjourning(d) Forming(e) PerformingChoose the right option which gives the correct sequence of the steps starting from the beginning: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.(a), (d), (e), (b), (c)
  • B.(d), (a), (b), (e), (c)
  • C.(a), (b) (e), (d), (c)
  • D.(e), (d), (b), (a), (c)
Correct Answer: (d), (a), (b), (e), (c)

The explanation details the stages of group formation, aligning with Bruce Tuckman's renowned model: forming, storming, norming, performing, and adjourning. It effectively describes each stage, offering insights into the behaviors and dynamics typical at each phase.

 

To summarize:

 

Forming (Stage 1): Characterized by high dependence on the leader, unclear roles, and an orientation phase where the team tests the leader and the system.

Question 12
A group consisting of members working together to attain a specific objective with which each is concerned, is known as: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2019)
  • A.informal group
  • B.task group
  • C.friendship group
  • D.interest group
Correct Answer: interest group

An interest group comprises members working collaboratively toward a particular objective, individually motivated by this shared aim. These groups are structured to accomplish specific goals that are of significance to each participant involved. For instance, when employees unite to pressurize management for subsidized transport, they form an interest group. This type of group operates based on shared concerns and objectives, differing from formal groups established by an organization for specific tasks, or from informal groups created by members themselves, outside the organization's structured framework.

Question 13
Related to group, when the tendency for individuals to expend less effort when working collectively than when working individually is called: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)
  • A.Group conflict
  • B.Social loafing
  • C.Group cohesiveness
  • D.Group think
Correct Answer: Social loafing

Social loafing refers to the phenomenon where individuals tend to exert less effort when working collectively within a group compared to when working alone. This behavior often leads to decreased productivity or effort from individuals when they are part of a team effort, as opposed to working independently. This tendency can undermine the overall group performance and output, impacting the achievement of collective goals. It's important to address and mitigate social loafing to ensure optimal group performance.

Question 14
Which of the following is not an organizational level intervention? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)
  • A.Appreciative Inquiry
  • B.Parallel Learning Structure
  • C.Transformational Leadership
  • D.Team Building
Correct Answer: Team Building

While interventions like team building are pivotal for enhancing team dynamics and performance, they're usually categorized as interventions aimed at enhancing group or team-level dynamics rather than addressing the broader organizational scope. Interventions targeting groups focus on ameliorating the performance and functionality of a specific team or a subset within the organization. Conversely, organizational-level interventions are geared towards enhancing the overall functioning and efficacy of the entire organization.

 

Appreciative Inquiry, Parallel Learning Structure, and Transformational Leadership are examples of interventions designed to function at the organizational level, aiming to enhance overall organizational performance. Appreciative Inquiry involves recognizing an organization's strengths and leveraging them for positive change. Parallel Learning Structure involves establishing cross-functional teams to drive innovation and strategy implementation. Transformational Leadership centers on inspiring and motivating employees toward shared organizational goals through visionary and impactful leadership.

Question 15
Which of the following represent the extent to which groupmemberssupport and validate one another while at work? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)
  • A.Group Collaboration
  • B.Group Functioning
  • C.Group Cohesion
  • D.Citizenship Behaviour
Correct Answer: Group Cohesion

Group cohesion refers to the level of unity and commitment among members of a group in achieving shared objectives. It signifies the strength of interpersonal connections within a group and significantly influences its effectiveness.

 

Elevated levels of group cohesion offer several advantages, including heightened member satisfaction, increased productivity, better communication, enhanced decision-making, and improved conflict resolution capabilities. Cohesive groups tend to withstand challenges and setbacks more effectively.

 

Several factors influence group cohesion:

a) Shared goals: When group members share common objectives and values, it positively impacts cohesion, fostering effective collaboration toward those objectives.

b) Interpersonal relationships: The quality of relationships among group members affects cohesion. Positive relationships built on trust and respect contribute to a sense of unity.

c) Group size: Smaller groups often exhibit higher cohesion as members tend to interact more, fostering stronger relationships.

d) Group identity: Strong identification and a sense of belonging within the group contribute to cohesion. Members who strongly identify with the group are more inclined to support and collaborate effectively.

Question 16
Group Norms help in:a. Establishing distinctive identity of group.b. Non-predictable behaviour of group members.c. Avoiding embarrassing interpersonal problems.d. Expressing cultural values or goals of group.Choose the correct answer from the options given below: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)

  • B.c and d Only
  • C.a, b and d Only
  • D.a, c and d Only

(i) Establishing a distinctive identity of the group: Norms contribute to forging a unique identity for the group, crucial in nurturing a sense of unity and belonging among members.

 

(ii) Avoiding embarrassing interpersonal problems: These norms set clear behavioral expectations, which in turn help in preventing uncomfortable or embarrassing interpersonal issues within the group.

 

(iii) Expressing cultural values or goals of the group: Group norms serve as a platform for expressing the cultural values or aspirations of the group, thereby enhancing a positive group identity and a sense of collective purpose.

Question 17
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)Statement I:“Social Loafing” is a dysfunction due to pressure to conform and reach consensus in highly cohesive groups and teams.Statement II:“Groupthink” occurs when members reduce their effort and performance levels while acting in a group.In the light of the above statements, choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II is true.
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II is false.
  • C.Statement I is true but Statement II is false.
  • D.Statement I is false but Statement II is true.
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II is false.

Both Statement I and Statement II are false.

 

Statement I is incorrect because "Social Loafing" refers to the phenomenon where individuals exert less effort in a group setting than they would if they were working alone. It is not related to pressure to conform or reach consensus in highly cohesive groups and teams.

 

Statement II is also incorrect because "Groupthink" refers to the tendency of a group to make irrational or dysfunctional decisions because of pressures to maintain a consensus and avoid conflict. It is not related to members reducing their effort and performance levels while acting in a group.

Question 20
Read the following passage and answer the questions given at the end by picking up the appropriate answer from the given alternatives.In principle, a cohesive group-one whose members generally agree with one another and support one another’s judgements-can do a much better job at decision-making than it could if it were non-cohesive. When cohesiveness is low or lacking entirely, compliance out of fear of recrimination is likely to be strongest. To overcome this fear, participants in the group’s deliberations need to be confident that they are members in good standing and that the others will continue to value their role in the group, whether or not they agree about a particular issue under discussion. As a member of a group feel more accepted by the others, they acquire greater freedom to say what they really think, becoming less likely to use deceitful arguments or to play it safe by dancing around issues with conventional comments. Typically,then, the more cohesive a group becomes, the less its members will deliberately censor what they say out of fear of being punished socially for antagonizing their fellow members. But group cohesiveness can have pitfalls as well. While the members of a highly cohesive group can feel much free to deviate from the majority, their desire for genuine concurrence on every important issue often inclines them not to use this freedom. In a highly cohesive group of decision makers, the danger is not that individuals will conceal objections they harbour regarding a proposal favoured by the majority, but that they think the proposal is a good one without attempting to carry out a critical scrutiny that could reveal grounds for strong objections. Members may then decide that any misgivings they feel are not worth pursuing- that the benefit of any doubt should be given to the group consensus. In this way, they may fall victim to a syndrome known as ‘groupthink’. Collective decision making has been defined as “a deterioration of mental efficiency, reality testing and moral judgement that results from in-group pressures”. Based on analyses of major fiascos of international diplomacy and military decision making, researchers have identified groupthink behaviour as a recurring pattern that involves several factors; overestimation of the groups power and morality, manifested, for example, in an illusion of invulnerability, which creates excessive optimism; close- mindedness to warnings of problems and to alternative view points; and unwarranted pressures toward uniformity, including self-censorship with respect to doubts about the group’s reasoning and a concomitant shared illusion of unanimity concerning group decisions. Cohesiveness of the decision making group is an essential antecedent condition of this syndrome but not a sufficient one. So it is important to work toward identifying the additional factors that determine whether group cohesiveness will deteriorate into groupthink or allow for effective decision making.Why the author does think that the cohesive group can do a much better job at decision making than it could if it were non-cohesive? (UGC NET HRM Nov 2017)(a) The members of a highly cohesive group can feel much free to deviate from the majority(b) Individuals will not conceal objection they harbour regarding a proposal favoured by the majority.(c) Participants in the group’s deliberations are confident that they are members in good standing and that the others will continue to value their role in the group, whether or not they agree about a particular issue under discussion.Select the correct answer using the codes given below:
  • A.only (a)
  • B.only (b)
  • C.both (a) and (c)
  • D.(a), (b) and (c)
Correct Answer: (a), (b) and (c)

The author believes that a cohesive group can perform better at decision-making compared to a non-cohesive one due to several reasons:

(a) Members in a highly cohesive group have the freedom to deviate from the majority when necessary.

(b) Individuals in this cohesive setting won't conceal objections they hold regarding a favored proposal by the majority.

(c) Participants in the group feel confident about their standing within the group, knowing their role is valued regardless of their stance on a particular issue.

 

So, the correct answer is (D), as all three reasons contribute to why a cohesive group is believed to excel in decision-making compared to a non-cohesive one.

Question 21
Nominal group technique is (UGC NET Management Dec 2011)
  • A.aconsensus planning tool, generally used by groups to discuss, debate and decide on issues of strength identification, problems, and solutions.
  • B.a consensus planning tool to arrive at decisions on issues, for instance man-power requirement, by involving group of experts through blind rounds of communication
  • C.a majority-based decision-making tool
  • D.None of the above
Correct Answer: aconsensus planning tool, generally used by groups to discuss, debate and decide on issues of strength identification, problems, and solutions.

The nominal group technique (NGT) serves as a consensus planning tool used by groups to discuss, debate, and reach decisions on issues related to identifying strengths, problems, and potential solutions. It involves a structured process where group members contribute their opinions and solutions, followed by eliminating duplicates and ranking the proposed solutions collectively. This method ensures inclusive decision-making by considering everyone's input rather than relying solely on the majority vote, making it suitable for groups aiming for quick yet comprehensive decision-making.

Question 22
The three different types of interdependence among groups was primarily suggested bywhom ?(UGC NET Management Aug 2016)
  • A.Likert
  • B.Kurt Lewin
  • C.Thompson
  • D.GordonLippit
Correct Answer: Thompson

James D. Thompson proposed the classification of three types of interdependence among groups in his book "Organizations in Action." Thompson's categorization delineated pooled interdependence, sequential interdependence, and reciprocal interdependence to elucidate the varying degrees of interaction and reliance between organizational units or departments.

Question 23
Read the following passage and answer the questions given at the end by picking up the appropriate answer from the given alternatives.In principle, a cohesive group-one whose members generally agree with one another and support one another’s judgements-can do a much better job at decision-making than it could if it were non-cohesive. When cohesiveness is low or lacking entirely, compliance out of fear of recrimination is likely to be strongest. To overcome this fear, participants in the group’s deliberations need to be confident that they are members in good standing and that the others will continue to value their role in the group, whether or not they agree about a particular issue under discussion. As a member of a group feel more accepted by the others, they acquire greater freedom to say what they really think, becoming less likely to use deceitful arguments or to play it safe by dancing around issues with conventional comments. Typically,then, the more cohesive a group becomes, the less its members will deliberately censor what they say out of fear of being punished socially for antagonizing their fellow members. But group cohesiveness can have pitfalls as well. While the members of a highly cohesive group can feel much free to deviate from the majority, their desire for genuine concurrence on every important issue often inclines them not to use this freedom. In a highly cohesive group of decision makers, the danger is not that individuals will conceal objections they harbour regarding a proposal favoured by the majority, but that they think the proposal is a good one without attempting to carry out a critical scrutiny that could reveal grounds for strong objections. Members may then decide that any misgivings they feel are not worth pursuing- that the benefit of any doubt should be given to the group consensus. In this way, they may fall victim to a syndrome known as ‘groupthink’. Collective decision making has been defined as “a deterioration of mental efficiency, reality testing and moral judgement that results from in-group pressures”. Based on analyses of major fiascos of international diplomacy and military decision making, researchers have identified groupthink behaviour as a recurring pattern that involves several factors; overestimation of the groups power and morality, manifested, for example, in an illusion of invulnerability, which creates excessive optimism; close- mindedness to warnings of problems and to alternative view points; and unwarranted pressures toward uniformity, including self-censorship with respect to doubts about the group’s reasoning and a concomitant shared illusion of unanimity concerning group decisions. Cohesiveness of the decision making group is an essential antecedent condition of this syndrome but not a sufficient one. So, it is important to work toward identifying the additional factors that determine whether group cohesiveness will deteriorate into groupthink or allow for effective decision making.The passage mentions which one of the following as a component of groupthink? (UGC NET HRM Nov 2017)
  • A.Unjustified suspicions among group members regarding an adversary’s intentions
  • B.Group members working under unusually high stress, leading to illusions of invulnerability.
  • C.strongbelief that the group’s decision are right.
  • D.The deliberate use of conventional comments.
Correct Answer: strongbelief that the group’s decision are right.

The passage discusses several components of groupthink, and among the options provided, the one highlighted in the passage is (C) A strong belief that the group’s decisions are right.

 

Groupthink involves a situation where there's an unwarranted certainty among members that the group's decisions are unquestionably correct. This belief can lead to a collective sense of infallibility and a dismissal of doubts or alternative perspectives, contributing to flawed decision-making processes.

Question 24
Consider the following. (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2019)Assertion-A:Brainstorming technique demands generation of a number of alternatives to a problem.Reason-R:Participants generate as many alternatives as possible without evaluating them in brainstorming sessions.In the context of above two statements, which of the following codes is correct?
  • A.Statement A is correct and R is the correct explanation of A
  • B.Both A and R are correct but R is not the right explanation of A
  • C.Statement A is correct but R is incorrect
  • D.Both A and R are correct
Correct Answer: Statement A is correct and R is the correct explanation of A

Statement A is correct: Brainstorming technique does indeed emphasize the generation of numerous alternatives or ideas to address a problem or challenge.

 

Statement R is the correct explanation of Statement A: In brainstorming sessions, the primary goal is to generate as many ideas or alternatives as possible without evaluating or critiquing them initially. The focus is on free-flowing idea generation without judgment or criticism to encourage creativity and a wide array of potential solutions.

 

Therefore, option (A) "Statement A is correct and R is the correct explanation of A" is the accurate assessment of the provided statements.

Question 25
When driven by group cohesion, a decision is taken only to be lamented for later is called: (UGC NET HRM Nov 2017)
  • A.Abilene effect
  • B.Placebo effect
  • C.Hawthorne effect
  • D.Halo effect
Correct Answer: Abilene effect

The Abilene Paradox refers to a situation in which a group makes a collective decision that none of its individual members actually agree with. This paradox occurs when group members conform to what they believe is the group's preference or consensus, even if it contradicts their personal thoughts or desires.

 

The term originated from a story by management expert Jerry B. Harvey, where a family embarks on a trip to Abilene despite each member individually preferring not to go. However, no one speaks up, assuming incorrectly that others wanted to go. The result is a group decision that nobody actually wanted.

 

This paradox highlights the dangers of conformity and the failure to voice dissenting opinions within a group, leading to poor decision-making and often regrettable outcomes.

Horizontal, vertical, and random cliques are examples of informal groups within an organization. These informal groups are formed by members themselves rather than being established by the organization, often serving social or task-related purposes outside the formal organizational structure.

Question 28
The theories that explain the formation of ‘Informal Groups’ are to include which of the following? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2019)(a) Propinquity Theory(b) Similarity(or) Balance Theory(c) Displacement Theory(d)Need for achievement TheoryChoose the correct option from the following options:
  • A.(a) and (d) only
  • B.(a) and (b) only
  • C.(a), (b) and (c) only
  • D.(a), (b), (c) and (d)
Correct Answer: (a) and (b) only

The theories explaining the formation of informal groups cover specific aspects of why and how individuals tend to form such groups. Among these theories:

 

(a) Propinquity Theory: This theory emphasizes that individuals affiliate with one another due to spatial or geographical proximity. It suggests that working in close physical proximity fosters the formation of groups more readily compared to working in distant locations.

 

(b) Similarity (or Balance) Theory: This theory, proposed by Theodore Newcomb, highlights that people are attracted to others based on similar attitudes towards commonly relevant objectives and goals. It focuses on the symmetrical balance in relationships based on shared attitudes.

 

These two theories specifically address the reasons behind the formation of informal groups. The other options mentioned, Displacement Theory and Need for Achievement Theory, while theories within psychology and motivation, do not directly explain the formation of informal groups in the context of organizational dynamics. Therefore, the correct answer is indeed (B) - (a) and (b) only, as these theories are specifically relevant to understanding the formation of informal groups within an organizational setting.

Question 29

Correct Answer: A, D and E only

The Performing stage in the group building process involves various key characteristics that distinguish it from other stages:

Question 2
Arrange the Five Stages of Conflict Process in proper sequence from beginning to end.(UGC NET Management Jun 2024)A. Potential opposition or incompatibilityB. IntentionsC. Cognition and personalizationD. OutcomesE. BehaviourChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, C, E, B, D
  • B.A, C, B, E, D
  • C.A, B, C, D, E
  • D.A, D, E, C, B
Correct Answer: A, C, B, E, D

The Five Stages of the Conflict Process are typically arranged as follows:

 

A. Potential opposition or incompatibility: This is the initial stage where differences arise, leading to the potential for conflict.

 

C. Cognition and personalization: In this stage, individuals become aware of the conflict and begin to perceive and personalize it.

 

B. Intentions: Here, individuals formulate their intentions regarding how they will respond to the conflict.

 

E. Behaviour: This stage involves the actions taken in response to the conflict, such as confrontations or avoidance.

 

D. Outcomes: Finally, this stage assesses the results of the conflict, which can be positive or negative for the parties involved.

 

So, the proper sequence is A, C, B, E, D, which corresponds to option (B).

Question 3
What is the belief among pluralists regarding conflict in organization? (UGC NET Management Jun 2024)
  • A.Conflict is unnecessary and should be avoided at allcost
  • B.Conflict is necessary and should be ignored
  • C.Conflict is necessary but it can be managed and resolved
  • D.Conflict should be eliminated through strict rules
Correct Answer: Conflict is necessary but it can be managed and resolved

The correct answer is (C) Conflict is necessary but it can be managed and resolved

Pluralists believe that conflict is an inevitable and necessary aspect of organizational life. However, they also believe that conflict can be managed and resolved through appropriate strategies, rather than being ignored or eliminated entirely. This perspective views conflict as a natural outcome of diverse interests and opinions within an organization.

Question 4
Which of the following are considered while avoiding conflict? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2023)a. Conflict based on interpersonal relationshipsb. All conflicts are not bad and can be taken positivelyc. Conflict over content and goals of the workd. Conflicts do not support a group's goal and improve its performancee. Conflict over how work gets doneChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a, b and c only
  • B.a, b and e only
  • C.a, c and e only
  • D.b, c and d only
Correct Answer: a, c and e only

To address conflict and understand its implications, it's important to recognize the nature and types of conflict as well as the potential benefits and drawbacks.

 

Let's consider each statement:

a. Conflict based on interpersonal relationships: This type of conflict, often referred to as "relationship conflict," involves personal disagreements and can be detrimental to a group's harmony and productivity. It is usually something to be avoided or carefully managed.

b. All conflicts are not bad and can be taken positively: This acknowledges that some conflicts, particularly "task conflicts" related to content and goals, can be beneficial by fostering discussion, innovation, and improvement.

c. Conflict over content and goals of the work: Task conflicts can be positive when they involve disagreements about the work's objectives and content, as they can lead to better decision-making and problem-solving.

d. Conflicts do not support a group's goal and improve its performance: This is generally false, as some conflicts (particularly task conflicts) can actually support a group's goals and improve performance by encouraging diverse viewpoints and critical thinking.

e. Conflict over how work gets done: Procedural conflicts, which involve disagreements over the methods and processes for completing work, can sometimes be constructive by improving efficiency and clarity in processes.

Considering these points, the correct answer is option (C) i.e., a, c and e only.

Question 5
Which of the following antecedent conditions explain intergroup conflict? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2024)A. Personal differencesB. Competition for resourcesC. Role incompatibilityD. Task independenceE. Jurisdictional ambiguityChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B & C Only
  • B.A, B, D & E only
  • C.A, C & D Only
  • D.B, D & E Only
Correct Answer: B, D & E Only

The correct answer is (D) B, D & E Only.

 

Intergroup conflict arises when groups within an organization experience disagreements or competition. Several antecedent conditions contribute to this:

 

Competition for Resources (B): When groups compete for limited resources such as funding, manpower, or equipment, conflicts can arise due to perceived or actual resource scarcity.

 

Task Interdependence (D): When teams depend on each other to complete tasks, any failure, miscommunication, or differing priorities between groups can lead to conflict. The higher the interdependence, the more potential there is for disagreement.

 

Jurisdictional Ambiguity (E): This occurs when there is confusion about roles, responsibilities, and authority boundaries. Groups may clash over who has control or responsibility over certain tasks or decisions.

 

Other options like personal differences (A) and role incompatibility (C) are more relevant to interpersonal conflicts rather than intergroup conflicts.

Question 6
Arrange the following stages of the conflict process in the proper sequence:(UGC NET Commerce Dec 2024)(A) Outcomes(B) Potential opposition or incompatibility(C) Behavior(D) Cognition and personalization(E) IntentionsSelect the correct answer using the codes given below.
  • A.D, B, E, C, A
  • B.B, D, E, C, A
  • C.A, B, E, D, C
  • D.D, C, B, E, A
Correct Answer: B, D, E, C, A

The conflict process consists of five stages, moving from the initial conditions that cause conflict to its outcomes. The correct sequence is as follows:

1. Potential Opposition or Incompatibility (B): This stage identifies the sources of conflict, such as communication issues, structural factors, or personal differences.

2. Cognition and Personalization (D): At this stage, the conflict is recognized and felt. Individuals become aware of the disagreement, and emotions may start to develop.

3. Intentions (E): This stage involves deciding how to respond to the conflict. It includes different conflict-handling styles such as competing, collaborating, compromising, avoiding, or accommodating.

4. Behavior (C): The conflict becomes visible through actions, whether through arguments, negotiations, or cooperation.

5. Outcomes (A): This is the result of the conflict, which can be either constructive (leading to better decisions) or destructive (causing reduced cooperation and dissatisfaction).

Question 7
Match the LIST-I with LIST-II (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2024)LIST-I (Conflict Handling intentions)A. CompetingB. CollaboratingC. AccommodatingD. CompromisingLIST-II (Description)I. A situation in which each party in aconflict desiresto satisfy fully the concerns of all parties.II. The willingness of one party in a conflict to place the negotiatingpartnersinterest above their own.III. A situation in which each party to a conflict is willing to give up something to resolve the conflict.IV. A desire to satisfy one’s interests regardless of the impact on the other party to the conflict.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A-I, B-IV, C-II, D-III
  • B.A-IV, B-I, C-II, D-III
  • C.A-IV, B-I, C-III, D-II
  • D.A-IV, B-II, C-I, D-III
Correct Answer: A-IV, B-I, C-III, D-II

The correct answer is (C) A-IV, B-I, C-III, D-II.

 

A. Competing — IV. A desire to satisfy one’s interests regardless of the impact on the other party to the conflict.

The competing style is assertive and uncooperative, where a party aims to satisfy their own interests at the expense of the other party. It is a win-lose approach.

 

B. Collaborating — I. A situation in which each party in a conflict desires to satisfy fully the concerns of all parties.

The collaborating style is both assertive and cooperative. It aims for a win-win outcome where both parties' needs are fully addressed.

 

C. Accommodating — III. Each party is willing to give up something to resolve the conflict.

The accommodating style is cooperative but unassertive. Each party is willing to make concessions to find a middle ground and resolve the conflict.

 

D. Compromising — II. The willingness of one party in a conflict to place the negotiating partner’s interest above their own.

The compromising style involves giving up some of one’s own interests in exchange for the other party’s interests, aiming for a balanced, though not ideal, resolution.

Question 8
Rita, a young enthusiastic manager has joined an organization as a project coordinator. The project head counsels her to socialize less with non-management employees; whereas the product head tells her to learn more about market issues. She should socialize more with the non-management employees. Rita is confused, she is facing:(UGC NET Management Dec 2014)
  • A.Inter-role conflict
  • B.Intra-role conflict
  • C.Interdepartmental conflict
  • D.Hierarchical conflict
Correct Answer: Intra-role conflict

Rita is experiencing an "Intra-role conflict." This conflict occurs when conflicting demands are within a single domain or role, such as in her job. The project head advises her to socialize less with non-management employees, while the product head suggests the opposite—encouraging more interaction with non-management employees to learn about market issues. These conflicting directives create a dilemma for Rita within her managerial role.

 

It's important to note that role conflict can manifest in various ways:

  • Intra-sender Role Conflict: This arises when a person is asked to perform a job within specified limits that they're incapable of doing, either due to insufficient resources or time.
  • Inter-sender Role Conflict: Occurs when expectations from one sender conflict with those from one or more other senders.
  • Self-Role Conflict: Arises when a person is asked to do a job that clashes with their own value system or personal beliefs.

 

While Rita's situation might appear to involve hierarchical or interdepartmental conflict initially, the conflict she faces—balancing contradictory advice within her managerial role—is more precisely an example of intra-role conflict.

Question 9
The conflict over content and goals of the work is called: (UGC NET Management Dec 2014)
  • A.Functional conflict
  • B.Process conflict
  • C.Relationship conflict
  • D.Task conflict
Correct Answer: Task conflict

It is task conflict that arises when there's disagreement over the content and goals of the work. This form of conflict revolves around differences in understanding or perspectives regarding the tasks and objectives within a team or group. It's distinct from other types of conflict such as relationship conflict, which is more centered on interpersonal issues among team members. Task conflict can generally be managed by encouraging open communication, respecting differing opinions, and striving for collaboration to find a unified solution.

This phase focuses on the perceptions and emotional involvement of the conflicting parties, as they discern and personalize the conflict. Question 11
The source of conflict where cause for conflict exists in an incipient form, but it need not necessarily lead to actual conflict. This may be described as: (UGC NET HRM Aug 2016)
  • A.Behavioural view of conflict
  • B.Conflict stimulation
  • C.Antecedent conditions
  • D.Inter-group conflict
Correct Answer: Antecedent conditions

The source of conflict that exists in an incipient form, preceding actual conflict, is known as "Antecedent conditions." These conditions lay the groundwork for potential conflict but do not necessarily guarantee the occurrence of conflict itself. Antecedent conditions, also referred to as latent conflict, indicate the presence of factors that might lead to conflict if not addressed or managed effectively. Understanding and addressing these conditions can often prevent or reduce unnecessary conflicts within an organization.

Question 16

Question 17

  • A.Approach - Approach conflict
  • B.Role conflict
  • C.Approach - Avoidance conflict
  • D.Vertical conflict
Correct Answer: Vertical conflict

The type of conflict that is not an individual-level conflict among the options provided is "Vertical conflict" (Option D). Vertical conflict, on the other hand, pertains to conflicts between different levels or hierarchical positions within an organization, rather than within an individual. Question 18

  • A.Referent
  • B.Legitimate
  • C.Coercive
  • D.Reward

The superior used coercive power to sack the employee for going on leave without informing superiors. Coercive power involves the use of threats, punishments, or sanctions to influence or control others' behavior. In this case, the superior used the threat of termination as a consequence of the employee's unauthorized absence, thereby demonstrating coercive power.

Question 19

Question 22
Given below are the various stages of the conflict process:(a) Cognition and personalization(b) Interventions(c) Potential opposition or incompatibility(d) Outcomes(e) BehaviourChoose the right option which gives the correct sequence of the stages starting from the beginning: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.(a), (c), (b), (d), (e)
  • B.(b), (a), (c), (e), (d)
  • C.(b), (c), (e), (a), (d)
  • D.(c), (a), (b), (e,) (d)
Correct Answer: (c), (a), (b), (e,) (d)

The conflict process unfolds in several stages, each contributing to its evolution within an organization. The correct sequence of these stages begins with potential opposition or incompatibility, as conflicting conditions set the stage for further developments. These conditions encompass communication challenges, structural variables, and personal differences.

 

Following this, cognition and personalization come into play, marking the recognition and personal understanding of the conflict by involved parties. This stage involves perceiving the conflict and personalizing its emotional impact, shaping how individuals engage with it.

 

Subsequently, interventions become necessary as the conflict progresses, prompting behavior that is visible and indicative of the conflict's manifestations. Intentions then emerge, guiding the actions of those involved, with varying approaches like competing, collaborating, avoiding, accommodating, or compromising.

 

Finally, the conflict reaches its outcomes stage, where the consequences of the conflict's action-reaction dynamics unfold. These outcomes can be functional, contributing positively to group performance, or dysfunctional, hindering collective success.

 

Functional conflict fosters better decisions, innovation, and self-reflection within the group. Conversely, dysfunctional conflict can erode cohesion, leading to discontent and ultimately group disintegration. Understanding these stages helps manage conflicts effectively within an organization, steering them toward constructive outcomes rather than destructive consequences.

Question 23
From among the following, which one is NOT an avoidance mode of conflict management? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.Resignation
  • B.Appeasement
  • C.Negotiation
  • D.Defusion
Correct Answer: Negotiation

Among the provided options, Negotiation (option C) is not considered an avoidance mode of conflict management.

 

Avoidance modes of conflict resolution primarily involve strategies aimed at evading or temporarily deferring the conflict without directly addressing or resolving its underlying issues. Options A, B, and D - Resignation, Appeasement, and Defusion, respectively - all align with avoidance modes by either conceding to circumstances, seeking temporary solutions, or delaying conflict resolution without actively addressing the conflict's root causes. However, Negotiation involves direct engagement and communication between conflicting parties to reach a mutually acceptable resolution, making it distinct from avoidance strategies.

Question 24
Given below are different models of conflict management.(a) Resignation(b) Confrontation(c) Appeasement(d) Negotiation(e)DefusionFrom among the following, choose the alternative which gives the approach modes of conflict management. (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.(b) and (d)
  • B.(a) and (e)
  • C.(c) and (e)
  • D.(c) and (d)
Correct Answer: (b) and (d)

Udai Pareek formulated a conflict management model based on avoidance-approach styles, hinging on three key factors:

(i) Mode of Conflict Management: This involves two primary approaches - Avoidance and Approach modes.

(ii) Reasonableness of the Out-group: Determining whether the out-group is open to reason or unreasonable.

(iii) Interest in Peace: Assessing whether there's an inclination towards peace or a belligerent stance.

 

Combining these variables yields eight distinct conflict management styles: four falling under avoidance strategies (aimed at postponing or evading conflicts) and four under approach strategies (involving more direct or confrontational conflict resolution).

 

Avoidance Modes: These styles involve evading or delaying conflict:

Resignation: Represents an extreme form of avoidance characterized by a sense of helplessness.

Withdrawal: Involves attempts to distance oneself from the conflict.

Defusion: Aims to stall conflict resolution, buying time for addressing the conflict.

Appeasement: Seeks temporary peace without resolving the underlying conflict, often leading to a deteriorating situation.

 

Approach Modes: These styles entail more direct engagement with conflicts:

Confrontation: Involves aggressive fighting over an issue to secure a solution in favor of one party, often through coercion, with a high risk of failure.

Compromise: Focuses on sharing gains without fully resolving the conflict.

Arbitration: Involves the intervention of a neutral third party to objectively assess the conflict and provide an acceptable solution for both parties.

Negotiation: Seeks a mutually satisfactory solution by jointly confronting the problem and exploring alternative resolutions.

 

In this model, conflicts are framed within the context of in-group ("we") and out-group ("they"). The perception of the out-group’s interest and reasonableness influences the emergence and handling of conflicts. Avoidance styles stem from fear and provoke defensive behaviors, whereas approach styles reflect a positive approach centered on collaborative problem-solving efforts. The selection of a conflict management style depends on how the in-group perceives the out-group's reasonableness, interest in peace, and alignment with their own interests.

Question 25
A situation in which the parties to a conflict, each desire to satisfy fully the concern of all parties is known as: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)
  • A.Collaborating
  • B.Competing
  • C.Compromising
  • D.Accommodating
Correct Answer: Collaborating

Behavioral scientists Kenneth Thomas and Ralph Kilmann, who developed the Thomas-Kilmann Conflict Mode Instrument, have identified 5 styles to responding to conflict—competition, collaboration, compromise, avoidance, and accommodation. No conflict style is inherently right or wrong, but one or more styles could be inappropriate for a given situation and the impact could result in a situation quickly spiraling out of control.

 

1. Competing (Goal: I win, you lose)

People who consistently use a competitive style come across as aggressive, autocratic, confrontational, and intimidating. A competitive style is an attempt to gain power and pressure a change at the other person’s expense. A competitive style of managing conflict can be appropriate when you have to implement an unpopular decision, make a quick decision, the decision is vital in a crisis, or it is important to let others know how important an issue is to you – "standing up for your right." The biggest disadvantage of using this style is that relationships can be harmed beyond repair and may encourage other parties to use covert methods to get their needs met because conflict with these people are reduced to – "if you are not with me, you are against me."

 

2. Accommodating (Goal: I lose, you win)

By accommodating you set aside your own personal needs because you want to please others in order to keep the peace. The emphasis is on preserving the relationship. Smoothing or harmonizing can result in a false solution to a problem and can create feelings in a person that range from anger to pleasure. Accommodators are unassertive and cooperative and may play the role of a martyr, complainer, or saboteur. However, accommodation can be useful when one is wrong or when you want to minimize losses when you are going to lose anyway because it preserves relationships. If you use it all the time it can become competitive – "I am nicer than you are" – and may result in reduced creativity in conflict situations and increased power imbalances.

 

3. Avoiding (Goal: I lose, you lose)

Avoidance is characterized by deliberately ignoring or withdrawing from a conflict rather than facing it. This style may be perceived as not caring about your own issue or the issues of others. People who avoid the situation hope the problem will go away, resolve itself without their involvement, or think that others are ready to take the responsibility. There are situations where avoidance is appropriate such as when you need more time to think of how to respond, time constraints demand a delay, confrontation will hurt a working relationship, or there is little chance of satisfying your needs. However, avoidance can be destructive if the other person perceives that you don’t care enough to engage. By not dealing with the conflict, this style allows the conflict to simmer and heat up unnecessarily, resulting in anger or a negative outburst.

 

4. Compromising (Goal: I win some, you win some)

The compromising style demonstrates that you are willing to sacrifice some of your goals while persuading others to give up part of theirs – give a little, get a little. Compromising maintains the relationship and can take less time than collaboration and resolutions might mean splitting the difference or seeking a middle ground position. The downside to compromising is that it can be an easy way out and reduces new creative options. If you constantly split the difference or “straddle the fence,” game playing can result and the outcome could be less than ideal. 

 

5. Collaborating (Goal: I win, you win)

The collaborative style views conflicts as problems to be solved and finding creative solutions that satisfy all the parties’ concerns. You don’t give up your self interest; you dig into the issue to identify the underlying concerns, test your own assumptions, and understand the views of others. Collaboration takes time and if the relationship among the parties is not important, then it may not be worth the time and energy to create a win-win solution. However, collaboration fosters respect, trust, and builds relationships. To make an environment more collaborative, address the conflict directly and in a way that expresses willingness for all parties to get what they need.

Question 27
According to C. I. Bernard, Zone of Indifference denotes: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2022)
  • A.The limit where actions are clearly unacceptable and will not be carried out.
  • B.The limit where actions are barely unacceptable and have weak chances of being carried out.
  • C.The limit within which individuals will respond willingly to the exercise of authority over them.
  • D.The limit where no directions are given to carry out actions.
Correct Answer: The limit within which individuals will respond willingly to the exercise of authority over them.

Option C is the correct answer.

 

The zone of indifference refers to the range of activities or decisions that employees are willing to accept without feeling any significant impact on their job satisfaction or commitment to the organization. It is the range of activities that employees perceive as being acceptable or neutral in terms of their job duties, and they are not particularly interested or invested in them.

Question 28
Which of the following statements is/are true/false regarding modes of Conflict Management Styles? (UGC NET HRM Jul 2018)a. The avoidance modes of Conflict Management aim at avoiding or postponing conflicts.b. The compromise mode involves coercion and is likely to fail to reach a solution.c. The main objective of the diffusion mode of conflict resolution is to buy time for dealing with a conflict.d.) Withdrawal is a form of approach mode that involves getting away from a conflict situation.
  • A.aand b are true; c and d are false.
  • B.aand d are true; b and c are false.
  • C.aand c are true; b and d are false.
  • D.band d are true; a and c are false.
Correct Answer: aand c are true; b and d are false.

Let's clarify the accuracy of each statement:

 

a. The avoidance modes of Conflict Management aim at avoiding or postponing conflicts.

True: Avoidance modes indeed seek to evade or delay conflict resolution, preferring to postpone dealing with the conflict directly.

 

b. The compromise mode involves coercion and is likely to fail to reach a solution.

False: Compromise doesn't involve coercion; it's a process of mutual concession or sharing gains without fully resolving the conflict. While it may not provide a comprehensive resolution, it's not inherently linked to coercion.

 

c. The main objective of the diffusion mode of conflict resolution is to buy time for dealing with a conflict.

True: The diffusion mode primarily aims to stall conflict resolution temporarily, buying time to address the conflict more effectively in the future.

 

d. Withdrawal is a form of approach mode that involves getting away from a conflict situation.

False: Withdrawal aligns more with avoidance modes. It's an attempt to distance oneself or get away from the conflict rather than directly engaging or confronting it.

 

Therefore, the accurate statements are: a and c are true; b and d are false. Hence, the correct code is (C).

Question 29
Which among the following is not a correct statement?(UGC NET Management Dec 2018)
  • A.In latent conflict, although the parties to the conflict realise the fact of conflict for various reasons but they do not show it openly.
  • B.There is a potential ground for perceived conflict to turn into reality.
  • C.Manifest conflict is always documented.
  • D.Manifest conflict in an open conflict.
Correct Answer: Manifest conflict is always documented.

The statement that is not correct among the options is (C) Manifest conflict is always documented.

 

Conflict goes through several stages in its progression:

 

1. Latent Conflict: The conflict exists but is not yet apparent or visible. It could be due to various underlying reasons, such as competition for resources or differing goals.

 

2. Perceived Conflict: This stage occurs when one or more parties start to recognize the existence of a conflict. However, not all latent conflicts are perceived as conflicts by the involved parties.

 

3. Felt Conflict: Emotions become involved here, leading to feelings of tension, frustration, or hostility. It's crucial to note that perceiving conflict doesn't necessarily mean personalizing it or experiencing emotional involvement.

 

4. Manifest Conflict: This stage involves actual conflict behaviors, which can take various forms like open aggression, verbal or physical violence, sabotage, withdrawal, or apathy. Manifest conflict involves actions or behaviors that evoke responses from the conflicting parties.

 

5. Conflict Aftermath: The aftermath of conflict resolution can have both positive and negative consequences for the organization, depending on how the conflict is managed and resolved.

 

The incorrect statement (C) states that manifest conflict is always documented. However, manifest conflict doesn't necessarily involve documentation; it encompasses observable conflict behaviors and actions between conflicting parties, which may or may not be formally documented.

Question 30
Consider the following. (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2014)Assertion “A”:Functional conflict is a type of institutionalized conflict.Reason “R”:Politics is a kind of emergent conflict.
  • A.Both A and R are true.
  • B.A is true, but R is false.
  • C.A is false, but R is true.
  • D.Both A and R are false.
Correct Answer: Both A and R are true.

The assertion "A": Functional conflict is a type of institutionalized conflict, and the reason "R": Politics is a kind of emergent conflict are both true.

 

Functional conflict refers to healthy, constructive disagreements within organizations that can lead to positive change, improvements, and innovative solutions. When conflict is channeled through acceptable arenas and methods, it becomes institutionalized, such as in arbitration, collective bargaining, or reconciliation through dialogue. These organized dispute resolution processes exhibit characteristics akin to games and possess predetermined termination points, classifying them as institutionalized conflicts.

 

On the other hand, emergent conflict, as mentioned in the reason, is conflict stemming from social change. This form of conflict arises as small alterations ignite processes leading to polarization, threats, escalation, and struggles for power. Politics, often stemming from social changes and power struggles, indeed embodies emergent conflict as it involves diverse perspectives, power dynamics, and varying interests competing for influence and control.

 

Therefore, both assertions are accurate: Functional conflict aligns with the concept of institutionalized conflict, while politics represents a form of emergent conflict arising from social changes and power struggles.

Question 31
Formal conflict is a kind of: (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2014)
  • A.Goal Conflict
  • B.Organizational Conflict
  • C.Role Conflict
  • D.Emergent Conflict
Correct Answer: Organizational Conflict

Formal conflict falls under the category of organizational conflict. Organizational conflict encompasses discord arising from perceived or actual opposition among individuals due to differences in needs, values, or interests within a workplace setting. This conflict within organizations may manifest as disputes over revenue distribution, methods of work, disputes over authority and jurisdiction among departments or individuals, as well as subtler conflicts like rivalries, personality clashes, struggles for power, and internal conflicts within individuals responding to competing needs and demands.

Question 32
The pluralistic approach of industrial conflict is based on which one of the following basic assumption / premises? (UGC NET Commerce Nov 2017)
  • A.That conflict occurs when the tendency of industrial society is to treat worker as an isolated individual and deprive him of all control over his environment
  • B.That an enterprise contain people with coalition of different interests
  • C.That industrial conflict is a part of the broader social conflict between classes
  • D.That no consensus is possible, in case of conflicts, because people are with different socio - cultural backgrounds.
Correct Answer: That an enterprise contain people with coalition of different interests

The pluralistic approach of industrial conflict is grounded in the premise that an enterprise contains individuals with a coalition of diverse interests. This approach recognizes that within an organization, various individuals and groups hold differing interests, needs, and objectives. The pluralistic perspective acknowledges the existence of multiple groups with varying concerns and aims, thereby emphasizing the presence of diverse interests within the organizational framework.

Question 33
Assertion “A”:Intra-individual conflict is perhaps the most difficult type of conflict toanalyze, since it is internal to the person.Reasoning “R”: Conflict arises within an individual whenever his drives and motives are blocked and/or he is confronted with competing roles and goals and he is unable to take decisions. (UGC NET Management Jul 2016)
  • A.Assertion“A”and Reasoning“R”, both are correct, and Reasoning“R”is correct explanation of Assertion“A”.
  • B.Assertion“A”and Reasoning“R”, both are correct but Reasoning“R”is not right explanation of Assertion“A”.
  • C.Assertion“A”is correct, whereas Reasoning“R”is incorrect.
  • D.Reasoning“A”is correct, whereas Assertion“A”is incorrect.
Correct Answer: Assertion“A”and Reasoning“R”, both are correct but Reasoning“R”is not right explanation of Assertion“A”.

The assertion "A" and reasoning "R" are both correct, but the reasoning does not directly explain assertion "A."

 

Assertion "A" accurately states that intra-individual conflict, which occurs within a person, is challenging to analyze and manage since it is internal. This form of conflict arises when conflicting tendencies or motives create inner tension, leading individuals to experience frustrations and exhibit various behavioral strategies.

 

Reasoning "R" elaborates on the causes of conflict within individuals, citing blocked motives, competing roles, and the inability to make decisions as sources of intra-individual conflict. It mentions factors like inacceptability, incomparability, and uncertainty contributing to conflict within individuals, leading to frustration, goal conflict, and role conflict.

 

While both the assertion and reasoning are correct, the reasoning does not explicitly explain why intra-individual conflict is challenging to analyze and manage. Instead, it focuses on the causes and types of conflict experienced within individuals. Therefore, the reasoning does not directly serve as an explanation for the difficulty in analyzing intra-individual conflict, resulting in option B being the correct choice.

Question 34
“Third Party intervention” as “Conflict Resolution” is: (UGC NET Management Jun 2012)
  • A.often required
  • B.seldom required
  • C.required as a mandate, when conflict remains unresolved
  • D.not at all considered as an option
Correct Answer: required as a mandate, when conflict remains unresolved

Third-party intervention in conflict resolution can be pivotal and comes in different forms. It's not a uniformly mandated process but becomes necessary when conflicts persist and other methods fail to bring about resolution. The statement (C) is on point in highlighting that third-party intervention is mandated when conflicts remain unresolved through other means.

 

In conflict situations between management and unions or among various stakeholders, third-party intervention might be a significant step to resolve issues. It can involve various levels, starting from voluntary arbitration, where both parties agree on a mediator to resolve the conflict. If no resolution is reached in this stage, the process may advance to conciliation by a government-appointed officer who facilitates discussions and aids in finding a solution. When conflicts persist beyond this stage, adjudication by a tribunal or labor court might become necessary, making it compulsory for the involved parties to accept the decision made by the third party.

 

So, while it's not always the first option, third-party intervention becomes essential as conflicts remain unresolved, moving through different levels or stages until a resolution is achieved or a decision is mandated by an external authority.

Question 35
When one individual or group wins at the expense of another individual or group, it is termed as. (UGC NET Management Dec 2015)
  • A.Zero-sum conflict
  • B.Non-zero sum conflict
  • C.Line-staff conflict
  • D.Formal-informal conflict
Correct Answer: Zero-sum conflict

The situation where one individual or group succeeds or gains while causing a direct loss or disadvantage to another individual or group is referred to as a "Zero-sum conflict" (Option A). In this scenario, the gains and losses balance out to zero, indicating that what one side wins, the other side loses.

Quiz Attempt #118965

Total Questions: 6
Question 1
Distributive bargaining may be explained as (UGC NET Management Sep 2013)
  • A.Bargaining wherein both parties are willing to negotiate over wages, hours and conditions of employment.
  • B.Bargaining that focuses on convincing the other party that the cost of disagreeing with the proposed terms would be very high.
  • C.Bargaining that focuses on convincing the other party that the benefits of agreeing with the proposed terms would be very high.
  • D.None of the above.
Correct Answer: Bargaining that focuses on convincing the other party that the cost of disagreeing with the proposed terms would be very high.

Distributive bargaining, also known as "win-lose" bargaining, involves a negotiation strategy where the focus is on convincing the other party that refusing the proposed terms would incur significant costs. It operates on the premise that the resources or benefits to be distributed are limited and finite, akin to a "Fixed Pie." In this approach, each party endeavors to maximize their share of the limited resources, leading to a competitive negotiation where one's gain is perceived as the other's loss.

Question 2
Negotiations are an important aspect of the collective-bargaining process. What do they ensure? (UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.That conflict is contained within manageable boundaries.
  • B.That there is an agreement between all parties involved.
  • C.That conflict is always resolved.
  • D.It achieves a set of lasting agreements.
Correct Answer: That conflict is contained within manageable boundaries.

Negotiations within the collective-bargaining process serve to contain conflicts within manageable boundaries rather than guaranteeing their resolution. They aim to facilitate discussions and agreements between involved parties, preventing conflicts from escalating beyond control and creating frameworks for addressing disagreements within manageable limits.

Question 3
With respect to collective bargaining match the items in List - I with those in List - II, using the codes at the end of the items.List - I(a) Win - Lose(b) Lose - Win(c) Lose - Lose(d) Win – WinList - II(i) Winning is everything(ii) Nothing for nothing(iii) Everything for everything(iv) Relationship is paramount
  • A.a-(ii), b-(i), c-(iii), d-(iv)
  • B.a-(i), b-(iv), c-(ii), d-(iii)
  • C.a-(i), b-(ii), c-(iii), d-(iv)
  • D.a-(iv), b-(iii), c-(ii), d-(i)
Correct Answer: a-(i), b-(iv), c-(ii), d-(iii)

The matching of negotiation approaches in collective bargaining from List I to List II:

 

(a) Win - Lose → (i) Winning is everything

(b) Lose - Win → (iv) Relationship is paramount

(c) Lose - Lose → (ii) Nothing for nothing

(d) Win – Win → (iii) Everything for everything

 

Win-Lose negotiation strategy emphasizes winning as the primary focus, where one party's gain comes at the expense of the other, signifying "Winning is everything."

Lose-Win negotiation prioritizes the relationship over individual victory, reflecting that "Relationship is paramount."

Lose-Lose negotiation implies "Nothing for nothing," as both parties may fail to reach an agreement, resulting in no beneficial outcome for either side.

Win-Win negotiation indicates "Everything for everything," aiming for mutually beneficial agreements where both parties gain.

 

Therefore, the correct matching of the collective bargaining negotiation strategies in List - I with their descriptions in List - II is option (B) a-(i) b-(iv) c-(ii) d-(iii).

Question 4
The overlapping area of the range of two Negotiating parties which indicates the existence of the possibility of settlement, is known as: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2014)
  • A.Ideals
  • B.Negotiating Continuum
  • C.Compromising Continuum
  • D.Arena
Correct Answer: Arena

The overlapping area between the ideal points and break points of two negotiating parties, signifying the potential for reaching a settlement, is termed the "Bargaining Arena." It represents the space where both parties can potentially find common ground and agree on terms within their respective limits. This arena reflects the range within which negotiations can occur, allowing for the exploration of mutually acceptable solutions that align with each party's interests while acknowledging their boundaries.

Question 5
Match the following. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2013)List – Ia. POSDCORBb. 14 Principles of Managementc. Integration Theory of Managementd. Management by ObjectivesList – IIi. Mary ParkerFolletteii. LutherGullickiii. Peter F. Druckeriv. Henry Fayol
  • A.a-ii, b-iii, c-iv, d-i
  • B.a-ii, b-i, c-iv, d-iii
  • C.a-ii, b-iv, c-i, d-iii
  • D.a-iii, b-i, c-iv, d-ii
Correct Answer: a-ii, b-iv, c-i, d-iii

a. POSDCORB - Luther Gullick

POSDCORB is an acronym representing the functional responsibilities of a chief executive officer, as formulated by Luther Gulick and Lyndall Urwick in their 1937 paper on administrative management theory. The acronym stands for Planning, Organizing, Staffing, Directing, Coordinating, Reporting, and Budgeting. 

 

b. 14 Principles of Management - Henry Fayol

Henry Fayol has given 14 principles of Theory of General and Administrative Management viz. Division of Work, Authority and responsibility, Discipline, Unity of Command, Unity of Direction, Subordination of Individual Interest to General Interest, Remuneration, Centralization vs Decentralization, Scalar Chain, Order, Equity, Stability of Tenure of personnel, Initiative and Espirit de Corps. 

 

c. Integration Theory of Management - Mary Parker Follette

M. P. Follett gave 4 ways of resolving conflict – domination, compromise, manipulation and integration. According to her, "Integration method" has its advantages. Bases of integration method are:

1. The first step to achieve integration is to bring the differences into the open instead of suppressing them. This is necessary to identify and understand real issues involved in a conflict.

2. Second step is to break demands of both parties in their constituent parts (individual issues).

3. Third step is anticipation of conflict. Anticipation does not mean avoidance of conflict but responding to it differently. To Follett, integration is like a game of chess. Anticipation of response by itself is not enough; there is need for preparation for response as well.

 

d. Management by Objectives - Peter F. Drucker

Management by objectives (given by Peter F. Drucker) involves setting specific measurable goals with each employee and then periodically reviewing the progress made. The term MBO almost always refers to a comprehensive organization wide goal-setting and appraisal program that consists of six main steps:

a. Set the organization’s goal

b. Set departmental goals

c. Discuss departmental goals

d. Define expected result

e. Performance review

f. Provide feedback

Question 6
International negotiation is a seven step process comprising of the following: (UGC NET Management Dec 2019)(a) Information exchange and offer(b) Concession(c) Preparation(d) Building a relationship(e) Strategy(f) Persuasion(g) AgreementWhich of the following sequence is in right order?
  • A.(e), (c), (a), (f), (g), (b) and (d)
  • B.(c), (e), (d), (a), (f), (b) and (g)
  • C.(g), (c), (e), (f), (d), (a) and (b)
  • D.(d), (a), (c), (e), (f), (g) and (b)
Correct Answer: (c), (e), (d), (a), (f), (b) and (g)

The correct sequence for the seven-step process in international negotiation is:

 

1. Preparation: Involves setting bargaining objectives, understanding the counterpart, selecting negotiation site, assembling the negotiation team, and establishing an agenda.

 

2. Strategy Development: Addressing questions for the initial session, predictions of the other side's inquiries, framing responses, defining the opening position, and gathering sufficient data to support the position.

 

3. Building Relationships: Initiation of pleasantries and establishing a personal understanding between negotiation partners, forming opinions on negotiators' personalities, goals, and trustworthiness.

 

4. Exchange of Information and the First Offer: Parties share task-related information concerning the proposed agreement, including specifics like quantity, quality, and price, presenting their initial proposals.

 

5. Persuasion: Focusing on understanding each other's positions, identifying commonalities and differences, creating new options, and striving for a win-win situation.

 

6. Concessions: Offering and receiving concessions as a means to meet the needs of the other party, either sequentially or holistically.

 

7. Agreement: The final stage where a formal agreement is formulated, implemented, and the negotiating experience is reviewed.

 

Therefore, the correct sequence is: (B) (c), (e), (d), (a), (f), (b), and (g).

Quiz Attempt #118966

Total Questions: 40
Question 1
As suggested by Collins, arrange the following leadership levels in sequentially higher order. (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2023)a) The leader is a competent managerb) The leader is an executivec) The leader is a highly capable individuald) The leader is an effective leadere) The leader is a contributing team member.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.b, c, d, a, e
  • B.c, e, a, d, b
  • C.c, a, e, d, b
  • D.c, e, a, b, d
Correct Answer: c, e, a, d, b

Option B is the correct answer.

 

In Jim Collins' book "Good to Great," he introduces a hierarchy of leadership levels, with Level 5 Leadership being the highest and most effective form of leadership. Here are the five levels of leadership according to Collins:

 

Level 1 – Highly Capable Individual: At this level, leaders possess skills, capabilities, and knowledge that make them competent contributors. They excel in their individual roles and can produce high-quality work. However, their focus is primarily on their own performance and achievements.

 

Level 2 – Contributing Team Member: Leaders at this level not only excel individually but also contribute effectively to the success of their teams. They work well with others, collaborate, and help the team achieve its goals. While they have the ability to work in a group setting, their influence is limited to their team.

 

Level 3 – Competent Manager: Level 3 leaders are capable managers who can organize people and resources to achieve specific goals. They are effective in planning, organizing, and coordinating tasks, and they ensure that their teams meet their targets. However, their impact is often limited to their immediate sphere of influence.

 

Level 4 – Effective Leader: At this level, leaders go beyond management and start to influence and inspire others. They are able to create a sense of unity and shared purpose within their organizations. They may possess qualities like charisma and vision that help them rally their teams toward achieving larger goals.

 

Level 5 – Executive: This is the pinnacle of Collins' hierarchy. Level 5 leaders combine the qualities of all the previous levels, but what sets them apart is their humility and a deep sense of commitment to the organization's success. They are driven by a desire to see the organization thrive rather than seeking personal glory. They often attribute success to their team and take responsibility for failures themselves. This paradoxical blend of personal humility and professional will is what makes Level 5 leadership so powerful.

 

Collins' research showed that Level 5 leadership was a key factor in transforming good companies into great ones. The Level 5 leader's focus on the organization's success over personal recognition helps create a sustainable and enduring legacy for the company. It's important to note that Collins' model emphasizes a progression through these levels and highlights the importance of humility and a focus on the greater good in effective leadership.

Question 2
Identify the correct sequence of the leadership development process as adopted by Anderson Consulting.(UGC NET Commerce Jun 2023)A. Coach executive terms on individual leadership and effective teamworkB. Assess organization’s direction and current strategies speed at whichsusneffresults hepchevedC. Create effective commination strategical for key influences director shareholder employedetcD. coach individual exclusive performed behavior communicationE. Assess againsetiwsculture dying required shifts and actionmerrleader to charge them cultureChoose the correct answer from the option given below:
  • A.C, D, B, A, E
  • B.E,B,A, C, D
  • C.D, A, B, E, C
  • D.B, E, D, A, C
Correct Answer: B, E, D, A, C

The correct answer is (D) B, E, D, A, C.

 

Anderson Consulting’s leadership development process follows a structured and sequential approach to ensure organizational and leadership transformation:

 

Step 1 (B): Assess the organization’s direction and current strategies and the speed at which success results are achieved.

This is the foundation step where the current state, vision, and strategic direction of the organization are evaluated.

 

Step 2 (E): Assess the organization’s culture, identify required shifts, and determine actions for leaders to drive that cultural change.

This stage focuses on understanding the present culture and the changes needed to align with the company’s goals.

 

Step 3 (D): Coach individual executives on performance behavior and communication.

Once the direction and culture are set, the next step is to coach leaders individually on how they communicate and perform to align with expectations.

 

Step 4 (A): Coach executive teams on individual leadership and effective teamwork.

After individual coaching, the focus moves to team coaching, helping executive teams collaborate effectively and enhance leadership at a group level.

 

Step 5 (C): Create effective communication strategies for key influencers, directors, shareholders, and employees.

Finally, the process includes designing communication strategies to convey changes and developments to all key stakeholders.

 

Therefore, the correct sequence is:

B → E → D → A → C

Question 3
Blake and Morten recognize four leadership styles. One of them is the autocratic tasks management style. The autocratic task manger is one who- (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2023)
  • A.concern themselves very little with either people or production and have minimum involvement in their jobs.
  • B.display in theiraction ,the highest possible dedication both to people and to production.
  • C.are concerned only with developing an efficient operation who have little or no concern for people
  • D.have little or no concern for production but are concerned only for people
Correct Answer: are concerned only with developing an efficient operation who have little or no concern for people

The correct answer is (C) — are concerned only with developing an efficient operation who have little or no concern for people.

 

According to Blake and Mouton's Managerial Grid, leadership styles are based on concern for people and concern for production (task).

 

The autocratic task management style is characterized by:

  • A high concern for production and task efficiency.
  • Little or no concern for people, their feelings, or relationships.

 

Leaders in this style focus on strict control, deadlines, and productivity targets, often ignoring team welfare and morale. This style typically results in an authoritative environment where work gets done, but employee satisfaction and involvement are low.

 

Therefore, the correct answer is (C).
