Question 5
Which of the following are the characteristics of a Leader? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2024)A. Focuses on systems and structureB. Eye on the horizonC. Asks how and whenD. Does things rightE. OriginatesChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A, B & D Only
  • B.B & E Only
  • C.B, C & D Only
  • D.A, B, D & E Only
Correct Answer: B & E Only

The correct answer is (B) B & E Only.

 

A. Focuses on systems and structure — This is a characteristic of a manager, not a leader. The leader focuses on people.

 

B. Eye on the horizon — Correct. The leader has their eye on the horizon, indicating a long-term vision and focus on future possibilities.

 

C. Asks how and when — This is a manager’s characteristic. A leader asks what and why.

 

D. Does things right — This is associated with managers. Leaders do the right thing.

 

E. Originates — Correct. The leader originates ideas and approaches, while the manager imitates.

 

Therefore, the correct answer is (B) B & E Only.

Question 6
Given below are two statements: (UGC NET Management Dec 2023)Statement (I):The adaptation of leadership styles to different contingencies has been well characterised by Robert Tannenbaum and Warren H. Schmidt, developers of leadership continuum concept.Statement (II):They see leadership as involving variety of styles, ranging from one that is highly boss-oriented to one that is highly subordinate centred.In the light of the above statements, choose the most appropriate answer from the options given below:
  • A.Both Statement I and Statement II are correct
  • B.Both Statement I and Statement II are incorrect
  • C.Statement I iscorrectbut Statement II is incorrect
  • D.Statement I isincorrectbut Statement II is correct
Correct Answer: Both Statement I and Statement II are correct

The most appropriate answer is (A) Both Statement I and Statement II are correct.

 

Statement I: The adaptation of leadership styles to different contingencies has indeed been well characterized by Robert Tannenbaum and Warren H. Schmidt. They developed the leadership continuum concept, which emphasizes the importance of adapting leadership styles based on various situational factors.

 

Statement II: Tannenbaum and Schmidt indeed see leadership as involving a variety of styles, ranging from one that is highly boss-oriented to one that is highly subordinate-centered. This idea is central to their leadership continuum concept, which suggests that effective leadership involves a range of styles that can be used based on the situation and the needs of the followers.

 

Therefore, both statements accurately describe the contributions of Tannenbaum and Schmidt to the understanding of leadership styles and their adaptation to different situations.

Question 7
What are the characteristics of an 'Ethical Charismatic Leader'? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2023)a. Uses power to serve othersb. Considers and learns from criticismc. Promotes own personal visiond. Open two-way communicationChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a and b only
  • B.b and d only
  • C.a, b and c only
  • D.a, b and d only
Correct Answer: a, b and d only

The correct answer is option D i.e., a, b and d only.

 

a. Uses power to serve others: This characteristic aligns with ethical leadership, where a leader utilizes their power and influence to benefit others and the greater good, rather than for self-interest or personal gain.

 

b. Considers and learns from criticism: Ethical leaders are open to feedback and criticism, and they use it as an opportunity for self-improvement and growth. They value different perspectives and are willing to learn from their mistakes.

 

c. Promotes own personal vision: This characteristic does not align with ethical leadership. Ethical leaders focus on shared values and the organization's mission rather than solely promoting their personal vision.

 

d. Open two-way communication: Ethical leaders encourage open communication and dialogue within the organization. They value input from others and foster an environment where team members feel comfortable sharing their ideas and concerns.

Question 8
What are the characteristics of transactional leadership? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2023)A. Contingent rewardB. Management by exceptionC. CharismaD. Laissez faireChoose the correct answer from the options given below.Codes
  • A.A and B only
  • B.C and D only
  • C.A, C and D only
  • D.A, B and D only
Correct Answer: A, B and D only

Option D is the correct answer.

 

Contingent Reward: Transactional leaders use contingent reward as a key aspect of their leadership style. This involves setting clear expectations for performance and providing rewards or incentives to employees when they meet these expectations. It's a form of exchange where employees receive rewards for fulfilling their responsibilities and achieving specific goals.

 

Management by Exception: Transactional leaders practice management by exception, which means they intervene or take action only when deviations from established norms or expectations occur.

 

Laissez-faire: Leader gave complete freedom to the group and did not provide any leadership. He did not establish any policies or procedures to do the task. Each member was let alone. No one attempted to influence the other.

Question 9
Which one of the following is identified as the third dimension in the Reddin’s Three-Dimensional Model of Leadership? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2023)
  • A.Effectiveness
  • B.Environments
  • C.Motivation
  • D.Conflict
Correct Answer: Effectiveness

Option A is the correct answer.

 

The Reddin 3-D Leadership Model is a theory proposed by Bill Reddin, which highlights the importance of understanding that the same behaviour can be viewed as appropriate or inappropriate based on the situation at hand.

 

The model is composed of 3 dimensions:

 

1. Task orientation: Task orientation refers to the extent to which a manager directs their subordinates towards achieving the set goals, through activities such as planning, organizing, and controlling.

 

2. Relationships orientation: Relationships orientation refers to the extent to which a manager has personal job relationships, characterized by mutual trust, respect for subordinates' ideas, and consideration for their feelings.

 

3. Effectiveness: Effectiveness refers to the extent to which a manager achieves the output requirements of their position.

Question 12
Functional Leadership Theory is associated with: (UGC NET Commerce Jul 2018)
  • A.Hackman and Walton and McGrath
  • B.Bernard and OrdwayTead
  • C.Koontz and O’Donnell
  • D.Alford and Beatty
Correct Answer: Hackman and Walton and McGrath

Functional Leadership Theory, associated with Hackman, Walton, and McGrath, aims to identify specific leader behaviors that enhance organizational or unit effectiveness. It asserts that a leader's primary responsibility is ensuring that the group's needs are met, leading to improved group cohesion and effectiveness.

 

This theory doesn't place sole leadership responsibility on one individual; rather, it emphasizes a collective set of behaviors within a group that drive accomplishment. It prioritizes how tasks or organizations are led over the formal assignment of leadership roles.

Question 13
In the managerial grid, developed by Blake and Mouton, a manager who has high consideration for production but little concern for people is known as: (UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.1.1 Management
  • B.1.9 Management
  • C.9.1 Management
  • D.5.5 Management
Correct Answer: 9.1 Management

In the Managerial Grid by Blake and Mouton, a manager characterized by high consideration for production yet little concern for people is known as a "9.1 Manager" or a "Task Management Leader."

 

This managerial grid theory highlights the various orientations of leaders toward both tasks and people. Leaders are evaluated on a scale from 1 to 9 along each axis, illustrating their level of concern for production and people.

Question 14
The leadership prototype:(UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.is useful primarily for selection and training of employees
  • B.uses LPC (Least Preferred Co-worker) as an important component
  • C.depicts the image of a model leader
  • D.emphasizes leadership development
Correct Answer: depicts the image of a model leader

The question refers to the concept of Implicit Leadership Theory, which is explained below:

 

Implicit Leadership Theory (ILT) is a cognitive theory of leadership developed by Robert Lord and colleagues. ILT is defined as cognitive structure or prototypes constituted by individuals’ conceptions of the traits and behaviours that characterize a leader. ILTs’ relevance to leadership relies on the premise that followers use these prototypes as a benchmark to categorize others as leaders. This categorization process influence followers’ attitudes and behaviours toward leaders. When a leader is closer to a follower’s idealized image of a leader (i.e., the higher a leader’s prototypicality), that leader will be evaluated more positively. The term implicit is used because they are not outwardly stated and the term theory is used because it involves the generalization of experiences to new experiences. ILTs allow individuals to identify leaders and aid them in responding appropriately to leaders in order to avoid conflict.

Question 15
According to Fiedler’s Contingency Model of Leadership, which one of the following is NOT a situational variable? (UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.Leader-Member relations
  • B.Task structure
  • C.Position power
  • D.Maturity of followers
Correct Answer: Maturity of followers

In Fiedler's Contingency Model of Leadership, the factor "Maturity of followers" is not considered a situational variable.

 

This model evaluates leadership style based on two main components. Firstly, the leadership style is rooted in the consistent interactions between a leader and their work group, perceived as fixed and dependent on the leader's personality. Fiedler employed the Least-Preferred Coworker (LPC) scale to assess leadership styles, determining whether a leader's orientation leans more toward task accomplishment or human relations.

 

The LPC scale asks leaders to describe the coworker they least prefer to work with based on various scales. A high score suggests a human relations orientation, while a low score indicates a task-oriented approach. This approach examines an individual's emotional response to those they struggle to work with, providing insights into their preferred leadership style.

 

The second aspect is situational favorableness or environmental variables that determine a leader's influence over a group.

 

Fiedler focused on three key situational factors: leader-member relations, task structure, and position power.

1. Leader-member relations depict the level of acceptance the group holds for the leader.

2. Task structure details the clarity and comprehensiveness of the assigned tasks to the leader.

3. Position power refers to the formal authority and power attributed to the leader's position within the organization.

Question 16
Which of the following are most closely interconnected? (UGC NET Management Dec 2013)
  • A.Leadership and organization structure
  • B.Leadership and motivation
  • C.Leadership and planning
  • D.Leadership and performance appraisal
Correct Answer: Leadership and motivation

Motivation is the driving force behind individuals striving for success. It significantly influences employee productivity, the quality of work, and the speed of task completion. This intrinsic quality is goal-oriented and aids individuals in accomplishing their objectives.

 

The relationship between leadership and motivation is pivotal. Leaders who possess desired traits can effectively influence employee motivation. Understanding the diverse needs of team members streamlines decision-making processes and daily operations.

 

Effective leaders are tasked with motivating their teams, a challenging responsibility. Hence, an understanding of motivational factors becomes crucial for a leader to effectively inspire and guide their team towards achieving shared goals.

Question 17
The four systems of Management in terms of Leadership styles are related to: (UGC NET Management Dec 2012)
  • A.Blake and Mouton
  • B.Philip Kotler
  • C.Peter F. Drucker
  • D.RensisLikert
Correct Answer: RensisLikert

Rensis Likert is associated with the four systems of management in terms of leadership styles, particularly the System 1 to System 4 models. Likert's research highlighted distinctive managerial approaches:

 

System 1 Management: Characterized as "exploitive-authoritative," it involves highly authoritarian leadership, lack of trust in subordinates, motivation through fear, downward communication, and centralized decision-making.

 

System 2 Management: Described as "benevolent-authoritative," this style exhibits condescending trust in subordinates, motivation using rewards and occasional fear, partial upward communication, some delegation of decision-making, with close policy control.

 

System 3 Management: Known as "consultative," this style demonstrates substantial but not complete trust in subordinates, encouragement of ideas, motivation through rewards and occasional punishment, bidirectional communication, broad policy decisions at the top with specific decisions at lower levels, and some consultation.

 

System 4 Management: Termed as "participative-group," this approach signifies complete trust in subordinates, constructive use of their ideas, rewards based on group participation, extensive communication flow, decentralized decision-making, and operating as a cohesive group.

Question 18
Match the following: (UGC NET Management Dec 2012)List – Ia. Functional Organizationb. Transactional Analysisc. Managerial Gridd. Need TheoryList – II1. F.W. Taylor2. McClelland3. Eric Berne4. Blake and Mouton
  • A.a-1, b-3, c-4, d-2
  • B.a-1, b-2, c-3, d-4
  • C.a-4, b-3, c-2, d-1
  • D.a-2, b-1, c-4, d-3
Correct Answer: a-1, b-3, c-4, d-2

The correct answer is Option A.

 

a. Functional Organization - F.W. Taylor

F.W. Taylor advocated functional organization, an extension of the principle of division of labor. He proposed appointing eight foremen under planning and production departments to guide workers, each with specific responsibilities to ensure smooth operations and efficiency.

 

b. Transactional Analysis - Eric Berne

Transactional Analysis, developed by Eric Berne, focuses on human social interactions and verbal communication. It categorizes interactions into three ego states: Parent, Adult, and Child, each reflecting specific ways of thinking, feeling, and behaving.

 

c. Managerial Grid - Blake and Mouton

The Managerial Grid by Blake and Mouton illustrates leadership styles based on concern for tasks and people. It categorizes leaders into five types based on their balanced or imbalanced concern for task accomplishment and relationships with subordinates.

 

d. Need Theory - McClelland

McClelland's Need Theory concentrates on three fundamental needs: the need for achievement (striving for success), the need for power (influencing others' behavior), and the need for affiliation (desiring friendly relationships). These needs significantly impact individuals' motivations and behaviors.

Question 19
The _____________ proposes that the effective group performance depends on the proper match between the leader's style and the degree to which the situation gives the leader control. (UGC NET Management Jun 2015)
  • A.Behavioural approach
  • B.Fiedler contingency model
  • C.Leader - member exchange theory
  • D.Trait Approach
Correct Answer: Fiedler contingency model

The Fiedler contingency model states that effective group performance relies on the alignment between a leader's style and the degree of control the situation offers to the leader. Fiedler's model categorizes leaders based on their personality-dependent leadership style, measured using the least-preferred co-worker (LPC) scale. High LPC scores indicate a leader with a people-oriented style, while low scores suggest a task-oriented approach.

 

This model incorporates situational favorability, emphasizing three key factors: leader-member relations, task structure, and position power. Task-oriented leaders excel in extremely favorable or unfavorable situations, while person-oriented leaders are effective in moderately favorable conditions.

 

Leader-Member Exchange (LMX) theory focuses on the dyadic relationships between leaders and individual subordinates rather than leader traits or situational factors. It differentiates between in-group members with close relationships marked by trust and mutual respect and out-group members who maintain more distant relationships with the leader.

 

Trait Theory attempts to link specific personal traits such as physical, personality, and mental attributes to leadership success. It categorizes traits into six areas including physical characteristics, background traits, intelligence, personality, task-oriented characteristics, and social traits.

 

Behavioural Theories highlight specific behaviors that differentiate leaders from non-leaders and include theories like Ohio State Studies, University of Michigan Studies, and the Managerial Grid, which focus on behaviors shaping effective leadership.

Question 20
Match the following: (UGC NET Management Sep 2013)List Ia. Delegatingb. Situational theoryc. Grid trainingd. Participative LeadershipList II1. A function of a situation wherein a leader is effective only when the style used to influence and alter the situation is appropriate.2. Low nurturing and low regulating behaviour.3. A function of a situation where in a leader permits subordinates to take part indecision making and permit them a considerable degree of autonomy.4. A multi-step process designed to cultivate concern for people and concern for production.
  • A.a-1, b-2, c-3, 4
  • B.a-2, b-1, c-4, 3
  • C.a-3, b-2, c-4, 1
  • D.a-4, b-3, c-1, 2
Correct Answer: a-3, b-2, c-4, 1

The correct matches are given below:

 

a. Delegating - In specific situations, leaders permit subordinates to actively participate in decision-making, granting them a significant level of autonomy. Delegation of authority involves transferring decision-making power from supervisors to subordinates, ensuring effective task execution and goal attainment.

 

b. Situational theory - The Hersey-Blanchard Situational Leadership Theory asserts the necessity for adaptive leadership styles based on followers' maturity and task specifics. It classifies four leadership styles: Telling (S1), Selling (S2), Participating (S3), and Delegating (S4), each emphasizing different aspects—task completion or fostering team independence.

 

c. Grid training - Blake and Mouton's Managerial Grid, an approach to Organizational Development (OD), focuses on instilling concerns for both productivity and people. It encompasses a multi-stage process: training, team development, intergroup development, organizational goal setting, goal attainment, and stabilization to enhance managerial effectiveness.

 

d. Participative Leadership - This leadership style involves democratic decision-making, where the leader solicits input from team members before making a final decision. Encouraging participation enhances job satisfaction, fosters skill development, and motivates team members to contribute beyond financial rewards. This approach suits contexts where quality and teamwork supersede speed or productivity.

Question 21
Which one of the following is not a component of Bass’ Theory of Transformational Leadership? (UGC NET Management Jul 2018)
  • A.Idealized influence
  • B.Inspirational motivation
  • C.Intellectual stimulation
  • D.Team consideration
Correct Answer: Team consideration

Team consideration is not a component of Bass’ Theory of Transformational Leadership. The theory is explained as follows:

 

The Bass Transformational Leadership Theory, is based on the extent to which a leader influences followers. Followers go after a leader because of trust, honesty, and other qualities and the stronger these are, the greater loyalty they have for the leader. The leader transforms the followers because of her or his having these qualities.

 

Bass saw following aspects of transformational leadership:

1. Individual consideration, where there is an emphasis on what a group member needs. The leader acts as a role model, mentor, facilitator, or teacher to bring a follower into the group and be motivated to do tasks.

2. Intellectual stimulation is provided by a leader in terms of challenge to the prevailing order, task, and individual. He seeks ideas from the group and encourages them to contribute, learn and be independent. The leader often becomes a teacher.

3. Inspirational motivation component states that transformational leaders behave in ways that are inspirational to followers and provide meaning and a sense of challenge to their work. This is achieved in three different ways: involving followers in the development of a preferred vision for the future, communicating clear expectations, and by demonstrating a clear commitment to the shared goals and vision of the group or team.

4. Idealized influenced refers to the leader becoming a full-fledged role model, acting out and displaying ideal traits of honesty, trust, enthusiasm, pride, and so forth.

Question 22
Blake and Mouton proposed famous managerial Grid with ‘task orientation’ and ‘people orientation’ as two independent dimensions. Identify the correct numericaldenotionsof the managerial styles given below: (UGC NET HRM Jul 2016)a. Team managementb. Impoverished managementc. Country club managementd. Middle of the road managemente. Authority compliance
  • A.a-(9,9), b-(1,1), c-(1,9), d-(5,5), e-(9,1)
  • B.a-(9,1), b-(1,1), c-(1,9), d-(9,9), e-(5,5)
  • C.a-(1,1), b-(5,5), c-(9,9), d-(1,9), e-(9,1)
  • D.a-(9,9), b-(1,1), c-(5,5), d-(1,9), e-(9,1)
Correct Answer: a-(9,9), b-(1,1), c-(1,9), d-(5,5), e-(9,1)

The correct matches are given below:

a. Team management – (9,9)

b. Impoverished management – (1,1)

c. Country club management – (1,9)

d. Middle of the road management – (5,5)

e. Authority compliance – (9,1)

 

Leaders can be oriented towards both tasks and persons. This theory (Managerial Grid) by Blake and Mouton (1978) has a popular application of both task and person orientation. According to this theory leaders are most effective when they achieve a high and balanced concern for people and for tasks. Each leader can be rated somewhere along each of the axes from 1 to 9.

 

Although there can be 81 possible combinations, you should try to understand following 5 types:

1. The (9, 1) leader is primarily concerned about the task or production. He is concerned with his responsibility to see that the work is completed. He is called a Task-Management leader.

2. The (1, 9) leader is primarily concerned for people and only incidentally concerned with production. The leader's major responsibility is to establish harmonious relationships among subordinates and to provide a secure and pleasant work atmosphere. He is called as Country Club Management leader.

3. The (1,1) leader is concerned with neither production nor people. He tries to stay out of the way and not become involved in the conflict between the necessity for production and the attainment of good working relationship. He is called as Impoverish Management leader.

4. The (5,5) leader reflects a middle ground position and is called as Middle of the Road Management leader. He seeks to compromise between high production and employee satisfaction.

5. The (9,9) leader is extremely concerned about the task and also the people. He is concerned to see that the work accomplishment is from committed people; interdependence through a'common stake' in organisation; purpose leads to relationship of trust and respect. He is called a Team Management leader.

Question 24
Who developed the ‘Managerial Grid’ Theory? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2010)
  • A.Sydney and BeatriceWebbs
  • B.Robert Blake and Jane S. Mouton
  • C.W.J.Reddin
  • D.RensisLikert
Correct Answer: Robert Blake and Jane S. Mouton

The managerial grid model (1964) is a situational leadership model developed by Robert R. Blake and Jane Mouton. This model originally identified five different leadership styles based on the concern for people and the concern for production. The optimal leadership style in this model is based on Theory Y. The model is represented as a grid with concern for production as the x-axis and concern for people as the y-axis; each axis ranges from 1 (Low) to 9 (High).

Question 25
Arrange the following systems in the right order on the managerial style continuum suggested byRensisLikert. (UGC NET HRM Dec 2012)(a) Consultative(b) Benevolent Authoritative(c) Exploitative Authoritative(d) Joint decision-making
  • A.c, b, a, d
  • B.c, a, b, d
  • C.b, a, c, d
  • D.c, d, b, a
Correct Answer: c, b, a, d

Rensis Likert identified four main styles of leadership, in particular around decision-making and the degree to which people are involved in the decision. 

1) Exploitive authoritative: In this style, the leader has a low concern for people and uses such methods as threats and other fear-based methods to achieve conformance. 

2) Benevolent authoritative: When the leader adds concern for people to an authoritative position, a 'benevolent dictatorship' is formed. The leader now uses rewards to encourage appropriate performance and listens more to concerns lower down the organization. 

3) Consultative: The upward flow of information here is still cautious and rose-tinted to some degree, although the leader is making genuine efforts to listen carefully to ideas. Nevertheless, major decisions are still largely centrally made. 

4) Participative: At this level, the leader makes maximum use of participative methods, engaging people lower down the organization in decision-making. People across the organization are psychologically closer together and work well together at all levels.

Question 26
Which of the following statements are not true? (UGC NET HRM Aug 2016)(a) According to Behavioural theories, success can be defined in terms of describable behaviour.(b) According to Trait theories people are not born with certain inherited traits.(c) Democratic leaders involve their people in decision making.(d) According to F.E. Fiedler relationships, power, and task structure are not the key factors that drive effective leadership styles.
  • A.Both (a) and (c)
  • B.Both (b) and (d)
  • C.Both (a) and (d)
  • D.Both (a) and (b)
Correct Answer: Both (b) and (d)

Statement (b) is not true because Trait theories actually propose that certain inherited traits are inherent to effective leadership. These theories often identify specific behavioral characteristics or personality traits that are believed to be common in effective leaders.

 

Statement (d) is not true as Fiedler's contingency theory argues that relationships, power dynamics, and task structures are indeed key factors influencing effective leadership styles. Fiedler's model highlights the importance of situational favorableness or contingency factors in determining leadership effectiveness, where the leader's style and the situation's favorability play crucial roles. The leader's style is assessed by the Least Preferred Co-worker (LPC) scale, while situational favorableness considers leader-member relations, task structure, and leader position power.

Question 27
Match the contributors (Behavioural Scientists) List-I with their contributions given in List-II. (UGC NET HRM Jan 2017)List – Ia. Blake R.R. & Mouton J.S.b. LikertR.c. Mc. Gregord. Mayo E andRothlisbergerF.J.List – IIi. Hawthorne Effectii. Theory X and Yiii. Michigan Study on Leadership Styleiv. Managerial Grid Theory
  • A.a-iv, b-i, c-ii, d-iii
  • B.a-iii, b-ii, c-iv, d-i
  • C.a-iv, b-iii, c-ii, d-i
  • D.a-iv, b-ii, c-iii, d-i
Correct Answer: a-iv, b-iii, c-ii, d-i

Option C is the correct answer.

 

a. Blake R.R. & Mouton J.S. - Managerial Grid Theory: This theory emphasizes a leader's effectiveness based on their concern for both tasks and people, rating leaders along axes to achieve a balanced concern.

 

b. Likert R. - Michigan Study on Leadership Style: Likert identified two main leadership orientations - employee orientation and production orientation. Employee-oriented leaders focus on relationships and individual needs, while production-oriented leaders emphasize production and technical aspects, relating these orientations to employee performance.

 

c. Mc. Gregor - Theory X and Y: McGregor's Theory X and Theory Y posit contrasting views about employee behavior. Theory X assumes a negative outlook where employees inherently dislike work and require control, while Theory Y adopts a positive view, seeing work as natural, and employees as self-directed and responsible.

 

d. Mayo E and Rothlisberger F.J. - Hawthorne Effect: The Hawthorne experiments, led by Elton Mayo and his team, highlighted the importance of social relationships and human factors in productivity, suggesting that these elements were more influential than mere changes in working conditions.

Question 28
The Leadership Theories based on the assumption that 'the leader's ability to lead is contingent upon various situational factors such as the leader's preferred style, the capabilities and behaviours of the followers etc. is known as: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2015)
  • A.Situational Leadership Theory
  • B.Behavioural Theories
  • C.Contingency Theories
  • D.Trait Theories
Correct Answer: Contingency Theories

Contingency theories of leadership assert that a leader's effectiveness hinges upon situational factors like their preferred style, follower capabilities, and behaviors. These theories, including the Fiedler model, Hersey-Blanchard situational theory, Leader-participation model, and Path-goal theory, emphasize that the most suitable leadership style depends on specific situations and contexts.

 

Behavioral theories posit that certain behaviors differentiate leaders from non-leaders. Examples include the Ohio State Studies, University of Michigan Studies, and Managerial Grid, which focus on identifying behaviors that distinguish effective leaders.

 

Trait theories, described by Kelly (1974), attempt to classify personal characteristics associated with leadership success, encompassing physical attributes, background, intelligence, personality traits, task-oriented qualities, and social characteristics.

 

The situational theory, or the Hersey-Blanchard Situational Leadership Theory, suggests that there isn't a single best leadership style; effectiveness relies on adapting one's style to the given situation. This theory stresses the importance of assessing various factors like task type, group nature, and contextual cues to determine the most appropriate leadership approach.

Question 29
Match the Leadership Theories and their proponents given in Lists - I and II below: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2015)List – I Leadership Theories(a) Managerial Grid Theory(b) Iowa Leadership Studies(c) Group and Exchange Theories of Leadership(d) Social Learning TheoriesList – II Proponents(i)Hollandderand Julian (1969)(ii) Albert Bandura (1977)(iii)Lippittand White (1939)(iv) Blake and Mouton (1978)
  • A.a­-(ii), b-(iii), c-(iv), d-(i)
  • B.a-(i), b-(ii), c-(iv), d-(iii)
  • C.a-(iii), b-(ii), c-(i), d-(iv)
  • D.a-(iv), b-(iii), c-(i), d-(ii)
Correct Answer: a-(iv), b-(iii), c-(i), d-(ii)

Option D is correct answer. The correct matches are given below:

 

(a) Managerial Grid Theory - Blake and Mouton (1978)

This theory by Blake and Mouton (1978) emphasizes both task and person orientation in leadership. It suggests that leaders are most effective when they achieve a balanced concern for both people and tasks, with each leader rated along axes from 1 to 9, allowing for multiple combinations.

 

(b) Iowa Leadership Studies - Lippitt and White (1939)

Conducted in the late 1930s, these studies by Lewin, Lippitt, and White identified three major leadership styles:

Authoritarian Leaders: Providing clear expectations and directives.

Democratic Leaders: Offering guidance while allowing input from group members.

Laissez-faire Leaders: Offering minimal guidance, leaving decision-making to the group.

 

(c) Group and Exchange Theories of Leadership - Hollander and Julian (1969)

Hollander and Julian's theory aligns with social exchange theory, which suggests that social behavior results from an exchange process aiming to maximize benefits and minimize costs. They propose that leaders provide benefits or rewards to followers in exchange for help in achieving organizational goals.

 

(d) Social Learning Theories - Albert Bandura (1977)

Albert Bandura's Social Learning Theory posits that individuals learn through observation, imitation, and modeling. It emphasizes that learning occurs through social interaction and is influenced by attention, memory, and motivation, bridging behaviorist and cognitive learning theories.

Question 30
Leaders who provide individualised consideration and intellectual stimulation and who possess charisma is known as:(UGC NET Management Jun 2009)
  • A.Transactional Leaders
  • B.Transformational Leaders
  • C.Situational Leaders
  • D.Visionary Leaders
Correct Answer: Transformational Leaders

Transformational leaders are characterized by their ability to inspire and motivate followers through individualized consideration, intellectual stimulation, and charisma. They aim to bring about significant changes by engaging and empowering their followers to achieve beyond their self-interests for the greater good of the organization.

Question 31
Managerial Grid suggests the following as the best leader behaviour: (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2014)
  • A.High structure and high consideration
  • B.Low structure and low consideration
  • C.High concern both for production and people
  • D.Low concern both for production and people
Correct Answer: High concern both for production and people

The Managerial Grid model proposes that the most effective leadership behavior involves having high concern for both production and people. According to this theory by Blake and Mouton, effective leaders find a balance between achieving tasks and caring for their team members. This balance leads to a leadership style known as Team Management, where leaders focus on creating a shared sense of purpose, trust, and respect among the team. Leaders strive to ensure work gets done while fostering committed and interdependent individuals invested in the organization's success.

Question 32
A leader who identifies what subordinates need to do to achieve objectives, clarify organizational roles and tasks, set up an organization structure, reward performance and provide for the social needs of their followers, is (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2013)
  • A.a transformational leader
  • B.a participative leader
  • C.a transactional leader
  • D.an autocratic leader
Correct Answer: a transactional leader

Transactional leadership, as a leadership style, is characterized by a leader who clarifies the roles and responsibilities of subordinates to achieve objectives, establishes the organization's structure, offers rewards for performance, and meets social needs within the team or organization.

 

Leadership styles are varied and can greatly impact the dynamics within a team or organization. Autocratic leadership displays high control levels with limited input from team members, often leading to discontent and high staff turnover. Bureaucratic leadership strictly follows procedures, which can be beneficial in high-risk or high-value situations but may stifle innovation in other contexts. Charismatic leadership focuses on enthusiasm but risks dependence on the leader. Democratic leadership encourages participation and contributes to job satisfaction, even though it might slow down decision-making processes. Laissez-faire leadership involves minimal interference, suitable for highly skilled and self-motivated teams, but can result in insufficient management.

 

People-oriented leadership concentrates on team development and collaboration, while task-oriented leadership is dedicated to task completion but may overlook team well-being. Transactional leadership, based on a transactional relationship where compliance is expected in return for compensation, provides little scope for enhancing job satisfaction or team motivation. Transformational leadership, on the other hand, inspires teams with a vision, emphasizing communication and delegation, which can drive innovation and progress.

 

While transactional leaders focus on short-term tasks and compliance, transformational leaders motivate teams through a shared vision, encouraging innovation and development. Organizations often benefit from a mix of transactional and transformational leadership, where transactional leaders ensure consistency and stability in routine tasks, while transformational leaders steer initiatives that bring added value.

Question 33
Which of the following is not true about an employee-centeredleader as identified by Michigan researchers? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2014)
  • A.Treats subordinates as human beings.
  • B.Shows concern for theirwell being.
  • C.Focuses on work standards and close supervision.
  • D.Encourages and involves them in goal setting.
Correct Answer: Focuses on work standards and close supervision.

The incorrect statement regarding an employee-centered leader as per the Michigan researchers is option (C), which suggests that this leader focuses on work standards and close supervision.

 

The Michigan researchers identified two primary leadership orientations: employee orientation and production orientation. The employee-centered leader, as highlighted by these studies, focuses on treating subordinates as individuals, showing concern for their well-being, and actively involving them in goal setting. This leader emphasizes personal relationships and values the individuality and personal needs of their team members. They encourage open communication, trust, and constructive use of ideas from their subordinates.

 

Conversely, the production-oriented leader emphasizes task accomplishment and the technical aspects of the job, viewing subordinates more as tools for achieving organizational goals rather than focusing on their individual well-being. These two orientations were linked to employee performance, with the employee-oriented style correlating with higher productivity compared to the production-oriented approach.

Question 34
Which of the following is suggested by Blake and Mouton as the best leadershipbehavior? (UGC NET Commerce Sep 2013)
  • A.Low concern for people but high concern for production.
  • B.Low concern for both people and production.
  • C.High concern for both people and production.
  • D.High concern for people and low concern for production.
Correct Answer: High concern for both people and production.

The best leadership behavior suggested by Blake and Mouton is option (C), which advocates high concern for both people and production. Their Managerial Grid theory emphasizes achieving a balance between task and person orientation for effective leadership.

 

The Managerial Grid proposed by Blake and Mouton introduces five types of leader orientations, depicted on a grid based on concern for production and concern for people.

 

These types include:

1. The (9, 1) leader: Primarily concerned about task or production, focusing on ensuring work completion. This leader is known as a Task-Management leader.

2. The (1, 9) leader: Primarily concerned with people and relationships, creating a harmonious work environment. This leader is referred to as a Country Club Management leader.

3. The (1, 1) leader: Shows little concern for both production and people, avoiding involvement in conflicts related to work relationships. This leader is called an Impoverish Management leader.

4. The (5, 5) leader: Represents a middle-ground position, aiming to balance high production with employee satisfaction. Known as the Middle of the Road Management leader.

5. The (9, 9) leader: Highly concerned about both task and people, focusing on achieving work accomplishments through committed individuals and fostering a relationship of trust and respect. This leader is identified as a Team Management leader.

Question 35
Consider the following leadership styles: (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2014)1. Telling2. Autocratic3. Selling4. Motivating5. Participating6. Delegating7. CharismaticSelect the four styles of leadership explained by Hersey andBlauchard.
  • A.1, 2, 6 and 7
  • B.2, 3, 4 and 5
  • C.1, 3, 5 and 6
  • D.4, 5, 6 and 7
Correct Answer: 1, 3, 5 and 6

The Hersey-Blanchard Situational Leadership Theory (which suggested four styles of leadership namely Telling, Selling, Participating and Delegating) was created by Dr Paul Hersey, a professor and author of "The Situational Leader," and Ken Blanchard, author of the best-selling "The One-Minute Manager," among others.

 

The theory states that instead of using just one style, successful leaders should change their leadership styles based on the maturity of the people they're leading and the details of the task. Using this theory, leaders should be able to place more or less emphasis on the task, and more or less emphasis on the relationships with the people they're leading, depending on what's needed to get the job done successfully.

 

According to Hersey and Blanchard, there are four main leadership styles:

(a) Telling (S1) – Leaders tell their people exactly what to do, and how to do it. 

(b) Selling (S2) – Leaders still provide information and direction, but there's more communication with followers. Leaders "sell" their message to get the team on board.

(c) Participating (S3) – Leaders focus more on the relationship and less on direction. The leader works with the team, and shares decision-making responsibilities. 

(d) Delegating (S4) – Leaders pass most of the responsibility onto the follower or group. The leaders still monitor progress, but they're less involved in decisions.

 

As you can see, styles S1 and S2 are focused on getting the task done. Styles S3 and S4 are more concerned with developing team members' abilities to work independently. 

Question 36
According to Hersey and Blanchard’s situational approach to leadership, the participating style of leadership has: (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2015)
  • A.High task and low relationship orientation
  • B.High task and high relationship orientation
  • C.Low task and high relationship orientation
  • D.Low task and low relationship orientation
Correct Answer: Low task and high relationship orientation

The participating style of leadership, as per Hersey and Blanchard’s situational approach, is characterized by low task and high relationship orientation. According to their theory, leadership styles should adapt to the maturity of the individuals being led and the specifics of the task at hand.

 

This theory outlines four primary leadership styles:

1. Telling (S1): Leaders instruct their team on what to do and how to do it without much discussion or collaboration.

2. Selling (S2): Leaders provide direction but engage in more communication, aiming to persuade the team to align with their message.

3. Participating (S3): Leaders focus more on building relationships, involving the team in decision-making, and sharing responsibilities.

4. Delegating (S4): Leaders entrust most responsibilities to the team, monitoring progress but allowing autonomy in decision-making.

 

The participating style (S3) emphasizes relationship-building over direction and task orientation. It involves collaborating with the team and sharing decision-making responsibilities to foster team development.

Question 37
According to Fiedler’s contingency model of leadership,favorablenessof situation depends on which combination of the following? (UGC NET Commerce Jul 2016)(a) Leader-member relationship(b) Member-member relationship(c) Leader’s position power(d) Degree of task structure(e) Degree of training
  • A.(a), (b) and (c)
  • B.(a), (c) and (d)
  • C.(c), (d) and (e)
  • D.(a), (b) and (e)
Correct Answer: (a), (c) and (d)

According to Fiedler’s contingency model of leadership, the favorableness of a situation depends on the combination of three factors:

(i) Leader-member relationship (a)

(ii) Leader’s position power (c)

(iii) Degree of task structure (d)

 

Fiedler's model revolves around two primary elements: leadership style and situational favorableness. The leadership style, classified using the least-preferred coworker (LPC) scale, determines whether a leader is more task-oriented or relationship-oriented based on their perception of the coworker they least prefer working with.

 

The model further considers situational favorableness, focusing on three key situational factors:

1. Leader-member relations: The degree of acceptance and rapport between the leader and the group.

2. Task structure: The clarity and specificity of the tasks assigned.

3. Position power: The extent of formal authority and power attributed to the leader’s position.

 

Favorability of a situation for a leader is determined by these factors, influencing the effectiveness of either a task-oriented or relationship-oriented leader. When the situation strongly favors or disfavors the leader, a task-oriented leader tends to be effective. However, in moderately favorable situations, a relationship-oriented leader performs more effectively.

  • A.Self Esteem
  • B.Self Actualization

Self-Esteem is your subjective sense of overall personal worth or value. Similar to self-respect, it describes your level of confidence in your abilities and attributes.

Question 1
Leader-Member relations; task structure and position power are attributes of which leadership theory? (UGC NET HRM Sep 2013)
  • A.Trait Theory
  • B.Behavioural Theory
  • C.Situational Theory
  • D.Contingency Theory
Correct Answer: Contingency Theory

Leader-Member relations, task structure, and position power are attributes associated with the Contingency Theory of leadership, particularly exemplified in the Fiedler Contingency Model developed by Fred Fiedler. This model posits that a leader's effectiveness is determined by the interplay of leadership style and situational favorableness. The three factors, namely Leader-Member Relations, Task Structure, and Leader's Position Power, are integral in assessing the favorability of a situation for a leader's effectiveness within this theory.

Question 2
Match the names of the Behavioural scientists and their contributions given. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2009)List–A(a) Mayo E. and Roethlisberger F. J.(b) Mc.GregarD.(c) Likert R.(d) Kelly J.List-B(i) Theory X and Y(ii) Michigan study an leadership style(iii) Trait Theory of leadership(iv) Hawthorne effect
  • A.a-(iv), b-(i), c-(ii), d-(iii)
  • B.a-(ii), b-(i), c-(iv), d-(iii)
  • C.a-(iii), b-(i), c-(ii), d-(iv)
  • D.a-(iv), b-(i), c-(iii), d-(ii)
Correct Answer: a-(iv), b-(i), c-(ii), d-(iii)

The correct answer is Option A. The correct matches are given below:

 

(a) Mayo E. and Roethlisberger F. J. - Hawthorne effect: The Hawthorne effect, as studied by Mayo and Roethlisberger, denotes the alteration in individuals' behavior when they know they are being observed. This effect was evident in the famous studies conducted at the University of Michigan in the 1950s, which highlighted three vital attributes of effective leaders: task-oriented behavior, relationship-oriented behavior, and participative behavior.

 

(b) Mc. Gregor D. - Theory X and Y: Douglas McGregor developed Theory X and Theory Y in the 1960s at MIT Sloan School of Management. Theory X presumes employees inherently dislike work, necessitating strict supervision and control systems. Conversely, Theory Y assumes employees are self-motivated, capable, and enjoy their work, proposing that their abilities are underutilized in most organizations.

 

(c) Likert R. - Michigan study on leadership style: Likert's study at the University of Michigan Survey Research Centre identified two primary leadership orientations: employee orientation and production orientation. Employee-oriented leaders prioritize individual relationships, showing trust and interest in their subordinates. Conversely, production-oriented leaders focus on task accomplishment, viewing employees as tools for organizational goals, emphasizing work conditions and methods for better productivity.

 

(d) Kelly J. - Trait Theory of leadership: Kelly's Trait Theory, developed in 1974, seeks to classify personal characteristics associated with leadership success. This theory links various traits such as physical, personality, intelligence, task-oriented and social traits to effective leadership, attempting to outline a comprehensive set of traits defining successful leaders.

Question 3
In the managerial grid, the managers who have little or no concern for production but are concerned only for people are known as what type of managers? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)
  • A.1.1 Management
  • B.5.5 Management
  • C.9.1 Management
  • D.1.9 Management
Correct Answer: 1.9 Management

In the Managerial Grid, managers who exhibit little or no concern for production but prioritize their focus solely on people are classified as "1.9 Managers" or "Country Club Managers."

 

The Managerial Grid, introduced by Blake and Mouton in 1978, illustrates leadership orientations concerning both tasks and people. It categorizes leaders based on their concern for tasks (production) and people, with a rating from 1 to 9 along each axis.

Question 4
Theory X represents: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2011)
  • A.Democratic style of leadership
  • B.Autocratic style of leadership
  • C.Laissez-faire style of leadership
  • D.Humanistic style of leadership
Correct Answer: Autocratic style of leadership

Theory X, as postulated by McGregor, aligns with an autocratic style of leadership. It asserts that employees inherently dislike work and will avoid it whenever possible. This management approach assumes that individuals need coercion, control, and even the threat of punishment to exert effort towards organizational goals. Moreover, Theory X contends that most people prefer to be directed, shun responsibility, lack ambition, and prioritize security above other factors. In contrast, Theory Y, the opposing assumption, views work as natural, believes in self-direction and self-control, and emphasizes that individuals can seek and accept responsibility when given the right conditions and incentives.

Question 5
Which of the following is not the characteristic of a transformational leader? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2014)
  • A.Inspiring by communicating high expectations.
  • B.Promoting intelligence and rationality.
  • C.Treating employees individually.
  • D.Avoiding making decisions.
Correct Answer: Avoiding making decisions.

A characteristic that doesn't align with a transformational leader is "Avoiding making decisions." Transformational leaders inspire and motivate followers by setting high expectations, promoting intelligence and rationality, and treating employees as individuals. They focus on changing and directing followers' thinking and needs, aiming to bring about transformation and a sense of purpose. These leaders are proactive in shaping their followers' mindset and goals rather than avoiding decision-making.

Question 6
Who developed the ‘Managerial Grid’ on the basis of Ohio State Study?
  • A.RensisLikert
  • B.Lewin,Lippittand White
  • C.Robert Blake and Jane S. Mouton
  • D.Victor Vroom and PhillipYetton
Correct Answer: Robert Blake and Jane S. Mouton

Managerial Grid Model, also known as Leadership Grid was developed by Robert R. Blake and Jane Srygley Mouton in 1964. The managerial grid model is composed of five different leadership styles. These styles were a relation between a manager's a) concern for people, b) concern for production and c) his motivation. The motivation dimension really provides the underlying motive of the leader behind a successful leadership style. 

Question 7
Who among the following developed the technique of Management by Exception? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2012)
  • A.Joseph L. Massie
  • B.Lester R.Bittel
  • C.L.F.Urwick
  • D.Peter F. Drucker
Correct Answer: Lester R.Bittel

The technique of Management by Exception was developed by Lester R. Bittel. It is a system of identification and communication that signals the manager as to when and where his attention is needed. The main object of this system is to enable the manager to identify and isolate the problems that call for decision and action, and avoid or ignore or pay less attention to less critical problems which better be handled by his subordinates.

Question 8
Which of the following are major principles of leading? (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2013)(i) Principle of motivation(ii) Principle of continuous development(iii) Principle of harmony of objectives(iv) Principle of open competition(v) Principle of communication claritySelect the correct answer from the codes given below:
  • A.(i), (ii), (iii), (v)
  • B.(i), (ii), (iii), (iv), (v)
  • C.(i), (iii), (iv), (v)
  • D.(i), (iii), (v)
Correct Answer: (i), (iii), (v)

The major principles of leading encompass motivation, harmony of objectives, and communication clarity.

 

1. Principle of Motivation: Leaders should employ various motivational techniques like praise and recognition to enhance productivity and job satisfaction among individuals.

 

2. Principle of Harmony of Objectives: Aligning individual goals with group or organizational objectives is fundamental in leadership. It involves resolving conflicts between personal aspirations and the organization's goals, fostering a cohesive approach towards shared objectives.

 

3. Principle of Communication Clarity: Effective leadership communication is precise and straightforward. Leaders must ensure clarity in their directives, ensuring team members understand precisely what is expected and when. This clarity avoids ambiguity and promotes better comprehension and execution of tasks.

Question 9
Match the following: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2010)Leadership Theory(a) Contingency Theory(b) Trait Theory(c) Charismatic TheoryLeadership Factors(i) Personal vision and energy(ii) Personal drive, desire to lead, personal integrity(iii) Leader’s position power, task structure and leader member relations
  • A.a-(i), b-(iii), c-(ii)
  • B.a-(iii), b-(ii), c-(i)
  • C.a-(ii), b-(iii), c-(i)
  • D.a-(i), b-(ii), c-(iii)
Correct Answer: a-(iii), b-(ii), c-(i)

The correct answer is Option B.

 

Contingency Theory aligns with the factors of a leader's position power, task structure, and leader-member relations. This theory posits that no single method suits all organizational structures or decision-making processes. Instead, it emphasizes adapting leadership styles based on internal and external situations to optimize effectiveness.

 

Trait Theory corresponds to personal drive, the desire to lead, and personal integrity. It delves into the measurement of stable behavioral, thought, and emotional patterns in individuals. Traits, as per this theory, remain relatively consistent over time, varying among individuals and significantly influencing their behaviors.

 

Charismatic Theory relates to personal vision and energy. It revolves around leadership provided by individuals perceived as heroic or inspirational. Such leaders wield significant organizational power, capable of driving remarkable changes and extracting exceptional performance from their teams. For instance, a charismatic business manager might spearhead a turnaround or introduce a groundbreaking product line.

Question 10
Given below are two statements, one labelled as Assertion and the other labelled as Reason.Read the statements and choose the correct answer using the code given below.(UGC NET Management Dec 2018)Assertion “A”:In the 21s century we are going to need a new generation of leaders; not managers.Reason “R”:Leadership is about developing a vision of the future rather than just aligning people by communicating this vision and inspiring them to overcome hurdles.
  • A.“A”is correct, but“R”is incorrect.
  • B.Both“A”and“R”are incorrect.
  • C.Both“A”and“R”are correct and“R”is the right explanation of“A”.
  • D.Both“A”and“R”are correct, but“R”is not the right explanation of“A”.
Correct Answer: Both“A”and“R”are correct and“R”is the right explanation of“A”.

In the 21st century, the requirement is for a new generation of leaders rather than managers. Managers focus on organizing routine work, while leaders guide, motivate, and set the direction for their teams. Leadership entails crafting a vision for the future and inspiring individuals to surmount obstacles, not solely aligning people with that vision through communication. This means that both the assertion and the reason are correct, and the reason provides an accurate explanation for the assertion.

Question 11
The characteristics of different levels of leaders are given below. Arrange these in an increasing order of levels. (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2021)1. He contributes to the achievement of group objectives and works effectively with others in a group.2. He builds enduring greatness through a paradoxical combination of professional will and personal humanity.3. He makes a productive contribution through talent, knowledge, skills, and good work habits.4. Hecatalyzescommitment to and vigorous pursuit of a clear and compelling vision and stimulates the group to high‐performance standards.5. He organizes people and resources towards the effective and efficient pursuit of predetermined objectives.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.3, 5, 4, 1, 2
  • B.1, 5, 4, 2, 3
  • C.1, 3, 5, 2, 4
  • D.3, 1, 5, 4, 2
Correct Answer: 3, 1, 5, 4, 2

The progression of leadership levels is as follows:

(i) He makes a productive contribution through talent, knowledge, skills, and good work habits.

(ii) He contributes to the achievement of group objectives and works effectively with others in a group.

(iii) He organizes people and resources towards the effective and efficient pursuit of predetermined objectives.

(iv) He catalyzes commitment to and vigorous pursuit of a clear and compelling vision and stimulates the group to high-performance standards.

(v) He builds enduring greatness through a paradoxical combination of professional will and personal humanity.

So, the increasing order of levels would be 3, 1, 5, 4, 2, making the correct answer (D).

Question 12
Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of transactional leaders? (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2021)
  • A.Gives personal attention, treats each employee individually.
  • B.Abdicates responsibilities, avoid making decisions.
  • C.Intervenes only when standards are not met.
  • D.Contracts exchange of reward for efforts.
Correct Answer: Gives personal attention, treats each employee individually.

Option (A) is not a characteristic of transactional leaders. Transactional leaders typically do not give personal attention or treat each employee individually. Instead, they tend to focus more on the tasks and outcomes, using a structured approach to motivate employees through rewards and punishments based on performance. This style emphasizes meeting standards and maintaining the status quo rather than individualized attention or personalized treatment.

Question 13
The leadership theory of describes that effective group performance depends on the proper match between the leader's style if interacting with his subordinates and the degree to which the situation gives control and influence to the leader. (UGC NET Management Dec 2015)
  • A.'Iowa State Leadership Studies'; RonaldLippittand Ralph K. White
  • B.'Managerial Grid'; Blake and Mouton
  • C.'Trait Theory';Stodgilland Barnard
  • D.'Contingency Model'; Fred Fiedler
Correct Answer: 'Contingency Model'; Fred Fiedler

The Contingency Model, proposed by Fred Fiedler, emphasizes that effective group performance relies on the compatibility between a leader's style of interacting with subordinates and the level of control and influence provided by the situation. This theory underscores the importance of situational factors in determining leadership effectiveness.

Question 14
InReddin’s‘TridimensionalGrid’, which one of the following is a less effective style of leadership? (UGC NET Management Jan 2017)
  • A.Developer
  • B.Missionary
  • C.Executive
  • D.Bureaucrat
Correct Answer: Missionary

In the Reddin model, the appropriate versions of these management styles are Developer, Executive, Benevolent Autocrat, Bureaucrat while the inappropriate styles are Missionary, Compromiser, Autocrat, Deserter.

Question 15
Consideration and Initiating Structure as the dimensions of leadership were identified by which of the following? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2021)
  • A.Michigan leadership studies
  • B.The Harvard leadership studies
  • C.The Iowa leadership studies
  • D.The Ohio State leadership studies
Correct Answer: The Ohio State leadership studies

Option D is the correct answer.

 

A series of studies on leadership was done by Ohio State University in 1945 to identify observable behaviours of leaders instead of focusing on their traits. They found two critical characteristics of leadership either of which could be high or low or independent of one another. The research was based on questionnaires to leaders and subordinates of the organizations. These are known as the Leader Behaviour Description Questionnaire (LDBQ) and the Supervisor Behaviour Description Questionnaire (SBDQ).

 

Ultimately, these studies narrowed the description of leader behaviour into 2 dimensions:

1. Initiating Structure Behaviour: The behaviour of leaders who define the leader-subordinate role so that everyone knows what is expected, establish formal lines of communication, and determine how tasks will be performed.

2. Consideration Behaviour: The behaviour of leaders who are concerned for subordinates and attempt to establish a warm, friendly, and supportive climate.

Question 16
Leader-Member relationship, degree of structure andleadersposition, power are dimensions of which of the following leadership theory? (UGC NET HRM Jun 2021)
  • A.Group exchange theory
  • B.Contingency theory
  • C.Path-goal leadership theory
  • D.Trait theory
Correct Answer: Contingency theory

Contingency theory states “that a leader's effectiveness is contingent on how well the leader's style matches a specific setting or situation”. If leaders were successful in the roles they played, then it was considered a perfect match.

The contingency theory of Fiedler gives 3 dimensions of situational favorableness. These are:

(i) Task Structure: It refers to the degree to which tasks are clearly explained and structured for workers.

(ii) Leader-Member Relations: It refers to the degree of trust, respect, and confidence that exists between the leader and the workers.

(iii) Leader Position Power: It refers to the degree to which a leader possesses inherent position and power.

Question 17
Which of the following two leadership behaviour patterns were identified by Ohio State Studies? (UGC NET HRM Dec 2019)
  • A.Employee Orientation and Production Orientation
  • B.Initiating structure and consideration
  • C.Concern for production and Concern for people
  • D.Personalism/Materialism and Opportunism
Correct Answer: Initiating structure and consideration

The Ohio State Studies focused on leadership behaviors, identifying two distinct dimensions of leadership: consideration and initiating structure. Consideration encompasses behaviors that emphasize mutual respect, warmth, and friendship between leaders and their group members. On the other hand, initiating structure involves actions that focus on defining roles, organizing tasks, and establishing clear patterns of communication and procedures within the workgroup. These two dimensions emerged consistently across various situations in the study, shaping the understanding of leadership behaviors in different group contexts.

Question 18
Trait Theories of leadership were developed by: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)A.StogdillB. Mc call andLambardoC. Bennis and ThomasD. Kurtlewin
  • A.A and B only
  • B.A, B, C
  • C.A, C, D
  • D.A, B, C, D
Correct Answer: A, B, C

Trait Theories of leadership were developed by:

A. Stogdill 

B. Mc call and Lambardo

C. Bennis and Thomas 

 

Stogdill (1974) identified the following traits and skills as critical to leaders.

Traits

Skills

Adaptable to situations

Alert to social environment

Ambitious and achievement-oriented

Assertive

Cooperative

Decisive

Dependable

Dominant (desire to influence others)

Energetic (high activity level)

Self-confident

Tolerant of Stress

Willing to assume responsibility

Clever (intelligent)

Conceptually skilled
