Knowledgeable about group task

Organised (administrative ability)

Persuasive

Socially skilled

 

McCall and Lombardo (1983) researched both success and failure identified four primary traits by which leaders could succeed or ‘derail’:

1. Emotional stability and composure: Calm, confident and predictable, particularly when under stress.

2. Admitting error: Owning up to mistakes, rather than putting energy into covering up.

3. Good interpersonal skills: Able to communicate and persuade others without resort to negative or coercive tactics.

4. Intellectual breadth: Able to understand a wide range of areas, rather than having a narrow (and narrow-minded) area of expertise.

 

In a book named Geeks and Geezers, Bennis and Thomas postulated that the most successful leaders have been shaped by an intense transformational experience. They looked at two groups of successful leaders: the geezers, who are now in their 70s and 80s; and the geeks, who, for the most part, are under 40. Geezers, when at the age the geeks are now, were concerned about making a living; they were mostly focused on careers, and they had heroes and role models. Geeks want to change the world, and seek balance between careers, family, and personal activities. They have fewer heroes (Bennis & Thomas, 2002). They call this transformational experience the crucible of leadership. Other elements that make the leader are the era in which they live (environment) and their own values. These help to determine whether this transformations experience will result in a leader or not. By their definition, the crucibles can be of many different types and can take on many different forms. They can be experiences that are forces on us or experiences we seek. They can be harsh, such as dealing with failure, or they can be pleasant, such as seeing unexpected positive results that yield an unanticipated revelation (Bennis & Thomas, 2002).

Question 19
The leader who guide and motivate a followers in the direction of established goals by clarifying role and task requirement is: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2020)
  • A.Transformational leader
  • B.Charismatic Leader
  • C.Transactional Leader
  • D.Facilitative Leader
Correct Answer: Transactional Leader

Transactional leaders focus on guiding and motivating their followers toward predefined goals by providing clarity on roles and tasks. They operate through a system of exchanges, rewarding productivity. In contrast, transformational leaders inspire their followers to surpass self-interests for the greater organizational good. They go beyond task clarification, sparking inspiration, and fostering a deeper understanding of issues, encouraging followers to question established perspectives. Transformational leadership leads to exceptional employee performance, increased satisfaction, creativity, and goal achievement, setting it apart from transactional leadership.

Question 20
Match List IwithList II: (UGC NET Commerce Jun 2022)List I (Management Style)a. Task Managementb. Country Club Managementc. Impoverished Managementd. Team ManagementList II (Approach)i. Love conquers all approach.ii. One plus one can adduptothree approach.iii. Authority-obedience approach.iv. Speak no evil, hear no evil,seeno evil approach.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.a-i, b- iii, c- iv, d- ii
  • B.a-i, b- iv, c- ii, d- iii
  • C.a- iii, b-i, c- iv, d- ii
  • D.a- iii, b- iv, c- ii, d-i
Correct Answer: a- iii, b-i, c- iv, d- ii

Option C accurately matches List I with List II as follows:

a. Task Management (iii)

b. Country Club Management (i)

c. Impoverished Management (iv)

d. Team Management (ii)

 

Task Management involves an authority-obedience approach where the leader primarily focuses on task accomplishment, being primarily concerned about productivity.

Country Club Management embodies a "love conquers all" approach where the leader is significantly concerned with maintaining harmonious relationships among team members, prioritizing people over task accomplishment.

Impoverished Management reflects a "speak no evil, hear no evil, see no evil" approach, as the leader attempts to stay aloof and uninvolved in both task and interpersonal relationships.

Team Management adopts a "one plus one can add up to three" approach by emphasizing teamwork, interdependence, and the creation of trust and respect among team members for achieving synergistic results.

 

Therefore, the correct match is found in option C.

Question 21
As per the managerial grid given by Blake and Mouton, the leadership style focusing on low task and high concern for the people is known as: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2019)
  • A.impoverished management
  • B.club country management
  • C.team management
  • D.middle of the road management
Correct Answer: club country management

As per Blake and Mouton's Managerial Grid, the leadership style focusing on low task and high concern for people is known as "Country Club Management." This style places a significant emphasis on fostering harmonious relationships among team members and prioritizing a secure and pleasant work environment. The primary focus is on people's needs rather than task efficiency.

Question 22
“If the leadership style allows substantial participation by members of the group in the management and decision-making process, subordinates are frequently consulted by the manager on wide-ranging problems and are allowed sufficient freedom to communicate with the leader and also with their fellow subordinates.” It is called: (UGC NET HRM Jun 2019)
  • A.Autocratic style of leadership
  • B.Democratic style of leadership
  • C.Laissez fair style of leadership
  • D.Paternalistic style of leadership
Correct Answer: Democratic style of leadership

The style described in the statement, where substantial participation by group members occurs in management and decision-making, aligns with the Democratic Leadership Style. In this style, the leader actively seeks input from team members, engages them in problem-solving, and grants them freedom to communicate among themselves and with the leader. This participatory approach fosters collaboration and empowerment among team members, promoting a sense of involvement and shared responsibility within the group.

Question 23
A leadership theory which proposed that effective group performance depended on the proper match between a leader’s style and degree to which the situation allowed the leader to control and influence is called: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)
  • A.Path goal theory
  • B.Trait theory
  • C.Situational theory
  • D.Fiedler’s contingency model
Correct Answer: Fiedler’s contingency model

The leadership theory that emphasizes the match between a leader's style and the level of control and influence a situation allows is referred to as Fiedler's Contingency Model. This model focuses on the interaction between a leader's style and the favorableness of the situation. Fiedler proposed that a leader's effectiveness relies on their innate leadership style, which is either task-oriented or relationship-oriented, as determined by the Least Preferred Coworker (LPC) scale.

 

The model also considers situational favorableness, encompassing leader-member relations, task structure, and position power. Depending on the situation's level of favorableness, either a task-oriented or person-oriented leader is more effective. In extremely favorable or unfavorable situations, a task-oriented leader thrives, while in moderately favorable situations, a person-oriented leader excels.

Question 24
Consider the following: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2018)(i) Supportive leadership behaviour(ii) Participative leadership behaviour(iii) Instrumental leadership behaviour(iv) Achievement- Oriented leadership behaviourThe above leadership behaviours are related to which of the following?
  • A.Managerial grid approach of leadership
  • B.Fiedler’s contingency model of leadership
  • C.Situational theory of leadership
  • D.Path-goal approach of leadership
Correct Answer: Path-goal approach of leadership

The leadership behaviors mentioned—supportive, participative, instrumental, and achievement-oriented—are associated with the Path-Goal Leadership Theory. This theory, developed by Robert House in 1971, focuses on how leaders facilitate goal achievement and provide rewards accordingly.

 

The original Path-Goal Theory identifies four types of leader behaviors:

 

1. Directive (Path-Goal Clarifying): This behavior involves the leader informing followers of expectations and instructing them on task performance. It's most effective when roles are ambiguous and tasks are intrinsically satisfying.

 

2. Achievement-Oriented: Here, leaders set challenging goals, exhibit confidence in their team's abilities, and encourage high performance. This style is suited for occupations where the drive for achievement is crucial, such as technical jobs, sales, and scientific fields.

 

3. Participative: Leaders engage followers by seeking their input before making decisions. This approach is valuable when employees are deeply involved in their work.

 

4. Supportive: This behavior is geared toward fulfilling the psychological needs and preferences of subordinates, showing concern for their well-being. It's particularly crucial in situations where tasks or relationships cause distress.

Question 25
Match List IwithList II: (UGC NET Commerce Dec 2022)List I (Leadership Style)A. Impoverished managementB. Team managersC. Country club managementD. Autocratic task managersList II (Description)I. Work accomplished is from a committee of people with interdependence through a common stake in organizational purpose and with trust and respect.II. Exertion of minimum effort is required to get work done and to sustain organizational morale.III. Efficiency results from arranging work in such a way that human elements have little effect.IV. Thoughtful attention to the needs of people leads to a friendly and comfortable organizational atmosphere and work environment.Choose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.A- I, B- II, C- IV, D- III
  • B.A- II, B- I, C- III, D- IV
  • C.A- II, B- I, C- IV, D- III
  • D.A- IV, B- I, C- III, D- II
Correct Answer: A- II, B- I, C- IV, D- III

Option C correctly matches List I with List II as follows:

A. Impoverished management (II)

B. Team managers (I)

C. Country club management (IV)

D. Autocratic task managers (III)

 

Impoverished management style involves a leader who minimally invests effort to accomplish tasks and maintain organizational morale.

Team management style refers to a leader fostering interdependence among a committee of individuals, creating a shared purpose and trust that results in collaborative teamwork for achieving goals.

Country club management style is characterized by a leader who pays careful attention to people's needs, cultivating a welcoming and supportive work environment.

Autocratic task management involves arranging work to minimize the influence of human elements, emphasizing efficiency through strict control and direction by the leader.

 

Hence, the correct match is found in option C.

Question 26
Match the ‘Style of Leadership’ with the ‘numbers’, as they are denoted by, in Managerial Grid: (UGC NET HRM Jan 2017)List – Aa. Task Managementb. Impoverishedc. Teamd. Country Clube. Middle of the roadList – Bi. 1, 1ii. 1, 9iii. 5, 5iv. 9, 1v. 9, 9
  • A.a-ii, b-i, c-iv, d-v, e-iii
  • B.a-ii, b-i, c-v, d-iv, e-iii
  • C.a-iv, b-i, c-ii, d-v, e-iii
  • D.a-iv, b-i, c-v, d-ii, e-iii
Correct Answer: a-iv, b-i, c-v, d-ii, e-iii

Leaders can be oriented towards both tasks and persons. This theory (Managerial Grid) by Blake and Mouton (1978) has a popular application of both task and person orientation. According to this theory leaders are most effective when they achieve a high and balanced concern for people and for tasks. Each leader can be rated somewhere along each of the axes from 1 to 9.

 

Although there can be 81 possible combinations, following 5 are important ones:

1. The (9, 1) leader is primarily concerned about the task or production. He is concerned with his responsibility to see that the work is completed. He is called a Task-Management leader.

2. The (1, 9) leader is primarily concerned for people and only incidentally concerned with production. The leader's major responsibility is to establish harmonious relationships among subordinates and to provide a secure and pleasant work atmosphere. He is called as Country Club Management leader.

3. The (1,1) leader is concerned with neither production nor people. He tries to stay out of the way and not become involved in the conflict between the necessity for production and the attainment of good working relationship. He is called as Impoverish Management leader.

4. The (5,5) leader reflects a middle ground position and is called as Middle of the Road Management leader. He seeks to compromise between high production and employee satisfaction.

5. The (9,9) leader is extremely concerned about the task and also the people. He is concerned to see that the work accomplishment is from committed people; interdependence through a'common stake' in organisation; purpose leads to relationship of trust and respect. He is called a Team Management leader.

Question 27
Match the following. (UGC NET HRM Jun 2022)List I(a) Managerial Grid Theory(b) X and Y Theory(c) Path-Goal Theory(d) Contingency TheoryList II(i) McGregor(ii) Fred E. Fielder(iii) Robert R. Blake(iv) Martin G. EvansChoose the correct answer from the options given below:
  • A.(a)-(iii), (b)-(i), (c)-(iv), (d)-(ii)
  • B.(a)-(ii), (b)-(iii), (c)-(i), (d)-(iv)
  • C.(a)-(iv), (b)-(i), (c)-(ii), (d)-(iii)
  • D.(a)-(i), (b)-(iv), (c)-(ii), (d)-(iii)
Correct Answer: (a)-(iii), (b)-(i), (c)-(iv), (d)-(ii)

Option A is the correct answer.

 

The correct match for the given theories and their respective proponents is as follows:

Managerial Grid Theory - Robert R. Blake (iii)

X and Y Theory - McGregor (i)

Path-Goal Theory - Martin G. Evans (iv)

Contingency Theory - Fred E. Fielder (ii)

 

This arrangement aligns each theory with its corresponding originator:

 

Robert R. Blake and Jane S. Mouton developed the Managerial Grid, a model emphasizing concerns for productivity and people in organizations.

 

Douglas McGregor proposed Theory X and Theory Y, contrasting negative and positive assumptions about employee behavior.

 

Robert House developed the Path-Goal Leadership Theory, centered on facilitating goal achievement and rewarding employees accordingly.

 

Fred E. Fielder is associated with the Contingency Theory, which emphasizes the need for organizations to align their internal structures with external environmental demands for effectiveness.

Question 28
What is ’Neotony’ as a leadership trait advanced by Bennis and Thomas? (UGC NET HRM Nov 2017)
  • A.Calm, confident and predictable under stressful condition
  • B.Youthful, curious, playful, fearless, warm and energetic
  • C.Encouraging dissent, empathy and obsessive communication
  • D.Ambitious, morally strong and competence
Correct Answer: Youthful, curious, playful, fearless, warm and energetic

Neotony, as defined by Warren Bennis and Robert Thomas in their research on "Geeks and Geezers," is about the retention of youthful traits into adulthood. It involves qualities like curiosity, playfulness, fearlessness, warmth, energy, and an eagerness for new experiences. Essentially, it's about maintaining a youthful mindset and openness to the world throughout one's life, which enables individuals to remain courageous, enthusiastic, and hungry for knowledge.

Question 29
In Black and Mouton’s “Managerial Grid”, the ‘task style’ represents: (UGC NET HRM Dec 2011)
  • A.High concern for people and low concern for production.
  • B.High concern for people and high concern for production.
  • C.Low concern for people and low concern for production.
  • D.High concern for production and low concern for people.
Correct Answer: High concern for production and low concern for people.

In Blake and Mouton's Managerial Grid, the 'task style' represents (D) High concern for production and low concern for people.

 

This grid assesses leadership behaviors based on concern for people (relationships) and concern for production (task accomplishment). The extreme end of the task-oriented style (9, 1) focuses heavily on achieving tasks and completing work, emphasizing productivity over concerns for the people involved.
